1201 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Yancsek v. Hull Corp.


A-1386-84T6


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


204 N.J. Super. 429; 499 A.2d 242; 1985 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1489


September 10, 1985, Submitted  
October 8, 1985, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication October 18, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Morris County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff customer sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Morris County, which denied her request for reinstatement and restoration to the trial list of her product liability complaint against defendant manufacturer.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff customer filed a product liability suit against a corporation. After plaintiff realized that the corporation did not manufacture the item, she sued defendant manufacturer. Defendant earned a dismissal of the suit on the grounds that the action was barred by the two-year statute of limitations. Plaintiff moved to reinstate the suit based on a recently decided decision of the Supreme Court of the United States, which permitted the tolling of the statute of limitations, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:14-22, for suits instituted before a certain date, including plaintiff's. The reviewing court found that the motion was improperly denied. The trial judge should have considered the original dismissal to be a mistake. Plaintiff's application to the trial court was timely, so the denial of the reinstatement of the complaint was a mistaken exercise of discretion under N.J. Ct. R. 4:50-1(a).


OUTCOME: The denial of plaintiff customer's request for reinstatement and restoration to the trial list of her product liability complaint against defendant manufacturer was reversed and remanded because the statute of limitations was tolled pursuant to a decision of the Supreme Court of the United States.

 

1202 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gately


A-1925-84T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


204 N.J. Super. 332; 498 A.2d 1271; 1985 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1445


September 19, 1985, Argued  
October 8, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court, Law Division, Somerset County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, which acquitted him of driving a motor vehicle while under the influence of alcohol but convicted him of refusing to submit to a breathalyzer test.


OVERVIEW: After observing defendant passed out in the front seat of running car, a police officer arrested him for drunk driving. However, defendant refused to take a breathalyzer test. At trial, defendant was acquitted of driving a motor vehicle while under the influence of alcohol but convicted of refusing to submit to a breathalyzer test. On appeal, the court reversed the conviction for refusing to submit to a breathalyzer test. The court noted that defendant had refused to take the test and that the elements of the offense as provided by N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:4-50.4a were established in the state's proofs. However, the court ruled that that an additional element of the offense, operation in fact, was not proven. The court held that without his express or implied consent, defendant had no obligation to submit to a breathalyzer test and was not subject to § 39:4-50.4a or its sanctions, including driver's license suspension. The court found that defendant did not give his express consent and that because he was not the operator of the vehicle, he had not given his complied consent as well.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for refusing to submit to a breathalyzer test. The court found that defendant had not expressly consented to the test and that because he was not the operator of the vehicle he had not given his implied consent to take the test. Therefore, defendant was not subject to the applicable statute or its sanctions.

 

1203 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


New Jersey State League of Municipalities v. Kimmelman


A-0018-84T7


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


204 N.J. Super. 323; 498 A.2d 1266; 1985 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1441


September 10, 1985, Argued  
October 2, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court, Law Division, Bergen County, whose opinion is reported at 197 N.J. Super. 89.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Attorney general challenged the decision of the Superior Court, Law Division, Bergen County (New Jersey), which declared that 1982 N.J. Laws 220 as amended by 1983 N.J. Laws 55, N.J. Stat. Ann. 54:4-23a, was unconstitutional because it exempted newly constructed residential structures from taxation until occupancy, and, thus violated N.J. Const. art. VIII (1947). Attorney general contended the law was general, not special, legislation.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, attorney general contended that the trial court erred in declaring that 1982 N.J. Laws 220 as amended by 1983 N.J. Laws 55, N.J. Stat. Ann. 54:4-23a was unconstitutional. The court agreed and reversed the trial court's decision. The legislation was constitutional because it was general, rather than special, in application. Applying a three part test, the court held that the legislation was designed to reduce the cost of housing; that it was not invalid merely because there may be some discriminatory impact and some imperfections; and, that there was a rational basis to support the exclusion of residential rental units. Therefore, plaintiff taxpayers failed to carry the burden of clearly demonstrating a violation of N.J. Const. art. VIII (1947).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision holding that the legislation, which exempted new residential construction from taxation, was constitutional because there was a rational basis that justified the classification between single-family units and rental units and the classification was reasonable and not arbitrary. Therefore, it was not unconstitutional "special" legislation.

 

1204 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Garcia


Docket No. A-592-83T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


204 N.J. Super. 202; 497 A.2d 1296; 1985 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1454


August 28, 1985, Submitted  
September 18, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court, Law Division, Camden County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court, Law Division, Camden County (New Jersey), which entered an order convicting him of second degree robbery, contrary to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:15-1, and sentenced him as a persistent offender to an extended term of imprisonment of 10 years with a parole ineligibility period of five years.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of second degree robbery, contrary to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:15-1, and was sentenced as a persistent offender to an extended term of imprisonment of 10 years with a parole ineligibility period of five years. The court affirmed defendant's sentence because it found that defendant met the statutory requirements for sentencing as a persistent offender pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:44-3 a: Defendant's two prior separate convictions were for possession of a controlled dangerous substance and its possession with intent to distribute; and for possession of a controlled dangerous substance and its distribution; the convictions occurred within 10 years of the robbery committed by defendant; he was over age 18 at the time of commission of both drug-related offenses; and sentences of imprisonment in excess of six months were authorized both for intent to distribute and for distribution of a controlled dangerous substance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court which entered an order convicting defendant of second degree robbery and sentenced him as a persistent offender to an extended term of imprisonment because it determined that defendant's prior convictions fulfilled the statutory requirements necessary for sentencing him as a persistent offender.

 

1205 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Kimmelman v. Burgio


No. A-5800-84T5


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


204 N.J. Super. 44; 497 A.2d 890; 1985 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1421


September 9, 1985, Argued  
September 11, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Secretary of State.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney general challenged a decision of respondent Secretary of State (New Jersey) to place a proposed amendment to the New Jersey Constitution on the ballot during the 1985 general election and requested an injunction prohibiting respondent from doing so.


OVERVIEW: Numerous senators sponsored and introduced a proposed amendment to N.J. Const. art. V, § 4, par. 6. The resolution set forth the form of the question on the ballot and an interpretive statement to appear on the ballot. The resolution was adopted in the Senate and the General Assembly. The following year, the legislature decided to place the resolution on the ballot during the 1985 general election. Respondent secretary of state decided that she would place the proposed amendment on the ballot unless otherwise instructed by the courts. Appellant attorney general sought an injunction barring respondent from placing the issue on the ballot, arguing that the proposed amendment was too ambiguous. The court denied appellant's request for an injunction. However, the court invalidated the interpretive statement included with the proposed amendment, on the ground that it was highly misleading, and remanded to the legislature for preparation of a new interpretive statement.


OUTCOME: The court denied appellant's request for an injunction, rejecting appellant's argument that the proposed amendment was too ambiguous. The court declared the interpretive statement included in the proposed amendment to be invalid as highly misleading, however, and remanded to the legislature for the preparation of a new interpretive statement.

 

1206 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sharkey


Docket No. A-4554-82T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


204 N.J. Super. 192; 497 A.2d 1291; 1985 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1456


August 13, 1985, Argued  
September 11, 1985, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certification denied by State v. Sharkey, 102 N.J. 360, 508 A.2d 229, 1985 N.J. LEXIS 3187 (1985)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Morris County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for possession of a "look-alike" drug with intent to distribute under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 24:21-19.1(a)(3), by the Superior Court of New Jersey, Morris County, on the grounds that § 24:21-19.1(a)(3) was unconstitutional and that the trial court improperly refused to admit the physician's desk reference into evidence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested after officers found a plastic bag containing 200 white capsules on his person. Due to their size and shape, the officers believed the capsules contained a controlled substance. Defendant gave a statement that he believed the pills to be "speed" and that he had intended to sell them. A lab test revealed that the pills contained caffeine, and defendant was charged with and convicted of possession of a "look-alike" drug with intent to distribute under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 24:21-19.1(a)(3). The court affirmed defendant's conviction, finding that § 24:21-19.1(a)(3) was not unconstitutionally vague because persons of ordinary intelligence would understand what conduct the statute proscribed. Defendant's conviction precluded him from complaining of the vagueness of § 24:21-19.1(a)(3) as applied to his own conduct. Section 24:21-19.1(a)(3) was not overbroad because it did not reach any constitutionally protected conduct. The statutory presumption was reasonable. The trial court's ruling as to the physician's desk reference was harmless error because the refusal to admit the book did not create a potential for prejudice or injustice.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction because the look-alike drug statute was not unconstitutionally vague or overbroad. The court also found that defendant did not have standing to challenge the statute's vagueness and that the trial court's refusal to admit the physician's desk reference was harmless error.

 

1207 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Alling Street Urban Renewal Co. v. Newark


Docket No. A-3462-83T2


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


204 N.J. Super. 185; 497 A.2d 1287; 1985 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1457


June 5, 1985, Argued  
September 11, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Essex County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant urban renewal contractor challenged a judgment from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Essex County, which declared that it was not entitled to the credit provision of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40:55C-65. Appellant had brought suit against appellee city seeking a tax exemption for improvements made under the provisions the Urban Renewal Corporation and Association Law of 1961, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40:55C-40 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Appellant urban renewal contractor unsuccessfully sought a declaration that its agreement with appellee city entitled it to the credit provision of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40:55C-65, and the Urban Renewal Corporation and Association Law of 1961, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40:55C-40 et seq. The court reversed. The court determined that an interpretation of the statute was required. The parties' agreement did not provide for the credit, but clearly it was entered into in conformity with the statute. The statute read that the credit was to apply against "such annual charge." Appellant was obligated to pay an "annual service charge." The court held that that the reference to "such" annual charge, which referred collaterally to real estate taxes, was forcefully and directly concerned with the annual service charge, and that it could only have meant the annual service charge. The court further held that the distinction between "annual service charge" and "annual charge," considered in the context of the whole body of law was too thin a reed to thwart the obvious public purpose inherent in the statute. The court directed the entry of judgment in favor of appellant.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment for appellee city, and remanded for judgment in favor of appellant urban renewal contractor. The court held that appellant was entitled to the statutory credit against its "annual service charge" for improvements it made under the Urban Renewal Corporation and Association Law of 1961.

 

1208 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Friends of Kean v. N.J. Election Law Enforcement Com


A-5517-84T5, A-5804-84T5


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


203 N.J. Super. 523; 497 A.2d 555; 1985 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1469


August 20, 1985, Argued  
August 30, 1985, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication September 13, 1985.
Certification granted Friends of Governor Kean v. New Jersey Election Law Enforcement Com., 102 N.J. 319, 508 A.2d 200, 1985 N.J. LEXIS 3030 (1985)
Affirmed by Friends of Governor Kean v. New Jersey Election Law Enforcement Com., 102 N.J. 325, 508 A.2d 204, 1985 N.J. LEXIS 3050 (1985)
Modified by, Affirmed by Friends of Governor Kean v. New Jersey Election Law Enforcement Com., 114 N.J. 33, 552 A.2d 612, 1989 N.J. LEXIS 10 (1989)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from final action of the New Jersey Election Law Enforcement Commission.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff campaign committees challenged the validity of two advisory opinions issued by defendant Election Law Enforcement Commission (New Jersey).


OVERVIEW: Defendant Election Law Enforcement Commission issued two advisory opinions requiring the allocation of a portion of certain campaign expenses of assembly candidates and county and other local office candidates to the gubernatorial campaign expenditure limits. Plaintiffs contended that the opinions exceeded defendant's authority under the statute and the regulations and challenged their validity on federal constitutional grounds. The court held that the opinions were arbitrary and unreasonable because they went beyond the authorization of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 19:44A-6f and defendant's regulations to limit campaign expenditures. The court also held that even if the opinions were authorized by statute and regulations, they were unconstitutional as applied because they violated First Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. I, freedoms of speech and association. The court therefore found that the opinions were invalid.


OUTCOME: The court found that advisory opinions affecting plaintiff campaign committees issued by defendant Election Law Enforcement Commission were invalid because they went beyond defendant's statutory authorization to limit campaign expenditures.

 

1209 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Abramowitz v. Kimmelman


A-1120-84T7


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


203 N.J. Super. 118; 495 A.2d 1362; 1985 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1375


June 12, 1985, Argued  
July 26, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Hudson County whose opinion is reported at 200 N.J. Super. 303.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff resident, plaintiff developer, plaintiff retailer, and plaintiff organization sought review of an order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Hudson County (New Jersey) that upheld the validity of 1984 N.J. Laws 160, an amendment and supplement to the Sunday Closing Law, N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 2A: 171-5.8 to -5.18.


OVERVIEW: In response to a referendum held pursuant to 1984 N.J. Laws 160 (chapter 160), an amendment and supplement to the Sunday Closing Law, N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 2A:171-5.8 to -5.18, plaintiff resident, plaintiff developer, plaintiff retailer, and plaintiff organization, among others, filed suit against defendant clerk and defendant attorney general. Plaintiffs contended chapter 160 was unconstitutional special legislation that violated constitutional guarantees of equal protection. Based upon their contention that a fundamental right was involved, plaintiffs argued chapter 160 was subject to strict scrutiny and had to serve a compelling state interest in order to be sustainable. The trial court applied the test of minimal scrutiny and upheld the validity of chapter 160. Consequently, plaintiffs sought review, again asserting that strict scrutiny was necessary. On review, the court affirmed, finding minimal scrutiny was sufficient, because chapter 160 did not indirectly affect a fundamental right in a substantial enough way to require even intermediate scrutiny.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order upholding the act because the act concerned the right to vote in a referendum, which was only statutory, not constitutional, and the act did not indirectly affect a fundamental right in a substantial enough way to require more than minimal scrutiny.

 

1210 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Soc'y for Envtl. Econ. Dev. v. N.J. Dep't of Envtl. Prot.


A-4789-83T7


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


208 N.J. Super. 1; 504 A.2d 1180; 1985 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1641


June 4, 1985, Argued  
July 15, 1985, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication February 13, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Adoption of Administrative Regulations, N.J.A.C. 7:13 By the Commissioner of the Department of Environmental Protection.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, association of developers and property owners, challenged the rules promulgated by respondent Department of Environmental Protection governing development in fresh-water flood hazard areas.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, association of developers and property owners, challenged three provisions of new regulations of respondent Department of Environmental Protection governing development in fresh-water flood hazard areas. Appellants challenged the 20% net fill rule, N.J. Admin. Code tit. 7 § 13-4.7(d), the creation of a category of Projects of Special Concern, N.J. Admin. Code tit. 7 § 13-5.1, et seq. and the so-called grandfather clause, N.J. Admin. Code tit. 7 § 13-1.4(d). The court found that appellants' allegations that respondent failed to provide the public with technical justification for the 20% net fill rule was without merit. The court held that the 20% net fill rule was neither arbitrary nor factually unsupported and did not constitute an unconstitutional taking of property without just compensation. The court rejected appellants' argument that respondent did not have statutory authority to formulate criteria for Projects of Special Concern because N.J. Stat. Ann. § 13:1D-1, et seq., accorded respondent broad powers of conservation and ecological control. The court held that limited retroactivity on a uniform basis did not contravene constitutional principles.


OUTCOME: The court held that the new rules promulgated by respondent Department of Environmental Protection governing development in fresh-water flood hazard areas were valid exercises of respondent's broad powers of conservation and ecological control. The court held that the 20% net fill rule did not constitute an unconstitutional taking of property without just compensation.

 

1211 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Atl. City Casino Asso v. Atl. City


No. A-1416-84T7


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


217 N.J. Super. 277; 525 A.2d 1109; 1985 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1687


June 5, 1985, Argued  
July 15, 1985, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication April 10, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court, Law Division, Atlantic County whose opinion is reported at 204 N.J. Super. 652.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, city and officials, sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Atlantic County, that found unconstitutional 1984 N.J. Laws 67, which deferred the implementation of a revaluation of real property for the 1984 tax year, on plaintiff property owners' action.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff property owners brought an action to have 1984 N.J. Laws 67 (statute) declared unconstitutional because it permitted defendants, city and officials, to defer implementation of a revaluation of real property for the 1984 tax year. The trial court ruled the statute was unconstitutional. On review, the court found that, although there was litigation in which defendant city had been ordered to undertake a complete revaluation, it did not bar the legislature from enacting the statute because the suit involved a public right. The court also found the statute was not special legislation, in violation of N.J. Const. art. IV, § VII, par. 9(6), because the peculiar and profound disturbance of real estate values that resulted from the adoption of the casino referendum provided a rational basis for the legislature to deal separately with defendant city. The court ruled the statute did not unconstitutionally delegate authority to the state treasurer by allowing him to extend the temporary moratorium for the 1985 tax year if it was in defendant's best interest. The court held, given the complexity of the revaluation a more precise standard was unrealistic, and reversed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the finding that the statute deferring the implementation of a revaluation of real property for the tax year was unconstitutional. The court found that the litigation ordering the revaluation involved a public right and that the legislature had a rational basis for dealing with defendant city separately because the casino referendum caused a profound disturbance of real estate values.

 

1212 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


In re Hotel & Restaurant Employees & Bartenders International Union Local 54


A-993-82T5, A-317-84T5, A-525-84T5, A-880-84T5


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


203 N.J. Super. 297; 496 A.2d 1111; 1985 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1398; 110 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P56,022


February 21, 1985, Argued  
July 11, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from an Order of the New Jersey Casino Control Commission.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, union and certain members, sought review of the order of the New Jersey Casino Control Commission, which disqualified appellants certain members from licensing under § 86 of the Casino Control Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 5:12-86 for their association with career offenders.


OVERVIEW: The New Jersey Casino Control Commission (Commission) disqualified appellants, certain members of the union, from licensing, under § 86 of the Casino Control Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 5:12-86, due to their involvement with career offenders. The court found that the Commission's findings that appellants associated with career offenders was supported by the evidence. The continued participation of appellants in the casino industry created an unacceptable risk of corruption. The court found that U.S. Const. amend. I provided for the right of association, but in light of the state's compelling interest to protect the gaming operations, an infringement on appellants' right of association was warranted. The court also found that the Commission did not deny one appellant due process by failing to grant him a stay or immunity, or by failing to reopen the record for a rehearing. The court affirmed the order of the Commission on those grounds.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the Casino Control Commission, which disqualified from licensing appellants, certain members of appellant union, because of their ongoing involvement with career criminal offenders which created an unacceptable risk of corruption in the gaming industry. A compelling interest warranted the infringement on appellants' First Amendment right of association.

 

1213 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Mulcahy


A-5787-83T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


202 N.J. Super. 398; 495 A.2d 166; 1985 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1364


June 18, 1985, Argued  
July 10, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Bergen County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Bergen County, which convicted him of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:4-50(a) and of refusing to submit to an alcohol breath test in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:4-50.4(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:4-50(a) and of refusing to submit to an alcohol breath test in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:4-50.4(a). On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction for operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor because there was sufficient credible evidence to support the conviction. Although the arrest was invalid because the officers lacked the requisite knowledge to properly arrest defendant for a violation of § 39:4-50(a), the legality of the arrest had no bearing upon the validity of the conviction. Defendant was fairly apprised of the charge and knew the essence of the state's possible testimony. The court reversed the conviction for refusing to submit to an alcohol breath test because of the invalid arrest. A lawful arrest was required under § 39:4-50.4(a) in order for the police to have requested that defendant submit to the testing.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor was affirmed because it was a valid conviction despite defendant's unlawful arrest. Defendant's conviction for refusing to submit to an alcohol breath test was reversed because a lawful arrest was statutorily required in order for the police to request that defendant submit to testing.

 

1214 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Welch v. Engineers, Inc.


A-4953-83T3


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


202 N.J. Super. 387; 495 A.2d 160; 1985 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1362


March 11, 1985, Argued  
July 9, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Morris County).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured person appealed an order from the Superior Court of Morris County (New Jersey), which granted summary judgment to defendant designer-builder in a personal injury action. The trial court concluded that the action was time-barred pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:14-1.1.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff injured person slipped and fell while working on a truck dock area designed and constructed by defendant designer-builder. Plaintiff brought a personal injury action against defendant, alleging that the truck dock was poorly designed because of its proximity to the sidewalk where plaintiff fell. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of defendant, holding that the action was time-barred pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:14-1.1.The trial court found that defendant's engineer completed the design more than 10 years before plaintiff filed her complaint, even though defendant's work on the project was completed less than 10 years prior to the institution of suit. Plaintiff appealed. The appellate court reversed, holding that the statute of limitations did not begin to run until substantial completion of the structure. The court reasoned that courts did not condone a piece-meal concept of repose where the contractor was involved in multiple phases of the undertaking. The court held that, under § 2A:14-1.1, the limitations period had to be measured from the final date defendant furnished any and all services or construction that it had undertaken at the job site.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed an order that granted summary judgment in favor of defendant designer-builder. The court held that plaintiff injured person's action was not time-barred because the statute of limitations did not begin to run until substantial completion of the structure.

 

1215 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Matawan Regional Teachers Asso. v. Board of Education


A-4872-83T7


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


202 N.J. Super. 142; 493 A.2d 1334; 1985 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1338


May 22, 1985, Argued  
June 12, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the State Board of Education.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, individual school employees and their association, challenged a decision of the State Board of Education (New Jersey), granting respondent regional school district board's denial of applications by the individual appellants for additional paid sick leave days under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 18A:30-6. Appellants contended that respondent applied a blanket policy of denial to each appellant.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, individual school employees and their association, challenged decisions of respondent regional school district board, which denied their applications for additional paid sick leave under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 18A:30-6. Appellants contended that respondent's actions constituted a blanket policy of denial. On appeal, the court examined the statute, and first held that there were no specific standards governing the use of discretion by boards of education in resolving whether to pay additional sick leave. The court found that because no formal guidelines had been adopted by respondent, and respondent had indeed considered the individual characteristics of each case, including length of service, imminence of retirement, nature of the sickness or injury, that merely denying the appellants' applications did not amount to blanket denial per se, and affirmed the decisions of respondent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed respondent regional school district board's decision denying applications of appellant individual school employees, holding that denial of appellants' cases did not per se establish a blanket policy of denial of sick leave petitions, and that respondent had statutory discretion to review each case on its merits.

 

1216 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Ayers v. Jackson


A-2103-83T3


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


202 N.J. Super. 106; 493 A.2d 1314; 1985 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1326; 15 ELR 20642


April 2, 1985, Argued  
June 4, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Superior Court, Law Division, Ocean County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant township appealed the decision of the Superior Court, Ocean County (New Jersey), which awarded plaintiff township residents damages for emotional distress, loss of quality of life, and cost of medical surveillance in connection with defendant's negligent operation of its landfill.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff township residents brought an action for negligence against defendant township after defendant's landfill contaminated plaintiffs' well water. The trial court awarded plaintiffs damages for emotional distress, loss of quality of life, and the cost of medical surveillance to guard against plaintiffs' increased risk of developing cancer. On appeal, the court affirmed the award for loss of quality of life and vacated that portion of the award that granted recovery for emotional distress and medical surveillance. The court held that the award for emotional distress was an award for pain and suffering and that defendant was immune from liability pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 59:9-2(d). The court held that the evidence was insufficient to prove that defendant's negligence had so significantly increased the reasonable probability that any of plaintiffs would develop cancer as to justify an award for the costs of a lifetime of medical surveillance. The court further held that the award for loss of quality of life did not represent compensation for pain and suffering but rather was compensation for damages characterized by inconvenience and disruption of daily activities.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the award for loss of quality of life, vacated the award for emotional distress, because defendant township was immune from liability, and vacated the award for the cost of medical surveillance, because the evidence did not support that defendant's negligence had increased the probability that plaintiffs would develop cancer in the future.

 

1217 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Mack Paramus Co. v. Paramus


A-668-84T7, A-1426-84T7


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


201 N.J. Super. 508; 493 A.2d 593; 1985 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1325


April 22, 1985, Argued  
May 30, 1985, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certification granted by Mack Paramus Co. v. Paramus, 102 N.J. 325, 508 A.2d 205, 1985 N.J. LEXIS 3052 (1985)
Reversed by Mack Paramus Co. v. Paramus, 103 N.J. 564, 511 A.2d 1179, 1986 N.J. LEXIS 976 (1986)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Bergen County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, Borough of Paramus and Borough of Midland Park, sought review of summary judgments from the Superior Court, Bergen County (New Jersey), which invalidated municipal ordinances that prohibited virtually all commercial activities on Sunday. The trial court held that these ordinances were ultra vires, because their subject matter was preempted by the Code of Criminal Justice, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:1-5(d).


OVERVIEW: The Code of Criminal Justice (code), N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:1-5(d), prohibited the local governmental units of New Jersey from enacting or enforcing any ordinance or other local law or regulation conflicting with, or preempted by, any provision of the code or with any policy of New Jersey expressed by the code, whether that policy was expressed by inclusion of a provision in the code or by exclusion of that subject from the code. These consolidated cases implicated the validity of municipal ordinances adopted by appellants, Borough of Paramus and Borough of Midland Park, curtailing commercial activities on Sundays. The court held that the code, by saving the Chapter 119 county option for the applicability of limited Sunday closing provisions prohibiting the sale of certain merchandise, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:171-5.8 et seq., from repeal, repealing the balance of the Sunday closing sections, N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 2A:171-1, 2, 4, 5, and 6-12, and failing to include any municipal option to expand upon this expressed state policy, preempted concurrent municipal regulation in this field. Thus, appellants were without authority to adopt the ordinances, which therefore were invalid.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgments that declared the municipal ordinances invalid. The court held that appellants Borough of Paramus and Borough of Midland Park had no authority to enact ordinances curtailing commercial activities on Sundays, because this field of action was preempted by the Code of Criminal Justice.

 

1218 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. McMeekin


A-3523-82T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


204 N.J. Super. 496; 499 A.2d 515; 1985 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1498


January 28, 1985, Submitted  
May 24, 1985, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication October 25, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Ocean County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner, who was convicted of manslaughter, atrocious assault and battery, assault with the intent to kill and committing the crimes while armed, sought review of his sentence from the Superior Court of New Jersey.


OVERVIEW: Appellant prisoner contended that the trial court erred in re-sentencing him because the trial court imposed more than the 17 year maximum which he was sentenced to in the first sentencing hearing. The court noted that appellant was in a "transitional" class of offenders who could choose whether to be sentenced under Title 2A or Title 2C pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. 2C:1-1(c)(2). The court stated that appellant was fully warned by the sentencing judge, that resentencing would restore the Title 2A convictions as they existed before sentencing, except that the conviction for atrocious assault and battery would still be merged into the assault to kill conviction and that count four for being armed would be restored, which would expose appellant to an enhanced sentence for having committed an assault with intent to kill while armed. The court stated that vacation of the second sentence would be anomalous because appellant chose to be sentenced under Title 2A knowing of his exposure to a greater maximum term under 2A but equally aware that he would probably serve less real time because of the earlier parole date.


OUTCOME: Appellant prisoner's sentence was affirmed. Appellant was fully informed at resentencing that if he chose to be sentenced under a certain law he would have been exposed to a greater maximum term but probably serve less time due to an earlier parole date. Therefore, appellant could not claim that his second sentence was improper.

State v. Edmondson


A-5480-83T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


201 N.J. Super. 200; 492 A.2d 1087; 1985 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1307


May 7, 1985, Submitted  
May 16, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Camden County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Camden County, which convicted him of purchasing alcoholic beverages while under the legal age limit in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 33:1-81. Defendant received the mandatory penalties.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a 19 year old, was found guilty of purchasing an alcoholic beverage while under the legal age limit. The mandatory penalties of a fine plus one-year license suspension were imposed. Defendant appealed the sentence arguing that the mandatory penalties were unconstitutional under both federal and state law. On review the court noted that the mandatory suspension had been reduced to six months by amendment. The court found no merit in defendant's contentions and affirmed the conviction, but reduced the suspension to six months to reflect the amended law.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentence of one-year license suspension was reduced to six months because the statute had been amended, but the conviction and sentence were affirmed in all other respects.

 

1220 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Mountain Management Corp. v. Hinnant


A-1584-84T5


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


201 N.J. Super. 45; 492 A.2d 693; 1985 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1291


April 1, 1985, Submitted  
May 1, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Special Civil Part, Essex County, whose opinion is reported at    N.J. Super.     (Law Div. 1985).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant tenant sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Essex County, which denied appellant's grant for an additional one-year stay and dissolved the stay of execution of the warrant of removal in appellee building owner's dispossess action against appellant after appellee converted the apartment unit from the rental market to condominium ownership under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:18-61.1k.


OVERVIEW: Appellant tenant challenged the judgment that denied appellant's grant for an additional one-year stay and dissolved the stay of execution of the warrant of removal in appellee building owner's dispossess action against appellant after appellee converted the apartment unit from the rental market to condominium ownership under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:18-61.6k. Appellant received notice of his right to purchase the condominium unit under § 2A:18-61.8. Appellant chose not to purchase the apartment but instead, within the requisite 18 months, requested comparable housing under § 2A:18-61.11. Appellee's judgment for possession was entered but eviction was stayed for one year because appellant had not been offered the comparable housing he requested under § 2A:18-61.11a. Appellee waived one month's rent as moving expense compensation and also five months' rent as hardship relocation compensation under § 2A:18-61.11c. The court affirmed the judgment and held that the legislative history and the plain reading of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:18-61.11 allowed appellee to elect between waiving rent or finding comparable housing for appellant.


OUTCOME: The judgment denying appellant tenant's grant for an additional one-year stay and dissolving the stay of execution of a warrant of removal was affirmed because the legislative history and the plain reading of the statute allowed appellee building owner to elect between waiving rent or finding comparable housing for appellant.

 

1221 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Automatic Merchandising Council v. Edison


No. A-5655-82T2


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


204 N.J. Super. 395; 499 A.2d 224; 1985 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1486


November 5, 1984, Argued  
May 1, 1985, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication October 9, 1985.
Certification granted by Automatic Merchandising Council v. Edison, 101 N.J. 316, 501 A.2d 970, 1985 N.J. LEXIS 2859 (1985)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by Automatic Merchandising Council v. Edison, 102 N.J. 125, 506 A.2d 352, 1986 N.J. LEXIS 879 (1986)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Middlesex County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant township sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Middlesex County, which determined that appellant's ordinance imposing a licensing fee on vending machines was invalid pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40:52-2, in the class action of respondents, vending machine owners and operators, challenging the validity of the ordinance.


OVERVIEW: Appellant township challenged the judgment finding that its ordinance imposing a licensing fee on vending machines was invalid, in the class action of respondents, vending machine owners and operators, challenging the ordinance's validity. The lower court found the fee unreasonable and arbitrary. The court affirmed the judgment in part, findng that appellant's licensing power was granted under N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 40:52-1(d), (g), and 52-2. Section 52-2 permitted license fees enacted pursuant to § 52-1(d), (g) to be imposed for revenue. The court held that the fees must be reasonably related to regulatory costs and only incidentally provide revenue, so as to avoid amounting to an unauthorized taxing measure. Appellant's total cost of regulation of any one machine under the ordinance totaled $ 6.93, and appellant set the license fee at $ 40. The court held that, under § 52-2, appellant's fee of $ 40 was six times the proven regulatory costs and was thus unreasonable and arbitrary. The court reversed the judgment in part and held that the role of the lower court was to determine the validity of the ordinance. The lower court erred by determining what fee amount was appropriate.


OUTCOME: The judgment determining that appellant township's ordinance imposing a licensing fee on vending machines was invalid was affirmed in part, because appellant's licensing fee was unreasonable and arbitrary where it was six times the amount of proven regulatory costs. The judgment was reversed in part because the lower court lacked authority to determine an appropriate fee amount.

 

1222 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Brooks


A-1438-84T5


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


201 N.J. Super. 10; 492 A.2d 390; 1985 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1259


March 11, 1985, Submitted  
April 25, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Passaic County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of an order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Passaic County, which suppressed the results of a search of respondent's barbershop pursuant to a search warrant. The state claimed that the property seized was supported by the affidavits presented with the warrant, and that it was harmless error that the description on the warrant was incorrect.


OVERVIEW: The state sought review of the lower court's suppression of evidence obtained from respondent's barbershop pursuant to a search warrant. The state claimed that the property was seized in good faith reliance on the warrant, and that it was harmless error that the description on the warrant was incorrect because the warrant application supported the description of the property to be seized. The court determined that United States Supreme Court decisions dealing with whether officers reasonably believed the search they conducted was authorized by a valid warrant would apply retroactively because there was no bar to retroactive application when it was determined that police action was constitutional. The court found the affidavit correctly set forth the items to be seized, that the judge signing the warrant had performed the factual scrutiny necessary that probable cause existed, and that the officer's good faith reliance that the warrant authorized the requested search, even though the items described in the actual warrant were incorrect, was objectively reasonable. The court vacated the lower court's order to suppress the evidence.


OUTCOME: Order of the lower court which granted respondent's motion to suppress evidence obtained from a warrant with an incorrect description of what was to be seized was reversed because the state showed that the affidavit correctly set forth the items to be seized. The court held that the officer's good faith reliance that the warrant authorized the requested search was reasonable.

 

1223 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


North Bergen v. Hackensack Meadowlands Dev. Com.


A-4169-83T7


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


200 N.J. Super. 579; 491 A.2d 1314; 1985 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1271


February 26, 1985, Argued  
April 25, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Hudson County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant township sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Hudson County, which entered summary judgment against appellant in its constitutional challenge to the Hackensack Meadowlands Reclamation and Development Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 13:17-1 et seq., that alleged discrimination in violation of equal protection rights.


OVERVIEW: The Hackensack Meadowlands Reclamation and Development Act (Act), N.J. Stat. Ann. § 13:17-1 et seq., featured the establishment of an "intermunicipal account" to adjust among the constituent municipalities the losses and benefits accruing from the development of a meadowlands district. Previously, the Act's scheme was held to be constitutional against an attack that it was arbitrary. Mounting another constitutional challenge, appellant township contended that the Act required it to pay more than its fair share into the account. Essentially, appellant asserted that the Act failed to make timely adjustments for reductions in the aggregate assessed value because the Act did not account for assessment modifications in the tax court. The trial court entered summary judgment against appellant, which sought review. The court affirmed, holding that, because appellant was a municipality, it did not have standing to raise equal protection arguments against the state. Moreover, even if appellant had standing, it failed to support its equal protection argument with any evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's entry of summary judgment against appellant township in its constitutional challenge to the Hackensack Meadowlands Reclamation and Development Act, holding that, owing to its status as a municipality, appellant lacked standing to bring an equal protection claim against the state.

Edgewater Inv. Associates v. Edgewater


A-3975-83T3


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


201 N.J. Super. 267; 493 A.2d 11; 1985 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1255


March 19, 1985, Argued  
April 22, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Hudson County whose opinion is reported in    N.J. Super.     (Ch. Div. 1984).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant tenants appealed an order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Hudson County, which interpreted the Senior Citizens and Disabled Protected Tenancy Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:18-61.22 et seq., only partly in their favor. Plaintiff landlord cross-appealed, asserting that the act impaired existing contracts, in violation of U.S. Const. art. I, § 10, cl. 1, and N.J. Const. art. IV, § VII, par. 3.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff landlord converted an apartment complex to condomiums. Two months later, the Senior Citizens and Disabled Protected Tenancy Act (Act), N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:18-61.22 et seq., was enacted with retroactive effect, granting protected status against removal to defendant tenants. Plaintiff brought an action to require defendants to vacate the premises but the trial court found for defendants, except on one point. Defendants appealed and plaintiff cross-appealed. The court found that the Act did not impermissibly impair existing contracts in violation of U.S. Const. art. I, § 10, cl. 1, or N.J. Const. art. IV, § VII, par. 3. The state had a long history of regulating the housing industry and the remedial purpose of protecting elderly citizens constituted an appropriate governmental objective. The court also found that no taking had been committed simply because plaintiff was prevented from obtaining maximum profit. The court affirmed the trial court's enforcement of the Act against plaintiff but reversed the portion regarding defendants' applications under the Act, finding that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:18-61.24c only included their net, rather than gross, business income.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of defendant tenants on the action by plaintiff landlord to have them vacate their apartments so that condominiums could be sold, finding that the Senior Citizens and Disabled Protected Tenancy Act was constitutional in granting defendants a 40-year stay. The court reversed the judgment allowing consideration of defendants' gross business income in their applications.

Windman v. Englewood


A-4238-83T6


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


200 N.J. Super. 218; 491 A.2d 32; 1985 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1235


March 18, 1985, Argued  
April 10, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court, Law Division, Bergen County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, city and rent board, sought review of the judgment from the Superior Court of New Jersey, which found that the rollback provisions of Englewood, N.J., Ordinance 83-42 (1983), a rent control ordinance, were invalid.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff property owners brought suit seeking to invalidate Englewood, N.J., Ordinance No. 83-42 (1983), a rent control ordinance which lowered the annual rent increase limit and which was retroactive four months before its enactment. The trial court invalidated the rollback provision, finding that it impaired obligations under contracts, and the trial court upheld one plaintiff's rent increase during the rollback period. Defendants, city and rent board, appealed. The reviewing court vacated and reversed. The reviewing court upheld the ordinance, including the rollback provision. The reviewing court held that Ordinance No. 83-42 was a rational means to address a significant and legitimate public interest. The reviewing court found that the ordinance did not violate due process of law.


OUTCOME: The reviewing court vacated the trial court's judgment insofar as it upheld plaintiff property owner's specific rent increases, and the reviewing court reversed the invalidation of the rollback provision. The reviewing court held that the rent control ordinance, including the rollback provision, was a valid exercise of police power and did not violate due process.

 

1226 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gilmore


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


199 N.J. Super. 389; 489 A.2d 1175; 1985 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1402


May 2, 1984, Argued  
March 8, 1985, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Remanded May 21, 1984. Reargued October 17, 1984.
Certification granted State v. Gilmore, 101 N.J. 285, 501 A.2d 948, 1985 N.J. LEXIS 2728 (1985)
Affirmed by State v. Gilmore, 103 N.J. 508, 511 A.2d 1150, 1986 N.J. LEXIS 970 (1986)


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Gilmore, 195 N.J. Super. 163, 478 A.2d 783, 1984 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1391 (App.Div., 1984)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction by the New Jersey trial court of three first degree robberies. Defendant was tried by a jury after the assistant prosecutor excluded of all black prospective petit jurors by the use of peremptory challenges and was sentenced to three concurrent 15 year custodial terms with five years of parole ineligibility.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of three first-degree robberies of two attendants at a gasoline station, and was sentenced to three concurrent 15-year custodial terms with five years of parole ineligibility. Defendant, who was black, was tried to an all-white jury, comprised of six males and six females. During the jury selection, nine black potential jurors were seated in the jury box at different times. Two of them were excused for cause. The assistant prosecutor used peremptory challenges to excuse the remaining seven black prospective jurors. The court reversed, holding that peremptory challenges could only be used to eliminate prospective jurors based on a bias which related to the case on trial, the parties, attorneys or witnesses in the case, and that N.J. Const. art. I, paras. 5, 9, 10 proscribed the use of peremptory challenges to exclude prospective jurors solely by virtue of their membership in a cognizable group. The court found the assistant prosecutor's reasons for his preemptory challenges were sham excuses belatedly contrived to avoid admitting acts of group discrimination against all the black prospective jurors.


OUTCOME: The court reversed, holding that defendant was denied his right to a fair and impartial trial. The court found that the assistant prosecutor systematically excluded all black prospective petit jurors based on group association, rather than individual bias, in violation of defendant's rights.

 

1227 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Spring Lake Hotel & Guest House Asso. v. Spring Lake


A-5705-83T5


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


199 N.J. Super. 201; 488 A.2d 1076; 1985 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1184


December 3, 1984, Argued  
March 5, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Monmouth County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, hotel association, members, and residents, challenged an order of the Superior Court, Law Division, Monmouth County (New Jersey), which entered judgment in favor of defendant city in an action brought by plaintiffs claiming that defendant's ordinance prohibiting overnight on-street parking was invalid.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, hotel association, members, and residents, brought an action against defendant city, claiming that defendant's ordinance prohibiting overnight on-street parking was invalid. The trial court entered judgment for defendant. The appellate court affirmed, holding that the adoption of the ordinance was a valid exercise of the police power. Among other things, the ordinance aided police, fire, and first aid protection, aided traffic flow, particularly in inclement weather, and eased identification of unauthorized and suspicious vehicles. Further, the appellate court held defendant was not estopped from enforcing its ordinance due its nonenforcement in the past when the number of cars dramatically increased. The appellate court held that an ordinance could not be repealed by inaction. Further, there was no evidence of a studied policy not to enforce the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's order in favor of defendant city in an action brought by plaintiffs, hotel association, members, and residents, claiming that defendant's ordinance prohibiting overnight on-street parking was invalid. The fact that defendant had previously extended a courtesy to plaintiffs did not estop defendant from enforcing the ordinance when the number of cars dramatically increased.

Glassboro v. Gloucester County Bd. of Chosen Freeholders


A-1440-84T5


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


199 N.J. Super. 91; 488 A.2d 562; 1985 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1176


December 17, 1984, Argued  
February 15, 1985, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certification granted Glassboro v. Gloucester County Bd. of Chosen Freeholders, 101 N.J. 240, 501 A.2d 915, 1985 N.J. LEXIS 2543 (1985)
 Affirmed by Glassboro v. Gloucester County Bd. of Chosen Freeholders, 100 N.J. 134, 495 A.2d 49, 1985 N.J. LEXIS 2357 (1985)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Gloucester County.
 Glassboro v. Gloucester County Bd. of Chosen Freeholders, 98 N.J. 186, 485 A.2d 299, 1984 N.J. LEXIS 3570 (1984)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff borough appealed an order in favor of defendant Department of Environmental Protection entered by the Superior Court of New Jersey, Gloucester County, which barred any person or entity outside the southern New Jersey area from using defendant landfill, a privately owned and state regulated landfill.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff borough sough review of an order in favor of defendant Department of Environmental Protection, which closed and barred the use of defendant landfill to entities outside the tri-county area. Defendant landfill notified its customers that it would reach capacity and would close. Plaintiff filed a verified complaint to enjoin the closure and restricted use of defendant landfill. On appeal, the court affirmed the order, holding that by approving the new 16-foot vertical lift that would extend capacity of defendant landfill, the trial court ordered defendant landfill to accept new waste beyond its previously-determined environmentally-sound and lawful disposal capacity, but only to assure local health concerns, not to enhance provincial economic interests. The court also found that the order did not violate U.S. Const. Art. I, § 8, because it barred all trash from the emergently affected area and therefore it was not based on origin alone. Lastly, the court found that the trial court's order was narrowly tailored in duration, location, and neutrality of preclusion to meet the emergency needs of the citizens until new waste disposal sites could be established.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order, which barred any person or entity from outside the tri-county area from using defendant landfill, a privately owned, state regulated landfill. The court found that the trial court's order in favor of defendant Department of Environmental Protection did not violate the U.S. Constitutional rights of plaintiff borough.

 

1229 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Humanik


A-5197-81T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


199 N.J. Super. 283; 489 A.2d 691; 1985 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1189


January 8, 1985, Argued  
February 6, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Ocean County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction by the Superior Court of New Jersey, Ocean County, for murder pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:11-3.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of the murder of his former girlfriend and sentenced to life in prison pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:4-2, which required defendant to prove mental disease or defect by a preponderance of the evidence once the defense of diminished capacity was raised. Defendant appealed his conviction. The court affirmed defendant's conviction, holding that the application of § 2C:4-2 did not violate defendant's substantive and procedural due process rights and was properly applied at defendant's trial because the prosecution was required to establish the requisite state of defendant's criminal culpability beyond a reasonable doubt after the defense was raised. The trial judge's instructions clearly apprised the jury of the prosecution's obligation in that regard. The court also held that the retroactive application of § 2C:4-2 was not a violation of the ex post facto prohibition set forth in U.S. Const. art. I, §10, cl.1, or N.J. Const. art. IV, § VII, para. 3, because it did not decrease the nature, amount, or quality of the evidence the prosecution was required to present in order to obtain a conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for murder, holding that defendant's due process rights were not violated by the application of a statute requiring that defendant prove his defense of mental disease or defect by a preponderance of the evidence because the prosecution was required to bear the burden of establishing the requisite state of criminal culpability beyond a reasonable doubt.

 

1230 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jones


A-197-84T5


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


198 N.J. Super. 553; 487 A.2d 1278; 1985 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1167


January 8, 1985, Submitted  
January 29, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Atlantic County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the state of New Jersey, sought review from a judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Atlantic County, which granted defendant's motion to dismiss the charge of possession of a weapon having previously been convicted of a crime in violation of N. J. Stat. Ann. § 2C: 39-7.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, the state of New Jersey, challenged the dismissal of the charge against defendant of possession of a weapon having previously been convicted of a crime in violation of N. J. Stat. Ann. § 2C: 39-7. The court found that no U. S. Const. amend. I rights were implicated, nor did the statutory prohibition substantially impinge upon constitutionally protected conduct. Rather, the clear statutory purpose was to deter those previously convicted of serious crimes from possessing dangerous weapons. There clearly was a rational nexus between the statute and a valid legislative purpose. The court held that § 2C: 39-7 was not overly broad. Further, the court found that § 2C: 39-7 was sufficiently precise in its language to apprise the citizenry of the conduct proscribed. The statute provided fair notice of the activities prohibited and did not constitute a trap for a person of ordinary intelligence acting in good faith. Accordingly, the court reversed the order granting defendant's motion to dismiss and remanded for trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order granting defendant's motion to dismiss the charge of possession of a weapon having previously been convicted of a crime and remanded for trial in favor of appellant, the state of New Jersey. The court held that there was sufficiently precise language in the statute to apprise the citizenry of the conduct proscribed and it was not overly broad. The statute provided fair notice of the activities prohibited.

Falcone v. De Furia


A-4899-83T7


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


199 N.J. Super. 554; 489 A.2d 1263; 1985 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1136


December 11, 1984, Argued

 Affirmed by Falcone v. De Furia, 103 N.J. 219, 510 A.2d 1174, 1986 N.J. LEXIS 968 (1986)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Superior Court, Law Division, Passaic County whose opinion is reported at    N.J.Super.    .
 Falcone v. Defuria, 199 N.J. Super. 549, 489 A.2d 1260, 1984 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1303 (Law Div., 1984)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prosecutor and police chief sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Passaic County, which entered judgment in favor of respondent mayor and committee. The trial court held that N. J. Stat. Ann. § 40:A14-118 (1981), was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant prosecutor and police chief brought a declaratory judgment action to have the municipal ordinance N. J. Stat. Ann. § 40:A14-118 (1981), declared unconstitutional. Appellants asserted that the ordinance gave exclusive power of the internal operation of the police force to the police chief. Upon review, the court affirmed he trial court's judgment for respondents, mayor and committee, and found that appellants conceded that the power to appoint various officers to the police force and to promote officers resided exclusively in the governing body. Continental Trailways, Inc. v. Director, Div. of Motor Vehicles


A-2203-83T2


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


201 N.J. Super. 71; 492 A.2d 1016; 1985 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1308


December 5, 1984, Argued  
January 2, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the New Jersey Tax Court, opinion reported at 6 N.J. Tax 42.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, New Jersey Division of Motor Vehicle, sought review of the decision of the New Jersey Tax Court, which entered judgment in favor of respondent bus service. The tax court struck down as unconstitutional the bus excise tax imposed under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 48:4-20.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, New Jersey Division of Motor Vehicle, sought review of the tax court's judgment in favor of respondent bus service. The tax court struck down as unconstitutional the bus excise tax imposed under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 48:4-20. The tax court held that it unconstitutionally burdened interstate commerce in violation of the Commerce Clause, U. S. Const. art. I, § 8, cl. 3, because regularly scheduled intrastate passenger service was exempted from it. Upon review, the court affirmed and stated that interstate commerce could be taxed its fair share of highway repair and maintenance, but not more. The court stated that the imposition of the bus excise tax upon interstate bus travel only was patently not a fair share and was unjustified under decisional law authority or as the implementation of a legislative policy to subsidize indirectly state bus companies.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of respondent bus company that held that the bus excise tax imposed on interstate commerce was unconstitutional because intrastate bus service was exempt from it. Interstate commerce was taxed more than its fair share for highway repair and maintenance.

 

1233 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. McMinn


A-4619-81T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


197 N.J. Super. 621; 485 A.2d 1072; 1984 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1268


November 26, 1984, Submitted  
December 24, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On Appeal from Superior Court, Law Division, Morris County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, charged with distribution of more than one ounce of cocaine, of which at least 3.5 grams were pure freebase cocaine, sought review of an order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Morris County, which denied his motion for dismissal. Defendant claimed that the legislative classification of cocaine as a "narcotic" drug was erroneous and therefore violative of his constitutional guarantees of equal protection and due process.


OVERVIEW: Defendant filed a motion for dismissal of the count of the indictment charging him with distribution of more than one ounce of cocaine, of which at least 3.5 grams were pure freebase cocaine. At issue was his claim that the classification of cocaine as a Schedule II narcotic under the New Jersey Controlled Dangerous Substances Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 24: 21-1 et seq. violated his constitutional rights of equal protection and due process. The court found that although biologically a narcotic was a drug derived from the opium poppy and cocaine was not biologically a narcotic, its classification as such for purposes of regulation and penalty was not a constitutional violation, because it posed serious problems for the community and had a high potential for abuse. The court determined that the state statute was not unconstitutionally vague, because its definition of a "pure free base" drug apprised defendant that his particular conduct was unlawful. In affirming the denial of the motion to dismiss, the court held that the classification of cocaine as a Schedule II narcotic was constitutionally sound.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of defendant's motion to dismiss charges for distribution of more than one ounce of cocaine, of which at least 3.5 grams were pure freebase cocaine. The court held that the classification of cocaine as a "narcotic" drug did not violate his constitutional guarantees of equal protection and due process.

In re Z.O.


A-2621-83T5, A-2667-83T5, A-2990-83T5


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


197 N.J. Super. 330; 484 A.2d 1287; 1984 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1249


September 12, 1984, Argued  
December 12, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court, Law Division, Essex County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant psychiatric patients sought a consolidated review of decisions by the Superior Court, Essex County (New Jersey), which committed them for psychiatric treatment, on the grounds that the applications for commitment under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 30:4-38 were filed after the time limit set therein.


OVERVIEW: The trial court committed appellant psychiatric patients for treatment on applications that appellants asserted were filed after the period allowed by statute. Their cases were consolidated for appeal after they were released from hospitalization, and the court affirmed. The court found that the 20-day period within which N.J. Stat. Ann. § 30:4-38 required a hearing to be held on a commitment application ran from the end of the statutory post-entry observation period, not from the date appellants physically entered the hospital. The court found that the period appellants were hospitalized before their hearing did not deprive them of their constitutional rights. The court held that, absent constitutional violation, it was proper to hear the late applications to commit appellants and, provided the applications were otherwise facially valid, it was proper to schedule them for prompt hearings. The court ruled that minor time delays did not require the trial court to dismiss the applications where two physicians said appellants would be a danger to themselves or others outside of the hospital. The interests of appellants and of the community outweighed the benefit of penalizing delays.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's commitment orders because, absent a constitutional violation, it was proper to entertain the late commitment applications and, if they otherwise were facially valid, to schedule them for prompt hearings. The minor lateness did not warrant dismissal of the applications for appellant psychiatric patients' hospitalization after doctors opined that they posed a danger to themselves or others.

 

1235 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Genesis Leasing Corp.


A-3072-83T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


197 N.J. Super. 284; 484 A.2d 1263; 1984 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1233


October 9, 1984, Argued  
November 28, 1984, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reargued November 5, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court, Law Division, Burlington County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants challenged the judgments of conviction from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Burlington County, for seven violations of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:3-84.3, that provided penalties for operators of trucks exceeding the axle weight limitations set forth in N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:3-84(b).


OVERVIEW: Defendants' overweight trucks were registered in Pennsylvania, but not in New Jersey. Defendants challenged the lower court's judgments of conviction, contending that their vehicles were not subject to axle weight limitations because under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:3-84.1, the legislature had intended only to regulate the axle weights of vehicles registered in New Jersey. The court affirmed the judgments of conviction. It held that there was no reason to exempt out-of-state vehicles from the axle weight limitations. The purpose of the weight limitations was to protect the highways from damage from overweight vehicles, and defendants' argument would frustrate that purpose. Further, to use Pennsylvania solid waste vehicles in New Jersey and take benefit of a statutory exception, defendants would be required to obtain dual registrations and pay fees to both jurisdictions. The court finally found that the burden created by the state's axle weight limitations was reasonable and was far outweighed by the state's benefit receiving compensation for highway damage. Thus, it was a reasonable nondiscriminatory burden and was tolerated.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgments of conviction for seven violations of operating trucks that exceeded the axle weight limitations. The court held that the vehicles were subject to the axle weight limitations and to benefit from the statutory exception required obtaining dual registrations and paying fees to both jurisdictions.

D'Ercole v. Norwood


A-1201-83T3


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


198 N.J. Super. 531; 487 A.2d 1266; 1984 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1294


September 10, 1984, Argued  
November 16, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Bergen County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff former councilman appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Bergen County, which was granted in favor of defendants, the mayor and council, on a complaint in lieu of prerogative writ, which was filed by plaintiff. Plaintiff contended that an ordinance authorizing a long-term lease with intervenor volunteer fire company was invalid under N.J. Const. art. VIII, § III, para. 2 (1947).


OVERVIEW: In an attempt to resolve the problem of housing intervenor volunteer fire company, defendants, the mayor and council, adopted an ordinance, which authorized a long-term lease for the firehouse. Plaintiff former councilman filed a complaint in lieu of prerogative writ to challenge the validity of the ordinance. The trial court entered judgment in favor of defendants. The court affirmed. The court held that the lease had a public purpose, inherent in providing firehouse facilities to the community, which insulated the ordinance from an attack under N.J. Const. art. VIII, § III, para. 2 (1947). The court held that the lease was of a type expressly authorized by the Local Lands and Building Law, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40A:12-15, and permitted by the Local Budget Law, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40A:4-57(b). The court found that the total sum payable over the term of the lease was not a present debt, that the execution of the lease was a discretionary executive action, and that the ordinance was not the proper subject for a referendum.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment entered in favor of defendants, the mayor and council, in an action by plaintiff former councilman challenging the validity of an ordinance authorizing a lease with intervenor volunteer fire company. The court held that the ordinance had a public purpose insulating it from attack on constitutional grounds, and that the execution of the lease was an administrative act and was not subject to review by referendum.
