State v. Fort


A-3391-81T4, A-3402-81T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


197 N.J. Super. 113; 484 A.2d 323; 1984 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1202


September 18, 1984, Submitted  
October 25, 1984, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certification denied by State v. Fort, 101 N.J. 213, 501 A.2d 895, 1985 N.J. LEXIS 2425 (1985)
Certification denied by State v. Muhammad, 101 N.J. 216, 501 A.2d 898, 1985 N.J. LEXIS 2441 (1985)
Reversed by State v. Fort, 101 N.J. 123, 501 A.2d 140, 1985 N.J. LEXIS 2400 (1985)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Essex County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Essex County, on remand from the appellate division, that determined they were not denied compulsory process in their jury trials in which they were found guilty for conspiracy to possess and distribute controlled dangerous substances, possession, and possession with intent to distribute.


OVERVIEW: Defendants and co-defendants were charged with conspiracy to possess and distribute controlled dangerous substances, possession, and possession with intent to distribute. Co-defendants entered into plea agreements that included no testimony agreements in which they promised not to testify. Neither defendant issued a subpoena for co-defendants, and both were convicted by a jury of all charges. They appealed based on the no testimony agreements. The appellate division remanded the matter to the law division, and the trial judge found that there was no deprivation of their rights protected by U.S. Const. amend. VI, U.S. Const. amend XIV, and N.J. Const. art. I, para. 10. The court affirmed the judgment because although the plea agreement with the co-defendants that included the no testimony agreement was misconduct by the prosecutor that was intended to deprive defendants of compulsory process, in order to prevail defendants must have established prejudice. Since the decision not to subpoena co-defendants was a trial strategy, and defendants did not subpoena co-defendants in order to force them to choose whether or not to testify, they showed no prejudice.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed because although the plea agreement with the co-defendants that included the no testimony agreement was misconduct by the prosecutor intended to deprive defendants of compulsory process, in order to prevail defendants must have established prejudice. Because the decision not to subpoena co-defendants was a trial strategy, and defendants did not force co-defendants to choose whether or not to testify, they showed no prejudice.

State v. Latimore


A-3412-81T4, A-3459-81T4, A-3582-81T4, A-4795-81T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


197 N.J. Super. 197; 484 A.2d 702; 1984 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1206


August 28, 1984, Argued  
October 24, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Monmouth County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed their convictions in the Superior Court, Monmouth County (New Jersey), for possession of a prohibited weapon, a sawed-off shotgun, possession of the shotgun and two handguns with a purpose to use them unlawfully, and possession without obtaining a permit to carry two handguns. N.J. Stat. Ann. 2C:39-3b, 2C:39-4a, 2C:39-5b and 2C:58-4, respectively.


OVERVIEW: Defendants appealed their convictions for possession of a prohibited weapon. A sawed-off shotgun, possession of a sawed-off shotgun and two handguns with a purpose to use them unlawfully, and possession without obtaining a permit to carry two handguns. The court concluded that defendants' motion for acquittal was properly denied. Their claims that the verdicts were against the weight of the evidence and of an improper jury charge were not preserved for appeal, and, nonetheless, were without merit. The court affirmed the convictions, except two charges were merged and the corresponding sentences were vacated. The essence of the offenses was the failure to have a permit and the unlawful purpose, and neither was expanded or diminished by the quantity of weapons constructively possessed. The court concluded that the handgun convictions for no permit and the convictions for unlawful purpose should have been merged. One defendant did not have written notice of the intention to impose an extended sentence, thus, those sentences were vacated and remanded for resentencing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions, except the handgun convictions, which were merged and the sentences imposed on those counts were vacated. The sentences imposed on two counts were vacated for one of defendant and the matter remanded to the trial judge for resentencing, without extended terms. On remand, the trial judge was directed to set forth expanded statements of reasons for the sentences imposed upon two of defendants.

Keyes Martin & Co. v. Director, Div. of Purchase & Property, Dep't of Treasury


A-5967-82T2


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


196 N.J. Super. 52; 481 A.2d 572; 1984 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1148


May 1, 1984, Argued  
September 5, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from a final determination of the Director of the Division of Purchase and Property.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant advertising company sought review of a final determination of the Director of the Division of Purchase and Property (New Jersey), which rejected appellant's low bid for a two-year advertising contract with the New Jersey Lottery Commission on the grounds that appellant had maintained a business relationship with the chairman of the Lottery Commission.


OVERVIEW: Appellant advertising company was the low bidder for a contract to provide advertising for the New Jersey Lottery Commission, but respondent, the Director of the New Jersey Division of Purchase and Property, rejected appellant's bid because of an appearance of wrongdoing associated with appellant's relationship with the lottery commission director. The court vacated the order rejecting appellant's bid and held that the standard respondent applied was non-objective and improper and that respondent abused his discretion in applying it. The court found that rejecting public bids based on a subjective standard of an appearance of wrongdoing absent a finding of actual wrongdoing would undermine confidence in the public bidding process. The court directed that the contract be awarded to appellant and found no principled basis on which to say that respondent could reject bidders for contracts with the lottery commission under criteria distinctly different from those applicable to other user agencies.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the order of respondent Director of the State Division of Purchase and Property and ordered that the New Jersey Lottery Commission advertising contract be awarded to appellant advertising agency because it was the best qualified and lowest responsible bidder and because there was no finding that appellant engaged in wrongdoing or that its winning of the advertising contract would compromise the lottery commission's integrity.

Reed v. Attorney Gen.


A-4010-82T3


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


195 N.J. Super. 172; 478 A.2d 788; 1984 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1073


March 14, 1984, Argued  
August 7, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from New Jersey Commissioner of Education.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parents sought review of a decision of the New Jersey Commissioner of Education. Appellants had a child resident in New Jersey but enrolled in a private school in Pennsylvania and unsuccessfully challenged the refusal by the local Board of Education of their request for private school transportation. Appellants asserted that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 18A:39-1 was unconstitutional as limited to New Jersey.


OVERVIEW: Appellant parents unsuccessfully challenged the refusal by the local board of education (board) of their request for private school transportation for their child to a private school in Pennsylvania. Appellants sought review of respondent New Jersey Commissioner of Education's decision and alleged that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 18A:39-1 was unconstitutional as a violation of equal protection if limited to New Jersey. On review, the court affirmed respondent's decision. The court first noted that respondent lacked jurisdiction to decide constitutional claims, but that their decision was sound. The court held that the equal protection clause did not require uniformity provided that the classification was reasonable. The court found that controlling the expenditures of local school boards by limiting buses to school in New Jersey was a reasonable classification that did not offend equal protection. Thus, the limitation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 18A:39-1 to payment for transportation within the state was constitutionally permissible.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of respondent New Jersey Commissioner of Education because the equal protection clause did not require uniformity in all things, provided that the classification was reasonable. The limitation of the statute to payment for transportation within the state, found to be controlling upon the expenditure of the local board, did not offend the equal protection clause and was reasonable.

State v. Sarto


A-4532-82T5


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


195 N.J. Super. 565; 481 A.2d 281; 1984 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1132


June 6, 1984, Argued  
August 1, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court, Law Division, Salem County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed the order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, which, pursuant to defendant's petition for post-conviction relief, suppressed the marijuana found in defendant's car, and vacated his conviction for possession of marijuana with intent to distribute.


OVERVIEW: After a state trooper conducted a routine stop of defendant's vehicle and discovered a knife and marijuana, defendant was charged with unlawful possession of marijuana, possession of marijuana with intent to distribute, and unlawful possession of a dangerous weapon. When his motion to suppress the evidence was denied, defendant pleaded guilty to counts two and three under a plea agreement that dismissed count one. Defendant later filed a petition for post-conviction relief. The trial court granted defendant's petition, suppressed the evidence, and vacated his conviction. On appeal, the court reversed. The court found that while the valid search of defendant's car had become invalid by retroactive application of case law since his arrest, the application of two more recent cases had made the search valid again. The court found that pursuant to these cases, the search of both the interior and the trunk of defendant's car was reasonable, and constitutionally permissible, and the evidence should not have been suppressed. As the evidence was admissible, the court reversed the order below.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment vacating defendant's conviction for possession of marijuana with intent to distribute. The court held that the searches of the interior and trunk of defendant's car were reasonable and constitutionally permissible, and thus, the evidence should not have been suppressed.

State v. Curtis

Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division

July 18, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On Appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Monmouth County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Monmouth County, which convicted him of aggravated manslaughter and sentenced him to 20 years imprisonment with 10 years of parole ineligibility.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated manslaughter. Defendant challenged the conviction on various grounds. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment conviction defendant of aggravated manslaughter, holding that although the trial judge's jury charge on the difference between reckless manslaughter and aggravated manslaughter was somewhat unclear, the trial judge did instruct the jury on the difference in terms of probabilities. The court held that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:11-4 was not unconstitutionally vague or overbroad. The court determined that the statute gives a person of ordinary intelligence a reasonable opportunity to know what is prohibited so that he or she may conform his acts to the law. The court also concluded that the sentence imposed by the lower court was not excessive. The court held that for first degree crimes there is a presumptive sentence of 15 years. Thus, the court upheld the lower court's imposition of sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment convicting defendant of aggravated manslaughter. The court held that although the trial court's jury charge regarding the difference between reckless manslaughter and aggravated manslaughter was unclear, the judge properly instructed on the difference in terms of probabilities. The court concluded that the applicable statute was not unconstitutional because the prohibited behavior was clear.

State v. Witrak


A-1263-83T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


194 N.J. Super. 526; 477 A.2d 412; 1984 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1018


May 2, 1984, Submitted  
June 28, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court, Law Division, Passaic County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment by the Superior Court, Passaic County (New Jersey), which found him in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 43:21-16(e) for failing to remit unemployment insurance contributions. Defendant contended that this statute was unconstitutional because it violated N.J. Const. art. I, par. 13 and did not require proof of fraudulent intent by defendant.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found in violation of several counts of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 43:21-16(e) for failing to remit unemployment insurance contributions of employees to the state. Defendant contended that this statute was unconstitutional because it violated N.J. Const. art I, par. 13. The court held that § 43:21-16(e) imposes quasi-criminal liability for failing to remit the payments with intent to defraud the state. The court noted that there were other civil remedies available to collect unemployment taxes where no fraud was evidenced.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's convictions for failing to remit unemployment insurance contributions of his employees and dismissed the complaints. The court held that the state failed to prove that defendant acted with an intent to defraud the state which was required by the statute under which he was charged.

Country Club Towers Tenants' Asso. v. Country Club Towers I & II


A-1553-83T3


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


195 N.J. Super. 110; 478 A.2d 420; 1984 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1054


May 23, 1984, Argued  
June 22, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court, Law Division, Bergen County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff tenants' association sought review of a decision by the Superior Court of New Jersey, Bergen County, which upheld a decision by defendant municipal council that its vote by three members to two, to reverse a rent leveling board capital improvement surcharge, was a nullity because less than a majority of all seven members of defendant voted in the affirmative.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff tenants' association filed an action against defendant municipal council and challenged its decision that a vote by three members to two to reverse a rent leveling board capital improvement surcharge was a nullity because less than a majority of all seven members of the defendant voted in the affirmative. The trial court entered judgment in favor of the defendant. On review, the court affirmed the trial court's decision. In reaching its decision, the court held that under a municipal manager form of government, N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 40:79-1 to 40:84-19, a majority of all the members of the defendant constituted a quorum and the affirmative vote of a majority of all the members was necessary to take any action or pass any measure. N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40:81-20. Accordingly, the court held that the action challenged by the plaintiff's was a nullity, because less than a majority of the members of the defendant voted in the affirmative.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, holding that plaintiff tenants' association was not entitled to prevail in its action against defendant municipal council. The court held that the decision by the defendant was a nullity, because the vote was not supported by a majority of its members, as required by the statute.

Seton Co. v. Newark


A-5975-82T2


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


194 N.J. Super. 499; 477 A.2d 397; 1984 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1023


June 11, 1984, Argued  
June 20, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court, Law Division, Essex County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city appealed the order of the Superior Court, Essex County (New Jersey), which found that its ordinance establishing sewer user charges was unreasonable, invalid, and unlawful under state law in plaintiff large-scale water user's action to invalidate the ordinance. Plaintiff had attacked the ordinance as violative of due process and equal protection, under the U.S. Constitution, and that it constituted a taking.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff large-scale water user operated a water-intensive business. Defendant city adopted an ordinance that established sewer user charges, requiring large-scale users to assume a greater responsibility than small scale users for the costs of operating the sewer system. Plaintiff filed an action to invalidate the ordinance, claiming that it violated state law because it was arbitrary, that it violated the due process and equal protection clauses of the U.S. Constitution, and that it constituted a taking. The trial court entered judgment for plaintiff, holding that the ordinance was unreasonable under state law. The court reversed the order, holding that the ordinance was not arbitrary or unreasonable under state law, as it reasonably concluded that the benefit conferred on the user was directly proportionate to his use of the system. The ordinance did not violate due process, as it was not arbitrary or unreasonable. The ordinance did not violate U.S. Const. amend. XIV, as there was no taking because indirect costs were a cost of the system. The ordinance did not violate the Equal Protection Clause, as it did not make unreasonable classifications.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order, holding that the ordinance adopted by defendant city, which charged plaintiff large-scale water user more for the costs of operating the sewer system than small-scale users, was not arbitrary under state law, as charges were allocated, under the ordinance, based on the conclusion that a user's benefit was directly proportionate to his use of the system.

Stroman v. Brown


A-4206-82T2


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


194 N.J. Super. 307; 476 A.2d 874; 1984 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1097


April 9, 1984, Argued  
June 7, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Atlantic County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant owner challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Atlantic County (New Jersey), which enforced a default judgment rendered against defendant owner and defendant driver in Pennsylvania for liability to plaintiffs, injured party and spouse, arising from an automobile accident that involved defendant owner's vehicle driven by his spouse, defendant driver.


OVERVIEW: Defendant owner allowed defendant driver to take his vehicle to Pennsylvania, where she was in an accident. Plaintiffs, injured party and spouse, brought suit in Pennsylvania and recovered a default judgment against defendants for damages arising out of the accident. Defendant owner contended that Pennsylvania did not have personal jurisdiction over him such that the instant New Jersey trial court must give full faith and credit to the judgment. Pennsylvania's long-arm statute, 75 P.S. § 2001 (Supp. 1971), included a nonresident owner of a motor vehicle operated in Pennsylvania with his consent. However, the court held that defendant owner did not purposefully avail himself of activities in Pennsylvania by casually giving his wife permission to drive his vehicle there on her personal business. Thus, the judgment entered against defendant owner was not entitled to full faith and credit. Defendants' other issues were rendered moot by this opinion reversing that judgment. Because defendant driver died, those having an interest in her estate had to be made parties as required by N.J. R. Civ. P. 4:34-1(b) before a judgment against her estate could be valid.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment against defendant owner because he did not purposefully avail himself of activities in Pennsylvania, and thus the judgment against him was not entitled to full faith and credit in New Jersey. The court also reversed and remanded the judgment against defendant driver because she had subsequently died, and plaintiffs, injured party and spouse, had to substitute a proper party before proceeding against her estate.

Kessler v. Tarrats


A-4920-82T3


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


194 N.J. Super. 136; 476 A.2d 326; 1984 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1037


April 30, 1984, Submitted  
June 1, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Superior Court, Chancery Division, Passaic County reported at 191 N.J. Super. 273 (Ch. Div. 1983).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mortgage holder and appellant city challenged the judgment of the Superior Court, Passaic County (New Jersey), which was entered in the state's favor and which held that the Spill Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 58:10-23.11f(f), gave the state a paramount lien over appellant city's preexisting tax lien and the interests of appellant mortgage holder.


OVERVIEW: Toxic chemicals had been illegally stored on the property at issue. The property owner entered into a consent order with the state to clean up the property. The property owner defaulted under the consent order. The state obtained an order to clean up the site and expended considerable sums in performing that task. Appellant city also expended considerable sums in assisting in the clean up. Thereafter, appellant mortgage holder filed a complaint to foreclose on the property. Appellant city asserted a statutory lien on the property for unpaid taxes. The state filed its lien pursuant to the Spill Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 58:10-23.11f(f). The trial court entered judgment in the state's favor. Appellants challenged that judgment. On appeal, the court affirmed. The Spill Act lien provision was retroactive. Thus, appellant city's lien did not have priority over the state's lien. Also, appellant city had no rights against the state based on impairment of its statutory lien. If any impairment of appellant mortgage holder's contract occurred, such impairment was permissible under the state's police power. The imposition of the Spill Act lien was not a taking without just compensation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment which was entered in favor of the state. Because the state had been required to remove toxic waste from the subject property, the trial court properly gave it a priority lien over appellant city's preexisting tax lien on the property and appellant mortgage holder's interests in the property.

State v. New Jersey Trade Waste Asso.


A-560-83T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


194 N.J. Super. 90; 476 A.2d 301; 1984 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1045; 1984-2 Trade Cas. (CCH) P66,113


May 2, 1984, Argued  
May 22, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On Appeal from the Superior Court, Law Division, Somerset County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the State of New Jersey, sought relief from an order of the Superior Court, Law Division, Somerset County (New Jersey), which directed payment of fines to respondent county treasurer instead of the State Attorney General's revolving fund, as a result of successful prosecutions for violations of the Solid Waste Utility Control Act of 1970, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 48:13A-1 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Certain persons and firms pled guilty to monopolization in the garbage collection business in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 48:13A-10(a) of the Solid Waste Utility Control Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 48:13A-1 et seq., and were ordered to pay fines. Appellant sought relief from an order directing payment of the fines that resulted from these successful prosecutions to respondent. Appellant contended that the New Jersey Antitrust Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 56:9-19, allocated the fines to the State. Upon review, the court held that because the fines were derived from litigation instituted by the Attorney General under the State Antitrust Act, they were to be transferred to the State revolving fund.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order and remanded.

 

1249 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Abbott v. Burke


A-1526-83T5


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


195 N.J. Super. 59; 477 A.2d 1278; 1984 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1033


April 3, 1984, Argued  
May 11, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Superior Court, Chancery Division, Mercer County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff schoolchildren challenged an order of the Superior Court, Mercer County (New Jersey), which dismissed their complaint against defendant state education officials seeking a judgment that the finance provisions of the state's public education system were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff schoolchildren filed a complaint against defendant state education officials alleging that the finance provisions of the state's system of public education were unconstitutional. The trial court dismissed the complaint because plaintiffs failed to exhaust their administrative remedies. The court held that the trial court misunderstood the nature of the action as one requesting correction of deficiencies in plaintiffs' school districts' facilities and services, which could be repaired by increased funding. The court found that plaintiffs attacked the state's system of financing public education on the ground that it had produced gross disparities in financial resources for education. The court reversed and remanded because the exhaustion of administrative remedies was inapplicable since the issue to be decided was solely one of law, involving a question of constitutionality.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order dismissing plaintiff schoolchildren's complaint against defendant state education officials attacking the state's system of financing public education because plaintiffs were not required to first exhaust administrative remedies since the issue was solely one of law.

 

1250 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Booth v. Winslow


A-2467-82T2


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


193 N.J. Super. 637; 475 A.2d 644; 1984 N.J. Super. LEXIS 989


February 28, 1984, Argued  
March 15, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court, Law Division, Camden County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant police officer sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court, Camden County (New Jersey), which declared N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40A:14-122.1 unconstitutional. Section 40A:14-122.1 prohibited a municipality from requiring police officers to reside within the municipality as a condition of employment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant police officer was terminated by respondent, the township that employed him, because he did not reside in the township as required by a local ordinance. Appellant brought suit and contended that the ordinance violated the preemptive provisions of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40A:14-122.1 (statute). Respondent countered that the statute was unconstitutional because it was based on an irrational classification and that the ordinance was therefore valid and enforceable. After the trial court granted summary judgment in favor of respondent, appellant sought review. The court held that the statute constituted a valid exercise of legislative power because it bore a rational relationship to a legitimate governmental objective. The legislative scheme of which the statute was a part accorded municipalities the right to give preference to candidates who were also residents while allowing the municipalities to consider non-residents if necessary to maintain an adequate police force. The court held that the scheme constituted a rational response to a governmental problem. The court reversed the judgment and remanded the cause for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment holding that a statute was unconstitutional because it held that the statute bore a rational relationship to a legitimate governmental objective. The court remanded the cause for further proceedings.

 

1251 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


American Bank & Trust Co. v. Lott


A-5060-82T5


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


193 N.J. Super. 516; 475 A.2d 73; 1984 N.J. Super. LEXIS 990


February 15, 1984, Argued  
March 14, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Burlington County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant borrowers challenged the order of the Superior Court, Burlington County (New Jersey), which denied their motion to dismiss plaintiff foreign bank's complaint. Defendants claimed that plaintiff was barred from recovery for its failure to comply with the Corporation Business Activities Reporting Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 14A:13-14 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff foreign bank sought recovery on loans made to defendant borrowers. Defendants claimed that plaintiff's recovery was barred because it had not complied with the Corporation Business Activities Reporting Act (Reporting Act), N.J. Stat. Ann. § 14A:13-14 et seq. The court affirmed the order of the trial court that denied defendant's motion to dismiss plaintiff's complaint. The court held that because plaintiff had received a certificate from the Commissioner of Banking pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 17:9A-318 and 319, that certificate satisfied the requirements of plaintiff having received a certificate of authority to do business in the state under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 14A:13-16(a).The court found that the application for a certificate of authority for a non-banking foreign corporation under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 14A:13-4 was virtually the same as that required for the application for a limited certificate from a foreign bank. The court determined that this limited certificate satisfied the Reporting Act, did no violence to the state's need for information, and bound the corporation to comply with the state's taxation provisions.


OUTCOME: The court held that because plaintiff foreign bank had obtained a Certificate of Authority from the Commissioner of Banking under the Banking Act of 1948 (Act), it was relieved from filing a notice of Business Activities Report. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that denied defendant borrower's motion to dismiss plaintiff bank's cause of action.

 

1252 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Wrightstown v. Medved


A-841-82T3


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


193 N.J. Super. 398; 474 A.2d 1077; 1984 N.J. Super. LEXIS 974


December 5, 1983, Submitted  
March 5, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Tax Court of New Jersey, whose opinion is reported at 4 N.J.Tax 582 (1982).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant widower appealed a judgment from the Tax Court of New Jersey that upheld the constitutionality of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 54:4-3.30, in a suit by plaintiff Borough of Wrightstown to collect a property tax, despite the law's facial discrimination against widowers of disabled war veterans in the granting of a tax exemption to widows of disabled war veterans only.


OVERVIEW: Defendant widower's deceased wife was a disabled veteran. N.J. Stat. Ann. § 54:4-3.30 provided that widows of disabled veterans were entitled to an exemption from property taxes, but widowers of disabled veterans were not. The court held that § 54:4-3.30 and other similar discriminatory statutes violated the U.S. Const. amend XIV guarantee of equal protection insofar as they withheld from spouses of female veterans the tax relief given to spouses of male veterans. The court held that the state's policy of cushioning the financial impact of spousal loss upon the sex for whom that loss imposed a disproportionately heavy burden was not a sufficient governmental objective to support the classification. Because the class of women receiving the tax break was restricted to the wives of veterans, as opposed to all women, the tax break required further justification. This back-handed discrimination was unconstitutional. Rather than deprive the current beneficiaries of the exemption, and noting that the constitutional authorization for the exemption, N.J. Const. art. VIII, § 1, para. 3, was now gender-neutral, the court construed the statute to extend to widowers as well as widows.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment for plaintiff Borough of Wrightstown and reinstated the judgment for defendant widower. The court held that a tax exemption extended to the widows of disabled veterans but not to widowers of disabled veterans was a back-handed discrimination against women based on outmoded stereotypes, was not supported by an adequate governmental interest, and violated equal protection of the laws.

 

1253 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Dow Jones & Co. v. Director, Division of Taxation


A-3214-82T3


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


193 N.J. Super. 80; 472 A.2d 168; 1984 N.J. Super. LEXIS 951


February 21, 1984, Argued  
March 2, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from a final judgment of the Tax Court of New Jersey. 5 N.J. Tax 181 (Tax Ct. 1983).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff news service appealed the judgment from the Tax Court (New Jersey), which held that the imposition of sales tax on rental agreements did not constitute unfair and inequitable double taxation.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff news service leased equipment and was subject to sales tax on the rental agreements. Plaintiff challenged the tax, arguing that it constituted unfair and inequitable double taxation. On appeal the court noted that a sales tax on leased equipment was allowable, because the lease agreement was held to constitute a retail sale within the provisions of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 54:32B-3(a). The court further held that the method of auditing was not discriminatory, nor did the imposition of the tax place plaintiff at an economic disadvantage with regard to its competitors. The sales tax was held to be a self-executing tax that must be reported and paid by the taxpayer. The court dismissed plaintiff's other arguments and affirmed the judgment of the tax court.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the tax court, holding that the application of a sales tax to plaintiff news service's lease agreements was not unfair and inequitable double taxation, was affirmed because lease agreements had been held to constitute retail sales under the statute.

 

1254 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


O'Neill v. Washington


A-3062-82T3


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


193 N.J. Super. 481; 475 A.2d 55; 1984 N.J. Super. LEXIS 975


December 21, 1983, Argued  
February 22, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Bergen County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant municipality appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Bergen County, which held that defendant could not set off a refund of real estate taxes due plaintiff trustee in bankruptcy against taxes due for subsequent years on the same property.


OVERVIEW: The lower court held that defendant municipality could not set off a refund of real estate taxes due plaintiff trustee in bankruptcy against taxes due for subsequent years on the same property. On appeal, the court affirmed. The amendment to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 54:3-27.2 that authorized any municipal governing body to set off a refund of real estate property taxes against delinquent taxes owed on the same property became effective nearly a year after the action was commenced, and the action did not fall within the enumerated types of pending actions to which the amendment applied. Defendant asserted that plaintiff was equitably estopped from bringing this action, but defendant did not rely upon any conduct of plaintiff and was not led to change its position by any conduct of or inaction by plaintiff. There was no unreasonable delay by plaintiff in instituting suit for funds rightly due under a prior judgment. Defendant, of its own volition, improperly applied the refund to delinquent taxes instead of making a refund to plaintiff.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment holding that defendant municipality could not set off a refund of real estate taxes due plaintiff trustee in bankruptcy against taxes due for subsequent years on the same property. The amendment permitting such setoff was effective nearly one year after the action was filed, and it did not apply. Defendant did not rely on any conduct of plaintiff, and plaintiff was thus not estopped from bringing the action.

 

1255 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Conway


A-3501-82T1, A-4148-82T1


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


193 N.J. Super. 133; 472 A.2d 588; 1984 N.J. Super. LEXIS 948


January 11, 1984, Argued  
February 14, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court, Law Division, Ocean County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants challenged the decision of the Superior Court, Law Division, Ocean County (New Jersey), finding them guilty of conspiracy, tampering with a witness and bribery.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, attorney and defendant, were both found guilty of conspiracy. Appellant attorney was also found guilty of tampering with a witness and appellant defendant was found guilty of bribery. On appeal, the court found that appellant attorney attended an arranged meeting between himself and the complaining parties. At that meeting, appellant attorney indicated that appellant defendant had altered the original arrest report and discussed the possibility of having a putative witness purposely fail to identify appellant attorney's client. The court reasoned that this was sufficient evidence indicating appellant attorney was involved in tampering with the putative witness. Both appellants contended that the trial judge erroneously refused to hold a charge hearing. The court found that neither party requested a charge hearing, nor was the trial judge required to hold a charge hearing. Further, the court found that appellants did not object to the trial judge's failure to hold a charge hearing until after deliberations began. The court also rejected appellants' argument that the conviction for conspiracy should be reversed because the other conspirators were undercover agents.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellants' convictions for conspiracy, tampering with a witness and bribery. The court held that there was sufficient evidence for a jury to find, beyond a reasonable doubt, that appellant attorney co-conspired to tamper with a putative witness. Further, the court found that the trial judge did not commit error in his procedure in framing and delivering the jury charge.

 

1256 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Pitman v. Skokowski


A-4436-81T3


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


193 N.J. Super. 215; 473 A.2d 100; 1984 N.J. Super. LEXIS 963


November 9, 1983, Argued  
February 1, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Local Finance Board of State of New Jersey.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant borough challenged a decision of the Local Finance Board (New Jersey), which affirmed the denial of appellant's municipal budget by respondent, the Director of the Division of Local Government Services. Appellant's municipal budget had been denied, because it failed to deduct an amount equal to the cost of providing street lighting services after transferring responsibility for those services pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40A:4-45.2.


OVERVIEW: Appellant borough challenged the decision that denied approval of its municipal budget. Appellant created a lighting district pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 40:91-1 et seq. and transferred responsibility for its street lighting services. Appellee Director of the Division of Local Government Services disapproved the budget, because it had not deducted the amount equal to what it had expended to provide street lighting services in violation of 1981 N.J. Laws ch. 64, § 1, the supplement to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40A:4-45.2. Appellant argued that the retroactive application of that law divested appellant of a vested right, the right to establish a lighting district as a means of creating a valid legal exemption to the "CAP" law, in violation of the U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The court affirmed, holding that appellant, as a political subdivision of the state, had no standing to invoke protection of the U.S. Const. amend. XIV against the state. Appellant had no vested right by its creation of a lighting district prior to the enactment of the law, which was a valid exercise of the legislature's control over the financial affairs of appellant.


OUTCOME: The decision denying appellant borough's municipal budget was affirmed, because appellant was a political subdivision of the state and had no standing to invoke the protection of the Fourteenth Amendment of the United States Constitution against the state.

 

1257 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


S.M.Z. Corp. v. Director, Division of Taxation


A-1973-82T2


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


193 N.J. Super. 305; 473 A.2d 982; 1984 N.J. Super. LEXIS 958


November 7, 1983, Argued  
January 11, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from final judgment of Tax Court of New Jersey, 5 N.J. Tax 232 (Tax Ct. 1982).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer challenged a decision of the Tax Court of New Jersey, which held that appellant did not have a regular place of business outside of the state as defined in N.J. Stat. Ann. § 54:10A-6 and therefore respondent Director of Taxation could not allocate his income accordingly.


OVERVIEW: Appellant taxpayer sought review of a decision of the tax court which held that respondent Director of Taxation could not allocate appellant's income, because he did not have a regular place of business outside of the state. The court affirmed the order that found that appellant did not have a regular place of business outside of the state as defined in N.J. Stat. Ann. § 54:10A-6. The court reasoned that appellant's only contact outside of the state was a property that it leased and that appellant had no employee's out side of the state. The court reversed the order that found that respondent could not allocate appellant taxpayer's income if he did not have a regular place of business out of the state. The court reasoned that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 54:10A-8 permitted respondent to allocate appellant's income if he believed it would more properly reflect appellant's activities.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that found that respondent Director, Division of Taxation could not allocate appellant taxpayer's income if he did not have a regular place of business out of the state, holding that respondent was authorized to allocate income to properly reflect appellant activities.

 

1258 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Women's Medical Center v. Finley


A-5269-81T3, A-5328-81T3, A-5329-81T3


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


192 N.J. Super. 44; 469 A.2d 65; 1983 N.J. Super. LEXIS 976


September 13, 1983, Argued  
November 17, 1983, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certification denied by Women's Medical Center at Howell v. Finley, 96 N.J. 279, 475 A.2d 578, 1984 N.J. LEXIS 2506 (1984)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Final Decision of the State Department of Health.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, health management corporations, challenged decisions of the Commissioner of Health (New Jersey), which found that physician practice groups working for appellants were subject to the Health Care Facilities Planning Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 26:2H-1 et seq.


OVERVIEW: An administrative law judge's initial decision was overridden by appellee health commissioner's conclusion that contracts between appellants, health management corporations, and physician practice groups altered the essential private-practice character of the physician groups, making them subject to agency and regulatory control under The New Jersey Health Care Facilities Planning Act (Act), N.J. Stat. Ann. § 26:2H-1 et seq. In a consolidated appeal, the court reversed, holding that, while appellants were health care facilities regulated by the Act, the business services appellants' provided to the physicians did not impinge upon the ordinary patient-private physician relationship or professional control by the physicians. Thus, the physicians' work in appellants' facilities was considered to be private practice, which exempted them from regulation under the Act.


OUTCOME: The court reversed judgment of appellee health commissioner concerning contracts between appellants, health management corporations, and physician practice groups, because appellee health commissioner's statutory interpretation was not supported by the plain language of the pertinent statute; thus, private medical practices were not within the regulatory scope of the agency or the statute.

 

1259 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. One 1979 Pontiac Sunbird


A-2800-82T3


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


191 N.J. Super. 578; 468 A.2d 715; 1983 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1008


October 12, 1983, Argued  
November 14, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Superior Court, Law Division, Somerset County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order for summary judgment from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Somerset County, which extinguished his interest in, and ordered the forfeiture of, his automobile in a forfeiture proceeding under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:64-3.


OVERVIEW: Defendant alleged his car, which was used by his son in three robberies, was not subject to forfeiture. On appeal, the court held forfeitures could be justified only if the owner could have prevented the abuse for which the forfeiture proceeding was begun. The court reversed the forfeiture and remanded for a plenary hearing because the record did not show defendant's property was used to further an unlawful purpose. Although the 1981 amendments to the forfeiture statute excised the exemption from forfeiture for an owner of property who had not consented and was not privy to the unlawful use of this property, the court inferred the legislature did not intend forfeiture to be applied inflexibly in all cases. Forfeitures could be justified only where it was within the owner's power to prevent the abuse for which the forfeiture proceeding was begun. It was difficult to reject an owner's constitutional claim when his property was taken from him without his privity or consent or when he proved, not only that he was uninvolved in and unaware of the wrongful activity, but also that he had done all that reasonably could be expected to prevent the proscribed use of his property.


OUTCOME: The order was reversed and remanded because defendant whose property was taken without privity or consent, who proved he was uninvolved in and unaware of wrongful activity, or who did all he reasonably was expected to prevent proscribed use of his property, was not subject to forfeiture of property.

 

1260 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. McCormack Terminal, Inc.


A-4201-81T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


191 N.J. Super. 48; 465 A.2d 545; 1983 N.J. Super. LEXIS 945


June 7, 1983, Argued  
August 29, 1983, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certification denied by State v. McCormack Terminal, Inc., 95 N.J. 198, 470 A.2d 420, 1983 N.J. LEXIS 3344 (1983)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Middlesex County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant terminal company appealed its conviction and $ 500 fine from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Middlesex County for violation of South Amboy, N.J., Ordinance 892 by polluting the air. Defendant contended that the ordinance definition was unconstitutionally vague and that the minimum fine provision was contrary to a municipality's limited statutory authority to adopt penal ordinances.


OVERVIEW: Defendant terminal company's conviction and $ 500 fine in violation of South Amboy's Air Pollution Control Code was affirmed on the grounds that under the ordinance's severability clause the unlawful minimum fine provision was severable, the remainder of the penalty clause was operable and conformed to statutory authority, and the definition of air pollution had earlier been deemed a sufficient standard. Defendant transferred coal from a railroad coal car to an open yard area without enclosing its conveyor and generated dust clouds that settled on the neighborhood. Defendant was fined the maximum amount under South Amboy, N.J., Ordinance 892 but contested that the ordinance definition of air pollution was unconstitutionally vague and that the ordinance's $ 5 minimum fine provision was contrary to a municipality's limited statutory authority to adopt penal ordinances. The court affirmed the conviction, found that the pollution definition was sufficiently defined, and found that there was a rebuttable presumption of severability when an ordinance contained a severability clause.


OUTCOME: Defendant terminal company's conviction and $ 500 fine for air pollution in violation of South Amboy's Air Pollution Control Code was affirmed on the grounds that under the ordinance's severability clause the unlawful minimum fine provision was severable, the remainder of the penalty clause was operable and conformed to statutory authority, and the definition of air pollution had earlier been deemed a sufficient standard.

 

1261 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Schride Associates v. Wall


A-2081-81T2


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


190 N.J. Super. 589; 464 A.2d 1189; 1983 N.J. Super. LEXIS 921


March 29, 1983, Argued  
August 3, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Superior Court, Law Division, Monmouth County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, comprised of a board of adjustment, township, land use officer, and township committee, challenged the decision of the Superior Court, Monmouth County (New Jersey), which determined that defendant township board of adjustment had authority to grant plaintiff land developer's application for variances to permit a planned unit development even though the township had no ordinance that provided for planned developments.


OVERVIEW: Defendants, comprised of a board of adjustment, township, land use officer, and township committee, sought review of a decision which determined that defendant township board of adjustment had authority to grant plaintiff land developer's application for variances to permit a planned unit development, even though the township had no ordinance that provided for planned developments. The court reversed and held that planned developments were permitted if appropriate standards and authority had been adopted by ordinance. The statutory scheme required that an appropriate ordinance had to be adopted before a planned unit development could be considered a permissible use in a municipality. Permitting boards of adjustment to have granted use variances for a planned unit development without participation of the planning board and without having established criteria by ordinance was completely contrary to the statutory scheme.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the determination that defendant township board of adjustment had authority to grant plaintiff land developer's application for variances to permit a planned unit development even though defendant township had no ordinance that provided for planned developments. It was contrary to the statutory scheme for a board of adjustment to grant use variances for a planned unit development without criteria established by ordinance.

 

1262 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Fasolo v. Board of Trustees


A-5319-81T2


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


190 N.J. Super. 573; 464 A.2d 1180; 1983 N.J. Super. LEXIS 935


June 14, 1983, Submitted  
August 1, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from a Final Determination of the Board of Trustees of Public Employees' Retirement System.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant retiree sought review of an order of respondent Board of Trustees of Public Employees' Retirement System (New Jersey), which denied the payment of pre- and post-judgment interest pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 43:15 A-1 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Appellant retiree was awarded a judgment against respondent Board of Trustees of Public Employees' Retirement System for overpayments. Appellant received a payment and notified respondent that he was entitled to interest. Respondent refused to pay interest and denied appellant a hearing. Respondent contended that there was no provision in N.J. Stat. Ann. § 43:15A-1 et seq. to pay interest on the refund of moneys other than when a member withdrew from the system. On appeal, the court held that appellant should have received interest on his excess contributions from the date of deposit and on his pension arrearages from the date due until the date of final payment. Appellant did not waive his right to interest because there was no point at which he had been required to raise it. In the absence of a statutory provision for interest on an obligation of a governmental entity, a legislative purpose to allow interest was found in the nature of the burden imposed and the relative equities between the beneficiaries. Interest was due because appellant had been required to overpay his contributions, at respondent's direction, and received no benefit from the improper retention of his funds.


OUTCOME: The court ordered respondent Board of Trustees of Public Employees' Retirement System to pay appellant retiree interest on his excess contributions from the date of deposit and on his pension arrearages from the date due until the date of final payment, because appellant had been required to overpay his contributions, at respondent's direction, and received no benefit from the improper retention of his funds.

 

1263 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Eatough v. Board of Medical Examiners


A-1022-82T1


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


191 N.J. Super. 166; 465 A.2d 934; 1983 N.J. Super. LEXIS 947


May 10, 1983, Argued  
August 1, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Board of Medical Examiners.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff doctors of osteopathy challenged the validity of N.J. Stat. Ann. 45:9-16 and N.J. Admin. Code tit. 13, §§ 35-4.1, 35-6.13, which were implemented by the New Jersey Board of Medical Examiners. The provisions contained minimum content requirements for professional commercial advertisements and prohibited false or deceptive advertising. Plaintiffs arguments focused on the distinction between the designations of "M.D." and "D.O."


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff doctors of osteopathy challenged the validity of N.J. Stat. Ann. 45:9-16 and N.J. Admin. Code tit. 13, §§ 35-4.1, 35-6.13, implemented by the New Jersey Board of Medical Examiners (Board). One plaintiff previously brought similar claims, which were rejected. The court ruled that res judicata and collateral estoppel did not bar the remaining plaintiffs' claims. Plaintiffs objected to the designations of "M.D." and "D.O." on licenses and in advertising. The court held that N.J. Stat. Ann. 45:9-16 restricted the Board to issue licenses to practice, but did not authorize a degree designation, and the court found no implied authority allowing the Board to do so. The court concluded that the Board exceeded its statutory powers in designating M.D. and/or D.O. on licenses and in adopting the challenged regulations. The court enjoined the Board from placing the designations on licenses issued in New Jersey. However, the court found no federal or state equal protection violations in the licensing scheme, and that the challenged regulations on commercial speech did not violate U.S. Const. amend. I or N.J. Const. art. I, para. 6.


OUTCOME: The court enjoined the New Jersey Board of Medical Examiners (Board) from designating M.D. or D.O. on licenses issued to practice medicine and surgery in New Jersey. The court held that the degree designation and advertising regulations were invalid as outside the authority given to the Board under the Medical Practices Act. The court found no federal or state equal protection or free expression constitutional violations.

 

1264 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


In re Hackett


A-1611-82T1


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


190 N.J. Super. 300; 463 A.2d 376; 1983 N.J. Super. LEXIS 893


May 16, 1983, Argued  
June 27, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Division of State Police, Department of Law and Public Safety.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant applicant sought review of a decision of the Division of State Police Department of Law and Public safety, (New Jersey), which denied appellant's application for a private detective license because appellant's conviction for kidnapping created a mandatory disqualification of appellant as an applicant for a private detective's license.


OVERVIEW: Appellant applicant was found guilty of kidnapping, which at the time was a high misdemeanor. Appellant's sentence to several years in prison was commuted. After his release, appellant was granted a writ of habeas corpus, which was never challenged. Several years later, appellant applied for a private detective license. The state police department denied the license application because appellant's conviction for kidnapping created a regulatory disqualification of appellant as an applicant for a private detective license. Appellant requested an administrative hearing. The administrative law judge concluded that appellant's license denial, solely on the ground that his disqualifying conviction for a high misdemeanor was still of record, was appropriate. The court reversed, holding that the reliability of the facts supporting appellant's conviction for kidnapping was inherently suspect and that his unchallenged habeas corpus nullified his state criminal conviction. The court remanded the matter to the state police department for reconsideration of appellant's application for a private detective license as if the record of the kidnapping conviction never existed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the decision of the state police department which denied appellant applicant's application for a private detective license because appellant's unchallenged habeas corpus motion nullified his state criminal conviction for kidnapping. The court held that appellant's conviction for kidnapping was inherently suspect.

State v. McCandless


A-4621-80-T4, A-4489-80-T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


190 N.J. Super. 75; 461 A.2d 1205; 1983 N.J. Super. LEXIS 881


June 1, 1983 (McCandless), Argued; June 1, 1983 (Hartey), Submitted  
June 16, 1983, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certification denied by State v. McCandless, 95 N.J. 210, 470 A.2d 428, 1983 N.J. LEXIS 3394 (1983)
Habeas corpus proceeding at McCandless v. Beyer, 835 F.2d 58, 1987 U.S. App. LEXIS 15909 (3d Cir. N.J., 1987)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court, Law Division, Atlantic County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, who were tried together by a jury, challenged a judgment of the Superior Court, Atlantic County (New Jersey), which convicted them of three counts of possession of a stolen credit card and one count of unlawful possession of an automatic pistol in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:39-5b.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were each convicted of three counts of possession of a stolen credit card and one count of unlawful possession of a so-called B.B. automatic pistol in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:39-5b. Defendants challenged the convictions, arguing that § 2C:39-5b and N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:39-2b, taken together, impermissibly relieved the state of its obligation to prove each element of the offense beyond a reasonable doubt. Under § 2C:39-2b, where the legality of a person's conduct depended on the possession of a license or a permit, it was presumed that he did not possess such a license or permit until he established the contrary. On appeal, the court affirmed the convictions. The court concluded that the statutory presumption was constitutional because it met the rational connection criterion and because it was not accorded mandatory effect. The court found that defendants, who were apprehended in possession of a weapon, would of necessity have been in the best position to offer proof of compliance with the license or permit requirements. The court also found that the trial court charged the jury in a constitutionally acceptable manner with regard to the presumption.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions for possession of a stolen credit card and unlawful possession of an automatic pistol. The court held that a statutory provision that created a presumption that defendants did not possess a license or a permit until they established the contrary was not unconstitutional. The court also held that the application of the presumption by the trial judge was constitutionally acceptable.

Karcher v. Kean


A-5581-81-T1


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


190 N.J. Super. 197; 462 A.2d 1273; 1983 N.J. Super. LEXIS 888


February 8, 1983, Argued  
May 11, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Final Decision of the Governor of the State of New Jersey deleting certain language from Senate Bill No. 1600.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the speaker of the general assembly and the president of the senate, sought review of a final decision of respondent governor, who exercised his line-item veto power and deleted certain language from a bill that had been passed by both houses of the legislature and presented to him for review and signature.


OVERVIEW: Both houses of the state legislature passed an annual appropriations bill and presented it to respondent governor for review and signature. Respondent objected to several items and used his line-item veto power to delete them. The legislature did not attempt to override respondent's veto. Appellants, the speaker of the general assembly and the president of the senate, filed an action seeking a declaration that respondent had exceeded his constitutional authority in his use of the line-item veto. The court held that respondent's use of the line-item veto to delete certain items that were not items of appropriation of money violated N.J. Const. (1947) art. V, § 1, para. 15. The court ruled that the failure of the legislature to attempt to override respondent's veto did not validate his improper use of the line-item veto power, but struck down those portions of the new law that it held unconstitutional. The court held that respondent's deletion of items related to public utilities franchise and gross receipts tax revenues was a proper use of the line-item veto because those were items of appropriation.


OUTCOME: The court held that respondent governor's exercise of the line-item veto power with respect to some of the deleted items was unconstitutional because those items were not items of appropriation of money, but upheld his exercise of the line-item veto power with respect to items of appropriation.

State v. T.P.M.


A-3337-81T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


189 N.J. Super. 360; 460 A.2d 167; 1983 N.J. Super. LEXIS 853


March 7, 1983, Argued  
March 29, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Monmouth County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the decision of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Monmouth County (New Jersey), which found that he was not entitled to expungement of the record of his conviction for drug offenses.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had previously pled guilty to two drug offenses in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 24:21-19. He later sought expungement of the criminal record, which could have prevented his licensing as a real estate agent. He sought expungement under the predecessor statute to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:52-25, claiming that the new statute did not apply to him based on the ex post facto doctrine. The prior statute permitted expungement as of right to youthful offenders, while the new statute no longer did so. The trial court held that § 2C:52-25 was retroactive and applicable to defendant. On appeal, the court affirmed. The trial court properly rejected defendant's federal constitutional challenge based on ex post facto and due process principles. Any injury allegedly sustained by defendant in being unable to obtain a real estate license was speculative and indirect. The expungement statute was remedial, not punitive. Expungement was only a potential remedy, not a right that inured to defendant's benefit. Defendant's criminal record was not part of the sentence and punishment. Thus, he had no constitutionally protected right to assume that the legislative remedy of expungement was immutable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed denial of defendant's right to expungement of his criminal record. The rejection of that right based on a new, stricter statute did not violate defendant's constitutional rights, as it was not an ex post facto law, and defendant had no constitutional right to expungement.

Taylor v. Board of Education


A-1385-81T2


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


187 N.J. Super. 546; 455 A.2d 552; 1983 N.J. Super. LEXIS 760


November 15, 1982, Submitted  
January 18, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Hudson County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Hudson County (New Jersey), finding that his dismissal by respondent board of education was governed by N.J. Disciplinary R. 2-110(B)(4) and that he was not entitled to veteran's tenure under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 38:16-1.


OVERVIEW: Appellant attorney brought a complaint against respondent board of education based on his dismissal as counsel without a fair and impartial hearing demonstrating good cause. The trial court found that the tenure provisions of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 38:16-1 were inapplicable and that, under N.J. Disciplinary R. 2-110(B)(4), appellant was required to withdraw from his position as attorney when his client no longer wanted him as its counsel. Appellant sought review, and the court affirmed, finding that § 38:16-1 and R. 2-110(B)(4) were in direct conflict. The court found that the general legislative grant of tenure of § 38:16-1 must give way to R. 2-110(B)(4), which was enacted by the N.J. Supreme Court under its exclusive constitutional responsibility for regulation of the practice of law pursuant to N.J. Const. art. VI, § II, para. 3 (1947). The court found that appellant failed to sustain his burden that a separate administrative employment or position was created for which he received a separate salary that would bring his claim under § 38:16-1.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, finding that appellant attorney was not entitled to veteran's tenure because as an attorney, appellant was required to withdraw from his position when his client, respondent board of education, no longer wished him to serve as its counsel.

State v. Lee


A-5263-80T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


188 N.J. Super. 432; 457 A.2d 1184; 1982 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1023


November 9, 1982, Submitted  
December 16, 1982, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certification granted by State v. Lee, 94 N.J. 592, 468 A.2d 228, 1983 N.J. LEXIS 3117 (1983)
Modified by State v. Lee, 96 N.J. 156, 475 A.2d 31, 1984 N.J. LEXIS 2420 (1984)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Superior Court, Law Division, Bergen County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction by the Superior Court (New Jersey), of burglary and possession of a weapon under circumstances manifestly inappropriate for lawful use.


OVERVIEW: The victim, an off-duty police officer, discovered defendant breaking into the victim's home through the kitchen window. The victim chased defendant, but defendant escaped, and the victim telephoned police. Defendant was caught, and identified by the victim. While arresting defendant, police discovered the defendant had a pair of scissors taped together to use as a stiletto. Defendant was charged, tried, and convicted of burglary, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:18-2(a)(1), and possession of a weapon under circumstances manifestly inappropriate for lawful use, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:39-5(d). Defendant sought review of his conviction. The court affirmed and held that the trial court properly charged the jury concerning the elements necessary for a conviction under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:39-5(d), that it was not necessary to instruct the jury that defendant possessed the scissors with the purpose, intent or knowledge to use it as a weapon if the crime was properly defined, that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:39-5(d) was not unduly vague, and that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:39-5(d) did not shift the burden of proof to defendant to prove that his possession was not manifestly inappropriate.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed because the jury charge was proper concerning the elements necessary for a conviction of the weapons charge, the trial court did not have to instruct the jury that defendant possessed the scissors with the purpose, intent or knowledge to use it as a weapon, the weapons statute was not unduly vague, and the weapons charge did not shift the burden of proof to defendant.

State v. Chapman


A-3471-80 T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


187 N.J. Super. 474; 455 A.2d 514; 1982 N.J. Super. LEXIS 998


November 23, 1982, Submitted  
December 10, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Bergen County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Bergen County, New Jersey, which convicted him of possession of heroin with intent to distribute, possession of heroin and cocaine, and possession in an automobile of a .22-caliber pistol without first having obtained the requisite permit. The trial court sentenced defendant to $ 25 as a mandatory penalty under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:43-3.1(a)(2).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of possession of heroin with intent to distribute, possession of heroin and cocaine, and possession in an automobile of a .22-caliber pistol without first having obtained the requisite permit. Defendant sought review of the judgment and challenged the imposition of the mandatory fines of $ 25 pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:43-3.1a(2). The court held that it was clear from the sentencing transcript that the trial judge felt constrained to impose for each conviction the $ 25 penalty required by § 2C:43-3.1a(2). The court held that the trial judge erred when he imposed the $ 25 penalties. The new code expressly provided that it did not apply to offenses committed prior to its effective date. Because defendant committed the crimes for which he was convicted prior to the effective date, and defendant did not voluntarily consent to be sentenced under the new code pursuant to the provisions of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:1-1c(2), the trial judge could not impose the mandatory penalties. The penalty was unquestionably barred by the prohibition of ex post facto legislation found in U.S. Const. art. I, § 10, cl. 1, and N.J. Const. art. IV, § VII, par. 3.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and vacated the imposition of the $ 25 mandatory penalties imposed upon defendant, and affirmed as modified. The matter was remanded for entry of an amendatory judgment. Defendant committed the crimes for which he was convicted prior to the effective date of the new code, and the trial court could not impose mandatory penalties of $ 25 as part of the sentence.

State v. Rockholt


A-4814-80T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


186 N.J. Super. 539; 453 A.2d 258; 1982 N.J. Super. LEXIS 939


October 13, 1982, Argued  
November 18, 1982, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certification granted State v. Rockholt, 93 N.J. 273, 460 A.2d 675, 1983 N.J. LEXIS 2498 (1983)
Affirmed by State v. Rockholt, 96 N.J. 570, 476 A.2d 1236, 1984 N.J. LEXIS 2712 (1984)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Atlantic County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Atlantic County, after he was convicted of distributing methamphetamine, receiving a stolen police motorcycle, misconduct in office in connection with the sale of the police motorcycle, and receiving stolen police identification cards. The conviction for receiving the stolen motorcycle was vacated and an aggregate sentence of eight years was imposed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a police officer, was arrested after selling a police motorcycle, police identification cards, and speed to undercover officers. On review of his conviction for distributing methamphetamine, misconduct in office in connection with the sale of a police motorcycle, and receiving stolen police identification cards, defendant argued that he was the victim of entrapment due to his drug and alcohol addiction. The court affirmed defendant's convictions, finding that the defense of subjective entrapment was not of constitutional dimension. Placing the burden of proving entrapment on defendant under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:2-12(b), was not improper as long as the state still had to prove every element of the offense charged beyond a reasonable doubt. The change in burden of proof was intended to both objective and subjective entrapment. There was no evidence of egregious conduct by the state to support the defense of objective entrapment. There was no prejudice from a charge on objective entrapment. Defendant's misconduct in office charge was supported by his status as a public servant at the time of the offense. Defendant's sentence was within the trial court's discretion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction, finding that the burden of proof was properly on defendant to prove entrapment, whether subjective or objective. There was no showing of objective entrapment, but defendant was not prejudiced by the instruction on objective entrapment. Aggravating circumstances substantially outweighed mitigating factors in defendant's sentence and there was no abuse of discretion.

Newark Superior Officers Asso. v. Newark


A-5095-80T3


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


187 N.J. Super. 390; 455 A.2d 81; 1982 N.J. Super. LEXIS 980


October 12, 1982, Argued  
November 17, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court, Law Division, Essex County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, city and associated individuals, sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Essex County (New Jersey), which declared that the appointment of police chiefs in unclassified civil service as required by N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40:69A-60.7 was unconstitutional as special legislation.


OVERVIEW: Defendants, city and associated individuals, adopted a Plan C form of government. After the city police chief retired, defendants did not appoint a new chief for several years. During that time, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40:69A-60.7 was enacted which provided that any governing body of any city of the first class which adopted Plan C could provide by ordinance that the mayor appoint a police director and that the director was in the unclassified civil service. Plaintiff deputy police chiefs challenged the statute, and the trial court ruled that it was special legislation enacted in violation of N.J. Const. art. IV, § VII, para. 9(13). On appeal, the court affirmed because there was no rational basis for cities not of the first class, cities which did not adopt the plan, and municipalities other than cities, to be excluded from the class which may adopt the ordinance. The statute's purpose of assuring the police chief's cooperation with the municipal administration was not a reasonable explanation of why the legislation was not equally desirable for other municipalities, thus, the classification did not have a reasonable basis and was unconstitutional special legislation.


OUTCOME: Judgment that statute was special legislation that violated the state constitution was affirmed. There was no reasonable basis for the statute's classification that only cities of the first class that adopted a specific plan of government could enact an ordinance that allowed the mayor to appoint a police director.

OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs were police officers in the employ of defendant town. Plaintiffs brought an action and sought to tack benefits under N.J. Stat. State v. Colon


A-3487-80T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


186 N.J. Super. 355; 452 A.2d 700; 1982 N.J. Super. LEXIS 917
