October 27, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Passaic County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Superior Court of Passaic County, New Jersey, which convicted him of unlawful possession of a weapon in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:39-5 d.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with murder in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:11-3a(1) and unlawful possession of a weapon in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:39-5(d). Defendant was convicted only of unlawful possession of a weapon. Defendant claimed that the verdict was against the weight of the evidence because the jury found that defendant acted in self-defense and that § 2C:39-5(d) was unconstitutionally vague. The court ruled that a lawful use of a weapon did not necessarily legitimate its prior possession and that the proscription contained within § 2C:39-5(d) was against possession, not use. Further, the court held that the issue was not whether a weapon could be lawfully used, but whether the circumstances surrounding the possession were manifestly appropriate for such lawful uses. The court affirmed defendant's conviction and concluded that § 2C:39-5(d) was not unconstitutionally vague because it gave sufficient notice that the conduct charged was criminal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction because the jury's verdict was well supported by the evidence, and the trial court's denial of defendant's motion for a new trial based on the contention the verdict was against the weight of the evidence was not error.

Belmar v. Buckley


A-2638-80-T1


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


187 N.J. Super. 107; 453 A.2d 910; 1982 N.J. Super. LEXIS 974


October 5, 1982, Argued  
October 22, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court, Law Division, Monmouth County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Borough appealed from the reversal by the Superior Court of Monmouth County (New Jersey) of defendant's conviction for violation of a borough ordinance prohibiting indecent exposure, on the ground that the subject matter of the ordinance was preempted by statute.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of a violation of Belmar, N.J., Ordinance 5-1.2 which prohibited indecent exposure. On her appeal, the conviction was reversed, without consideration of the merits, on the ground that the subject matter of the ordinance was preempted by statute. The borough appealed and the court reversed the order reversing the conviction. The court held that the enactment of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:14-4, which prohibited lewd acts, was not intended to preclude a municipality from prohibiting public nudity of a character which did not rise to the level of lewdness as therein defined but which it nevertheless regarded as indecent by prevailing community standards. Municipalities were precluded from exercising their delegated police powers on preemption grounds only if an enactment was intended to exclusively occupy the legislated area, or if the ordinance conflicted with the objectives, policy, or provision of state law, or if the subject matter was one requiring by its nature a uniform state-wide approach, or if the state law was so pervasive or comprehensive that it precluded coexistence of municipal regulation. The ordinance here met none of the tests of preemption.


OUTCOME: The order reversing defendant's conviction for a violation of a borough ordinance prohibiting indecent exposure was reversed because the enactment the lewd acts statute was not intended to preclude a municipality from prohibiting public nudity of a character which did not rise to the level of lewdness as therein defined but which it nevertheless regarded as indecent by prevailing community standards.

Dickinson v. Fund for Support of Free Public Schools


A-5259-81T1


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


187 N.J. Super. 224; 454 A.2d 491; 1982 N.J. Super. LEXIS 934


August 30, 1982, Argued  
October 22, 1982, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certification granted by Dickinson v. Fund for Support of Free Public Schools, 93 N.J. 294, 460 A.2d 691, 1983 N.J. LEXIS 2587 (1983)
Certification granted by Dickinson v. Fund for Support of Free Public Schools, 93 N.J. 294, 460 A.2d 691, 1983 N.J. LEXIS 2588 (1983)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by Dickinson v. Fund for Support of Free Public Schools, 95 N.J. 65, 469 A.2d 1, 1983 N.J. LEXIS 3241 (1983)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court, Law Division, Bergen County, whose opinion is reported at    N.J. Super.    .
Dickinson v. Fund for Support of Free Public Schools, 187 N.J. Super. 320, 454 A.2d 480, 1982 N.J. Super. LEXIS 958 (N.J. Super. Ct., 1982)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant state officials appealed from the decision of the Superior Court of Bergen County (New Jersey) which concluded that an amendment to the New Jersey Constitution regarding the state's claim to tidelands was not valid because the state could not comply with its terms.


OVERVIEW: The Legislature passed an amendment to the New Jersey Constitution, N.J. Const. art. VIII, § V, para. 1 (amendment), which provided that lands which had not been tide-flowed for 40 years were not riparian and state owned unless the state specifically defined and asserted a claim during that time period. With respect to lands that were not tide-flowed for 40 years immediately before the adoption of the amendment, the state was given an additional one-year after the adoption of the amendment to assert its claim. Plaintiff landowners filed suit alleging that the amendment was invalid. The court concluded that the amendment was invalid because the state could not complete its mapping process within the one-year in order to assert its claim to certain lands. Defendant state officers appealed. After review, this court concluded that the amendment was, in all respects, valid and that in order for the state to comply with the amendment, it had to specifically define and assert a claim. The contention that some persons' property would be timely mapped and others would not was without merit. The trial court's judgment was reversed, and the complaint was dismissed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court which concluded that an amendment to the New Jersey Constitution regarding the state's claim to lands which had not been tide-flowed for 40 years was not valid was reversed, and the complaint was dismissed. The amendment was valid, and the state was required to specifically define and assert a claim to the specific property.

State v. Wright


A-3477-80T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


187 N.J. Super. 160; 453 A.2d 1352; 1982 N.J. Super. LEXIS 968


August 30, 1982, Argued  
October 15, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Bergen County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment from the Superior Court of Bergen County, New Jersey, which convicted him of unlawful possession of a weapon.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of unlawful possession of a weapon under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:39-5(d). Defendant appealed and the court reversed and remanded for a new trial. The court held that under § 2C:39-5(d), the state was not required to prove unlawful purpose. The trial judge properly charged the jury and also properly charged that the state had the burden of proving that defendant's possession of the knife was under circumstances not manifestly appropriate for such lawful uses. The court held that § 2C:39-5(d) was neither vague nor overbroad. The judge erred in defining "manifestly" in his charge as "easily understood or recognized." Using it had the effect of lightening the state's burden of proof in a way not intended by the legislature. Given that instruction, the jury could have convicted defendant even though it was not convinced beyond a reasonable doubt that the state had disproved a lawful purpose as long as the jury was convinced beyond a reasonable doubt that a lawful purpose was not easily understood or recognized. The state had to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that the circumstances did not demonstrate that defendant possessed the weapon for any lawful use.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction and remanded for a new trial. The court held that the trial court erred in defining "manifestly" in the applicable statute as "easily understood or recognized" because it had the effect of lightening the state's burden of proof in a way not intended by the legislature.

In re Egg Harbor Associates


A-1999-80T2


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


185 N.J. Super. 507; 449 A.2d 1324; 1982 N.J. Super. LEXIS 854


March 29, 1982, Argued  
June 29, 1982, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certification granted In re Egg Harbor Associates, 91 N.J. 552, 453 A.2d 868, 1982 N.J. LEXIS 2765 (1982)
Affirmed by In re Egg Harbor Associates (Bayshore Centre), 94 N.J. 358, 464 A.2d 1115, 1983 N.J. LEXIS 2740 (1983)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Division of Coastal Resouces, Department of Environmental Protection.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant associates sought review of a decision of the Department of Environmental Protection, Division of Coastal Resources (New Jersey), which imposed "fair share" housing conditions upon a permit issued to appellant under the Coastal Area Facility Review Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 13:19-1 et seq., for a waterfront development including 1530 proposed housing units.


OVERVIEW: The Department of Environmental Protection (DEP) imposed upon appellant associates "fair share" housing conditions upon a permit issued to appellant under Coastal Area Facility Review Act (CAFRA), N.J. Stat. Ann. § 13:19-1 et seq., for a waterfront development, including 1530 proposed housing units. Appellant argued that imposed "fair share" housing condition was beyond the authority delegated to the DEP under CAFRA. The court held that where the DEP had the duty to "promote the public health, safety, and welfare under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 13:19-2, and was subject to the clearly stated public policy that provisions must be made for low and middle income housing, it had the authority to impose upon appellant a "fair share" housing condition to provide a certain percentage of low and moderate income housing in its development. As such, the court found that the DEP could engage in inclusionary zoning, which required low and moderate income housing to be built, where it had the duty to "promote the public health, safety, and welfare. Therefore, the court affirmed the DEP's decision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the Department of Environmental Protection's (DEP) decision imposing "fair share" housing conditions upon a permit issued to appellant associates, holding that where the DEP had the duty, pursuant to statute, to promote the public health, safety, and welfare, it had the authority to impose upon appellant a "fair share" housing condition to provide a certain percentage of low and moderate income housing in its development.

 

1282 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


In re 1977 Rate Appeal of Monmouth Medical Center


A-762-79-T4, A-3189 79-T4, A-815-80-T4, A-1794-79-T4, A-1675-79-T4, A-4639-79-T4, A-1959-79-T4, A-1676-79-T4, A-2004-80-T4, A-1960-79-T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


185 N.J. Super. 20; 447 A.2d 192; 1982 N.J. Super. LEXIS 823


January 11, 1982, Argued  
May 20, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from final decision of the Commissioner of the New Jersey Department of Health.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant hospitals sought review of determinations by the Commissioners of Health and Insurance (New Jersey) that set the per diem rates of reimbursement for services rendered by appellants to subscribers of insurer and Medicaid. Appellants raised individual challenges to the rates set for several years and also raised common objections to the fairness of the rate review process.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the determinations by the Commissioners of Health and Insurance that set the per diem hospital payment rate at which appellant hospitals could be reimbursed by insurer and Medicaid for services rendered to their subscribers. The court rejected the appellants' individual challenges as to various base period challenges and upheld the basic fairness of the rate review process. The court held that the failure of the hearing officers to allow evidence on the reasonableness of the minimum base period challenge, the accuracy of the economic factor, and the validity of the geographic equalization factor was not arbitrary, capricious or a denial of due process. The court held that the carry-over process did not deny appellants the opportunity to establish the reasonableness of the prior year's over-expenditures. The court held that appellants were not entitled to individual hearings on the desirability of economic and geographic equalization factors because that was part of the rulemaking process. Finally, the court held that the failure to provide appellants with a final determination by the end of the budget year did not result in substantial financial hardship.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the rates set by commissioners. The court held that appellants' individual challenges lacked merit and upheld the basic fairness of the rate review process. The court upheld procedures including the failure of the hearing officer to allow evidence on the reasonableness of minimum base period challenges, the carry-over process, the lack of individual hearings during rulemaking process, and the timing of the determinations.

 

1283 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Town Tobacconist v. Kimmelman


A-2991-80T2


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


186 N.J. Super. 449; 453 A.2d 209; 1982 N.J. Super. LEXIS 936


January 18, 1982, Argued  
May 14, 1982, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reargued April 26, 1982.
Certification granted Town Tobacconist v. Kimmelman, 91 N.J. 248, 450 A.2d 566, 1982 N.J. LEXIS 2467 (1982)
Affirmed by Town Tobacconist v. Kimmelman, 94 N.J. 85, 462 A.2d 573, 1983 N.J. LEXIS 2729 (1983)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court, Chancery Division, Middlesex County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney general sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court, Middlesex County (New Jersey), that declared unconstitutional N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 24:21-48, -49 and -50. Those sections make unlawful certain use, possession, distribution, and advertising of drug paraphernalia.


OVERVIEW: Respondent retailers brought suit seeking a declaratory judgment holding that supplements to the New Jersey Controlled Dangerous Substances Act, pertaining to drug paraphernalia, were unconstitutional. The trial court declared N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 24:21-48, -49, and -50 unconstitutional and enjoined appellant attorney general from enforcing them against any retail merchant or distributor. Appellant sought review and asserted that the trial court erred in declaring the statutes unconstitutional. The court agreed and held that because the statutes were carefully tailored to reach only conduct which knowingly facilitated or promoted violations of the criminal law, they did not impinge on any constitutionally protected conduct. The court noted that respondents' right to sell smoking accessories and a purchaser's right to buy and use them were entitled to only minimal due process protection. The court reasoned that regulation of items that had some lawful as well as unlawful uses was not an irrational means of discouraging drug use. The court reversed the judgment and its injunctive provisions and remanded the matter to the trial court for dismissal of the complaint with prejudice.


OUTCOME: The judgment appealed from was reversed and its injunctive provisions vacated; the matter was remanded to the chancery division for the entry of judgment dismissing the complaint with prejudice.

 

1284 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Paterson v. Paterson Police P. B. A. Local # 1


A-3359-80-T3


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


184 N.J. Super. 591; 446 A.2d 1244; 1982 N.J. Super. LEXIS 811


April 20, 1982, Argued  
May 11, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court, Chancery Division, Passaic County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the City of Patterson, appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court, Passaic County (New Jersey), confirming the award of an arbitrator in respect of a grievance filed by defendant police union, claiming entitlement to benefits accorded under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40A:9-5. Plaintiff contended that an intervening court decision holding the statute unconstitutional vitiated the arbitrator's award.


OVERVIEW: Defendant police union filed a grievance claiming benefits under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40A:9-5, which credited the period of a municipal employee's prior employment by a county or other municipality to his current period of employment. The grievance was denied by the Director of Public Safety, and the ensuing arbitration resulted in an award directing plaintiff city to grant the grievants credit for prior service under § 40A:9-5. The trial court confirmed the award, and plaintiff sought review, contending that because of an intervening court decision, § 40A:9-5 was unconstitutional and that the award thus must be vacated. The court affirmed the confirmation of the arbitration award. It held that the arbitrator's incorporation of the statutory rights into the grievants' union contract was not vitiated by the intervening finding of unconstitutionality of the statute. It reasoned that the disputed benefits were intended, to the extent that they were negotiable in the absence of the statute, to be encompassed by the arbitration award, and that any remaining issues as to the scope of the benefits should be resolved through recourse to the Public Employment Relations Commission.


OUTCOME: The court held that the arbitrator's incorporation of the statutory rights into the grievants' contracts was not vitiated by a holding of unconstitutionality of the statute, which occurred after the filing of the grievance but prior to the arbitration hearing, and affirmed the trial court's confirmation of the arbitration award, noting that issues as to the scope of benefits could be resolved by the Public Employment Relations Commission.

 

1285 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Application of Forsythe


A-3650-81-T1


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


185 N.J. Super. 582; 450 A.2d 594; 1982 N.J. Super. LEXIS 866


April 27, 1982, Argued  
April 30, 1982, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, U.S. House of Representatives members, filed an application challenging the constitutionality of 1982 N.J. Laws 1. Petitioners claimed that the process by which that law was passed violated N.J. Const. art. IV, § IV, para. 6, in that the bill enacted proceeded to a third reading without a one day interval and without a three-fourths vote to proceed in this fashion.


OVERVIEW: The New Jersey Senate passed a redistricting bill and forwarded it to the General Assembly. By the time the Senate bill arrived in the General Assembly, an identical bill had received two readings there six days earlier. The Senate bill was read in the General Assembly, and on a motion passed by less than a three-fourths vote, received a second reading. The Senate bill, by motion, was then substituted for the General Assembly bill, and was immediately read a third time, was passed, and was delivered to the governor and signed into law. Petitioners, U.S. House of Representatives members, challenged this procedure. The court held that the procedure did not offend the provision of the N.J. Const. art. IV, § IV, para. 6, that required a one-day interval between the second and third readings of a bill in either house unless three-fourths of the members of the house agreed to dispense with the interval. The court reasoned that because the bills were identical as to their content, if not their number or sponsor, they were but one bill, and the required interval between readings was satisfied.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the application of petitioners, U.S. House of Representatives members. The court held that the procedure employed in the passage of a redistricting bill did not unconstitutionally dispense with the one-day interval between second and third readings of the bill readings, because between the two identical bills that were read to the General Assembly, there was a one day-interval between the readings.

 

1286 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Farr


A-962-80 T4, A-1691-80 T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


183 N.J. Super. 463; 444 A.2d 593; 1982 N.J. Super. LEXIS 718


February 23, 1982, Argued  
March 17, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Middlesex County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: State challenged an order by the Superior Court of New Jersey which imposed a sentence of probation upon defendant for his conviction for the offenses of armed robbery, unlawful possession of a shotgun without first having obtained the requisite firearms purchaser's identification card, and possession of a shotgun with purpose of using unlawfully against another person. Defendant appealed his judgment of conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty by a jury of armed robbery, unlawful possession of a shotgun without first having obtained the requisite firearms purchaser's identification card, and possession of a shotgun with purpose of using unlawfully against another person. The trial court sentenced him to probation with a 90-day period of confinement. The court found that the state's cross-examination of defendant regarding his unemployment and substantial financial obligations was proper because the state's questioning of defendant was in direct response to defendant's testimony that he was employed and had money on the date of the armed robbery. The court dismissed the state's appeal of defendant's sentence because defendant's constitutional guarantee against double punishment barred by the Double Jeopardy Clause would be violated if the appeal resulted in an increase in his sentence. The court held that jeopardy attached when defendant commenced serving his sentences. Furthermore, by the time the state moved for a stay of defendant's sentenced pursuant to N.J. R. Civ. P. r. 2:9-3(d), defendant had already served over a month of his 90-day custodial sentence.


OUTCOME: State's appeal from the sentence imposed on defendant by the trial court was dismissed and defendant's conviction was affirmed because state's cross-examination of defendant regarding his unemployment was proper after he testified as to his employment and constitutional guarantee against double punishment would have been violated if the appeal were to result in the court increasing his sentence.

1288 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State in Interest of H. D.


J-6725


Juvenile and Domestic Relations Court of New Jersey, Somerset County


184 N.J. Super. 499; 446 A.2d 576; 1982 N.J. Super. LEXIS 804



March 5, 1982 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant juvenile was adjudicated as a juvenile delinquent based on a violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C: 33-2(b). Before the court was the juvenile's motion to set aside his adjudication of delinquency on the basis that the complaint failed to set out a violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:33-2(b).


OVERVIEW: Defendant juvenile was adjudicated a delinquent for directing threatening and vulgar language towards a police officer for an extended period of time. Defendant moved to set aside the adjudication on the basis that the complaint failed to set out a violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:33-2(b). Defendant contended the statute was unconstitutional because it could punish as a criminal act spoken words arguably protected by the First Amendment. The court rejected defendant's motion to set aside the adjudication of delinquency. The court determined that the statute extended only to unreasonably loud and offensively coarse or abusive language, and only when the speaker's intent was to offend the hearer or where he recklessly disregarded the likelihood of such offending. Language alone was no longer enough to support a conviction merely because it was vulgar. Therefore, the statute was constitutional because it did not seek to punish the speaker merely for speaking vulgar language. Defendant was in violation of the statute because defendant's prolonged harassment of the officer was a clear indication that the juvenile meant to offend the officer.


OUTCOME: The court denied the juvenile's motion to set aside his adjudication of delinquency.

 

1289 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Callen v. Sherman's, Inc.


A-2136-79T1


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


182 N.J. Super. 438; 442 A.2d 626; 1982 N.J. Super. LEXIS 672


January 5, 1982, Argued  
January 20, 1982, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certification granted by Callen v. Sherman's, Inc., 89 N.J. 443, 446 A.2d 164, 1982 N.J. LEXIS 2101 (1982)
Reversed by Callen v. Sherman's, Inc., 92 N.J. 114, 455 A.2d 1102, 1983 N.J. LEXIS 2339 (1983)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Monmouth County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant commercial tenants challenged a judgment from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Monmouth County, which entered judgment in favor of plaintiff landlords in their action for unpaid rent, and dismissed defendants' counterclaim for damages arising out of a purportedly illegal distraint.


OVERVIEW: Defendant commercial tenants leased commercial premises from plaintiff landlords for the purpose of operating a retail store. After defendants fell two months behind in their rent, plaintiffs instructed a municipal constable to secure the premises. One of the defendants notified a government agency which had a security interest in defendants' property. Plaintiffs gave the keys to the premises to the agency, and it auctioned off all of the goods to satisfy its security interest. Plaintiffs then brought an action against defendants for unpaid rent. Defendants counterclaimed for damages arising out of the allegedly illegal distraint issued by the constable. The trial court entered judgment in favor of plaintiffs and dismissed defendants' complaint. On appeal, the court held that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:33-1 et seq., the statute that permitted plaintiffs to seize defendants' property without any notice and without any prior judicial review, violated due process and was unconstitutional. However, the court also held that plaintiffs were entitled to damages because defendants were liable for the unpaid rent. Judgment was affirmed in part and reversed in part.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment that awarded plaintiff landlords damages was affirmed because the lease authorized plaintiffs to reenter the leased premises. Judgment was reversed and remanded for trial on defendant commercial tenants' counterclaim for illegal distraint because their due process rights were violated.

Enourato v. New Jersey Bldg. Authority


A-1220-81T1


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


182 N.J. Super. 58; 440 A.2d 42; 1981 N.J. Super. LEXIS 759


December 14, 1981, Argued  
December 17, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court, Law Division, Mercer County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer sought review of the order from the Superior Court of New Jersey, which dismissed his complaint that alleged that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 52:18A-78.1 et seq., which established defendant New Jersey Building Authority, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff taxpayer filed a suit alleging that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 52:18A-78.1 et seq. was unconstitutional. The trial court dismissed the complaint and plaintiff appealed. The reviewing court affirmed, holding that the trial court judge did not abuse his discretion in disposing of the matter on an oral motion to dismiss because of the unique circumstances of the case. The court held it had the power to accelerate the appeal and did not abuse its discretion by ordering the acceleration. The court held that the statute did not authorize a violation of the debt clause, N.J. Const. art. VIII, § II, par. 3 (1947), nor violated separation of powers, N.J. Const. art. III (1947).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of plaintiff taxpayer's complaint. The court held that its actions in accelerating the appeal and the trial court's summary dismissal were not abuses of discretion. The challenged statute was constitutional.

Sheeran v. Progressive Life Ins. Co.


A-3780-79T3, A-4181-79T3


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


182 N.J. Super. 237; 440 A.2d 469; 1981 N.J. Super. LEXIS 768


November 16, 1981, Argued  
December 15, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the final decision of the Commissioner of Insurance and from final judgment of the Superior Court, Law Division, Mercer County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurance company sought review of the decision of the Commissioner of Insurance (New Jersey), which held that it engaged in unfair practices under the Unfair Claim Settlement Practices Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 17B:30-2 and ordered restitution. The Superior Court, Mercer County (New Jersey), entered a judgment mandating that appellant comply with that order, refused to stay enforcement of the order, and imposed a penalty.


OVERVIEW: An administrative law judge (ALJ) held that appellant insurance company engaged in unfair practices, in violation of the Unfair Claim Settlement Practices Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 17B:30-2. Respondent Commissioner of Insurance adopted the conclusions of the ALJ except for her determination that he lacked jurisdiction to order payment of claims by way of restitution. Thus, he modified the decision to include restitution. Respondent instituted suit for imposition of statutory penalties for appellant's failure to comply and enjoining further noncompliance with the restitution order. The lower court ordered appellant to comply with the restitution order, refused to stay enforcement of the order pending appeal, and imposed a penalty for previous noncompliance. The court reversed the imposition of the penalty to the right of the department of insurance to institute such further proceedings as it deemed appropriate. The judgment of the lower court was vacated and remanded for further proceedings as the penalty imposed was based upon appellant's failure to comply with respondent's order to make restitution, which was improper. In all other respects, the order was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the lower court, which mandated that appellant insurance company comply with the restitution order, refused to stay enforcement of the order, and imposed a penalty, was vacated and the matter remanded as the penalty, improperly imposed, was based upon appellant's failure to comply with respondent commissioner of insurance's order for restitution. In all other respects, the court affirmed the restitution order.

 

1292 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Finance American Corp.


A-1686-80T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


182 N.J. Super. 33; 440 A.2d 28; 1981 N.J. Super. LEXIS 760


November 2, 1981, Argued  
December 9, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Atlantic County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant creditor sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Atlantic County, which entered a judgment after a trial de novo finding appellant guilty of violating N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:33-4(a) because its agent made harassing telephone calls to one of its debtors while she was at work.


OVERVIEW: Appellant creditor made telephone calls to debtor at a resort where she worked as a cashier supervisor. These calls were made after she informed appellant that she was not permitted to accept such calls. One of appellant's employees directed a racial slur at her as well. That employee also threatened police and casino control commission intervention. The lower court entered a judgment after a trial de novo finding appellant guilty of violating N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:33-4(a) because its agent made harassing telephone calls to one of its debtors while she was at work. The court affirmed the lower court's decision because the lower court judge reasonably could have found that defendant's agent persisted in calling the debtor at her job. Further, the court held that defendant's agent received fair warning of the criminality of his own conduct from N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:33-4(a) and could not have attacked it because the language would not have given similar fair warning with respect to other conduct which might have been within its broad and literal ambit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's decision which entered a judgment after a trial de novo finding appellant creditor guilty of violating a harassment statute because the lower court judge reasonably could have found that appellant's agent persisted in calling the debtor at her job.

 

1293 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Barcheski


A-4876-80-T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


181 N.J. Super. 34; 436 A.2d 550; 1981 N.J. Super. LEXIS 696


October 6, 1981, Submitted  
October 9, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On review of an order of the Superior Court, Law Division, Union County, transferring the cause to this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court reviewed an order of the Superior Court, Law Division, Union County (New Jersey), which transferred the cause to the court. The case involved defendant's contention that N.J. Admin. Code tit. 16:30-3.6 was invalid.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was issued a summons driving in a high occupancy vehicle lane without the minimum three passengers required by N.J. Admin. Code tit. 16:30-3.6. Defendant was then charged with violating N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:4-81. Defendant moved for dismissal pursuant to N.J. Ct. R. 7:4-2(e), contending that N.J. Admin. Code tit. 16:30-3.6 was invalid. The municipal court agreed. On appeal, the Law Division determined the issue was within the exclusive jurisdiction of the Appellate Division. The court remanded the action to the Law Division for a de novo trial pursuant to N.J. Ct. R. 3:23. The Law Division erred in concluding it lacked jurisdiction to hear defendant's collateral attack on the validity of N.J. Admin. Code tit. 16:30-3.6. The state supreme court, in its adoption of N.J. Ct. R. 3:10-3, expressly authorized the Law Division to consider, in criminal proceedings, collateral attacks on regulations. The state supreme court also by way of N.J. Ct. R. 3:23 and N.J. Ct. R. 7:4-2(e), which incorporated N.J. Ct. R. 3:10-3, so authorized the Law Division in respect of trials de novo.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case to the Law Division for a de novo trial pursuant to N.J. Ct. R. 3:23. The Law Division erred in concluding that it lacked jurisdiction to entertain defendant's collateral attack in a quasi-criminal proceeding on an administrative regulation. Such authority was expressly authorized.

 

1294 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


In re Estate of Maislin


A-150-80T1


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


181 N.J. Super. 14; 436 A.2d 539; 1981 N.J. Super. LEXIS 702


September 15, 1981, Argued  
October 6, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Superior Court, Law Division, Bergen County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court, Law Division, Bergen County (New Jersey), which held that illegitimate child was entitled to a full intestate share of decedent's estate.


OVERVIEW: Following a trial as part of probate proceedings, the trial court held that illegitimate child, who was adopted by her natural mother's husband, was entitled to a full intestate share of decedent's estate. Appellants sought review of the trial court judgment, arguing that at the time of adoption in 1948 New Jersey law barred an illegitimate child from inheriting from her natural father. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, holding that the trial court correctly applied the law of inheritance as it existed in New Jersey at the time of decedent's death. The court held that that law allowed inheritance by illegitimate children from either the natural mother or natural father. The court further held that the right of inheritance did not conflict with the adoption laws of New Jersey as they existed in 1948, the year of illegitimate child was adopted. The court also held that a mere expectation of property in the future was not considered a vested right, and hence the rules of descent were subject to change in their application to all estates not already passed to the heir by the death of the owner.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that illegitimate child was entitled to a full intestate share of decedent's estate, holding that the trial court correctly applied the inheritance law as it existed in New Jersey at the time of decedent's death.

 

1295 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Worthington v. Fauver


A-4796-80T2


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


180 N.J. Super. 368; 434 A.2d 1134; 1981 N.J. Super. LEXIS 659


August 11, 1981, Argued  
September 4, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Atlantic County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff county executive and sheriff challenged the order of the Superior Court, Law Division, Atlantic County (New Jersey), which upheld defendant governor's executive order giving authority to defendant Commissioner of the Department of Corrections to alleviate inmate overcrowding in state and county correctional facilities as a temporary measure under N.J. Stat. Ann. § A:9-30 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Defendant Governor of New Jersey (governor) issued an executive order, declaring a state of emergency in state and county correctional facilities because of overcrowding. The 90-day order stated that defendant Department of Corrections (department) was unable to accept inmates sentenced to the department and authorized the department to allocate inmates of state and county institutions to those institutions with available space. Plaintiff county executive and sheriff filed a complaint, seeking to compel the department to accept prisoners from plaintiffs' county based on N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:43-10(e) and N.J. Stat. Ann. § 30:4-6. The trial court denied relief. The court affirmed and held that the extensive powers delegated by N.J. Stat. Ann. § A:9-30 gave the governor the means to deal with an emergency until the legislature acted. The court further held that the specific power delegated to utilize and employ all the available resources of each political subdivision of New Jersey to avoid or protect against any emergency clearly gave authority to utilize and employ, temporarily, county correctional facilities, fairly paid for, as needed, without plaintiffs' consent.


OUTCOME: The court upheld defendant governor's executive order, giving authority to defendant Commissioner of the Department of Corrections to alleviate inmate overcrowding in state and county correctional facilities as a temporary measure because the executive order bore a rational relationship to the powers statutorily delegated to the governor. The court dismissed plaintiff county executive and sheriff's complaint and entered judgment for defendants.

 

1296 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State in Interest of B.


5320-88, 5377-80


Juvenile and Domestic Relations Court of New Jersey, Camden County


181 N.J. Super. 586; 439 A.2d 94; 1981 N.J. Super. LEXIS 851; 7 Media L. Rep. 2345



July 31, 1981 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner newspapers filed a motion to open juvenile proceedings over the objection of the juvenile and his parents, and the issue presented concerned the nature and extent of the confidentiality of a juvenile court dispositional proceeding.


OVERVIEW: The juvenile was adjudicated delinquent on his admission of risking widespread injury in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:17-2(c). The incident involved his placing a smoke bomb in a vacant locker in the high school. Upon discovery the school officials evacuated the school and closed it for two days, canceling school activities. The incident received widespread notoriety due to the mistaken information that the device was explosive and lethal. A social investigation was ordered by the court and the matter was listed for dispositional hearing. The newspapers moved to open the dispositional proceedings to the press. That court denied the request and held that fear of publication of intimate details of their lives would inhibit the family's open discussion of their situation. Good cause had been shown that the juvenile's interest in a closed, confidential hearing greatly outweighed any interest of the public in the details of his family life. The best interest of the juvenile would not be served by permitting the press to attend his dispositional hearing. The court would conduct a closed dispositional hearing.


OUTCOME: The court denied the newspapers motion and determined that the dispositional hearing would be closed to the press and public. Further, at the conclusion of the hearing the decision of the court would be released.

In re Application of Boardwalk Regency Corp. for Casino License


A-810-80-T1 and A-951-80-T1


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


180 N.J. Super. 324; 434 A.2d 1111; 1981 N.J. Super. LEXIS 658


January 20, 1981, Argued  
July 21, 1981, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certification granted by In re Application of Boardwalk Regency Corp., 89 N.J. 405, 446 A.2d 139, 1982 N.J. LEXIS 1951 (1982)
Modified by In re Application of Boardwalk Regency Corp. for Casino License, 90 N.J. 361, 447 A.2d 1335, 1982 N.J. LEXIS 2162 (1982)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Casino Control Commission.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant part owners of prospective casino, casino, and related entities challenged the decision of respondent New Jersey Casino Control Commission, which conditioned a plenary license for appellant casino on the divestiture of any interest of appellant part owners that had any capacity for exerting control over the casino or any related entity. Appellants argued that the Casino Control Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. 5:12-89 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Respondent Casino Control Commission (Commission) conditioned appellant casino's plenary casino license on appellant part owners' divestiture of any interest in any capacity for exerting control over appellant casino or any related entity. The commission found that appellant part owners did not qualify under the Casino Control Act (the Act), N.J. Stat. Ann. § 5:12-89 because appellant part owners did not possess the good character, honesty, and integrity demanded by the Act. The commission's determination was founded upon evidence that appellant part owners associated with a purported member of organized crime. Appellant part owners, casino, and related gaming entities challenged the decision. The court affirmed and held that the commission properly weighed the evidence in concluding that appellant part owners did not possess the good character demanded by the Act. However, in affirming, the court excepted that part of the divestiture requirement that applied to non-New Jersey non-gaming subsidiaries of appellant casino and related entities because such requirement did not serve legitimate state interests. The court further held that § 5:12-89 was constitutional.


OUTCOME: Except as to the divestiture requirement as it applied to non-New Jersey non-gaming subsidiaries of appellant casino and related entities, the court affirmed the determination of respondent New Jersey Casino control Commission in conditioning appellant's casino license on the divestiture of any interest of appellant part owners that could exert control over appellant casino or related entities. It remanded for recasting of a consistent order.

 

1298 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Son


A-4218-79T4


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


179 N.J. Super. 549; 432 A.2d 947; 1981 N.J. Super. LEXIS 612


June 8, 1981, Argued  
July 9, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court, Law Division, Ocean County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant truck operator sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court, Law Division, Ocean County (New Jersey), which affirmed the decision of the municipal court, which convicted defendant for operating dump trucks without mud flaps or mud guards, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:3-79.1 (1953).


OVERVIEW: Defendant truck operator was convicted and fined in the municipal court on five charges of operating dump trucks without mud flaps or mud guards, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:3-79.1 (1953). At the time the summonses were issued, the dump trucks were being used to haul gravel along the highway. The superior court affirmed the convictions after de novo review. Defendant appealed, arguing that the statute exempted dump trucks. Plaintiff state argued that the statute only exempted dump trucks that required complete freedom around the wheel for their designed use. The court affirmed, holding that because N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:3-79.2 allowed for imprisonment, it was penal and quasi-criminal, and thus required strict construction; the legislative intent was to exempt from the requirement only those vehicles that needed such exemption for complete freedom around the rear wheels; the absence of a legislative amendment following the opinion of the attorney general giving the same interpretation suggested that such interpretation was correct; and mud flaps would not have interfered with the trucks' hauling of gravel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's judgment which affirmed the judgment of the municipal court which convicted defendant truck operator for operating dump trucks without mud flaps, holding that the clear language of the statute, as well as its interpretation by the attorney general which was not disapproved by the legislature, indicated that only dump trucks requiring complete freedom around the wheel were exempted under the law.

 

1299 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


In re N.J.A.C. 11:5-1.32-Rental Location Operations


A-1384-80


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


179 N.J. Super. 294; 431 A.2d 855; 1981 N.J. Super. LEXIS 604


March 30, 1981, Argued  
June 10, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the New Jersey Real Estate Commission.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant rental location licensees sought review of the validity of an amendment to N.J. Admin Code tit. 11, § 5-1.32 promulgated by respondent New Jersey Real Estate Commission, which restricted prepayment of fees appellants were permitted to charge prospective tenants.


OVERVIEW: Respondent New Jersey Real Estate Commission promulgated an amendment to N.J. Admin Code tit. 11, § 5-1.32 prohibiting rental location operators from charging a fee of more than $ 10 in advance to locate rental units for prospective tenants. Appellant rental location licensees challenged the amendment, contending that it constituted rate-making that was beyond respondent's authority, and that it was arbitrary and confiscatory. The court upheld the amendment as a valid exercise of respondent's rule making authority, designed for the proper legislative purpose of protecting the public from documented improper practices within the real estate industry. The court held that the amendment did not constitute rate-making because it did not restrict the fee that could be charged, only the amount of the fee that could be collected before services were rendered.


OUTCOME: The court upheld the validity of the regulatory amendment promulgated by respondent New Jersey Real Estate Commission. The amendment was not arbitrary or capricious and did not constitute unauthorized rate-making by respondent.

Joint Legislative Committee on Ethical Standards v. Perkins


A-184-79


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


179 N.J. Super. 352; 432 A.2d 116; 1981 N.J. Super. LEXIS 600


January 13, 1981, Argued  
June 5, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Hudson County District Court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant legislator sought review of the decision of the Hudson County District Court (New Jersey) affirming the fine imposed on him by respondent committee. Appellant contended that the statutory prohibition on legislators appearing before state agencies was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant legislator appeared as counsel for a party before a state agency. Respondent committee, acting under the Conflict of Interest Law, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 52:13D-12 et seq., imposed a fine on appellant, who sought review. The trial court affirmed and the court affirmed the trial court. The court held that the prohibition on legislators appearing on behalf of parties before state agencies was a valid measure to avoid impropriety in agency actions and did not unconstitutionally chill the opportunity for attorneys to serve as legislators. The court held that the authority delegated to respondent did not violate the rule in N.J. Const. art. IV § 4, para. 3 that only a house of the legislature could expel a member, because respondent's delegated authority was limited to lesser sanctions than expulsion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision affirming respondent committee's fine against appellant legislator. The statutory prohibition on legislators representing parties before state agencies did not unconstitutionally chill legislative service by attorneys.

 

1301 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Thompson


A-4085-78


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


179 N.J. Super. 27; 430 A.2d 246; 1981 N.J. Super. LEXIS 567


April 7, 1981, Submitted  
April 30, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Passaic County whose opinion is reported at 162 N.J. Super. 302.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant complained of his conviction by the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, for a violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:138-1, carnal abuse. On appeal defendant contended that § 2A:138-1 was unconstitutional because it created an impermissible gender classification, in violation of the Equal Protection Clause of the Federal Constitution.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was 25 years of age at the time of the offense; his victim was an 11-year-old girl. N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:138-1, the carnal abuse statute, provided for punishment by sentence up to 30 years for any person who unlawfully and carnally abused a woman-child under the age of 12 years with or without consent. Defendant contended that the statute violated the Equal Protection Clause because the penal sanction was not similarly extended to females who offended against young males. The point was extensively considered in the trial judge's written opinion in which he ruled against defendant's motion to dismiss the indictment. The statute, though gender differentiating, served a valid legislative purpose through a reasonable classification. Defendant's remaining two contentions, that the trial judge erred in permitting the testimony of two police officers, and that his sentence was manifestly excessive, under N.J. Ct. R. 2:11-3(e)(2), were clearly without merit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1302 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


O'Neill v. State, Dep't of Treasury, Div. of Pensions


A-2175-79


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


178 N.J. Super. 211; 428 A.2d 562; 1981 N.J. Super. LEXIS 517


March 24, 1981, Submitted  
April 7, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the final decision of the Board of Trustees of the Public Employees Retirement System.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner retired employee sought review of a decision from respondent Board of Trustees of the Public Employees Retirement System (New Jersey) (board), which denied retirement benefits because petitioner was receiving retirement benefits from another state. Petitioner contended that the board was estopped from denying his eligibility and contended that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 43:3C-1 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner retired employee began receiving pension benefits upon his retirement under the Public Employees Retirement System (PERS). Respondent board of trustees of PERS then cancelled petitioner's retirement allowance because he was receiving retirement benefits from another state and was ineligible for PERS membership pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 43:3C-1. Respondent affirmed its original decision denying benefits, and the court affirmed respondent's decision. There was an unambiguous statutory declaration that deprived respondent of jurisdictional authority to award pension benefits under the circumstances and the doctrine of equitable estoppel was inapplicable. There was no evidence that any agent, employee, or representative of the Division of Pensions or PERS made representations of any kind to petitioner to induce him to accept the state employment. The court rejected petitioner's attack on the constitutionality of § 43:3C-1 finding no equal protection violation. The different treatment between state and federal employees had a rational basis because federal pensioners were not given credit for pension purposes for time served in out-of-state public employment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision from respondent board of trustees of the Public Employees Retirement System denying retirement benefits to petitioner retired employee. Statute denying benefits to one receiving benefits from another state was unambiguous and was constitutional because it had a rational basis for distinction between state and federal employees.

 

1303 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Carmel v. Hillsdale


A-2743-79


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


178 N.J. Super. 185; 428 A.2d 548; 1981 N.J. Super. LEXIS 514


March 23, 1981, Argued  
April 6, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court, Law Division, Bergen County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff corporation and associated individual appealed a judgment from the Superior Court of Bergen County (New Jersey), which denied plaintiffs' application for an award of counsel fees pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988, following their successful challenge to the validity of an anti-pornography ordinance that had been adopted by defendant borough and associated individuals.


OVERVIEW: The trial court denied plaintiffs' application for an award of counsel fees pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988, following their successful challenge to the validity of an anti-pornography ordinance which had been adopted by defendant borough and associated individuals. Plaintiffs appealed and the court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the case for entry of the court's judgment of a fee allowance. The court found that the ordinance was invalidated by the trial judge on the federal and state grounds asserted by plaintiffs. The court was satisfied that the trial court had the authority to award counsel fees. The court found that there was no special circumstance here presented which would render an award of counsel fees unjust. The court held that where a party prevails on both state and fee-qualifying federal issues, an apportionment may be made in respect of the legal services involved in each and an award allowed pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 for the services attributable to the federal issue. The court held that under the totality of the circumstances, the trial judge mistakenly exercised his discretion in declining to make an award of counsel fees to plaintiffs.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court that had denied plaintiff corporation and associated individual an award of counsel fees following their successful challenge to the validity of an anti-pornography ordinance. The court elected to exercise its original jurisdiction in fixing a fee allowance and remanded for entry of its judgment because the trial judge had mistakenly exercised his discretion in not awarding counsel fees.

 

1304 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Dolce


A-3793-78


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


178 N.J. Super. 275; 428 A.2d 947; 1981 N.J. Super. LEXIS 512


October 21, 1980, Argued  
April 3, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Monmouth County, whose opinion is reported at 165 N.J. Super. 488.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his convictions from the Superior Court, Monmouth County (New Jersey) for possessing a hypodermic syringe and prescription legend drugs, which were not controlled dangerous substances.


OVERVIEW: A horse trained by defendant tested positive to the presence of a drug. A track steward requested the state police to search defendant's stable area for drugs pursuant to N. J. Admin. Code tit.13, § 14.21(a)(2). Defendant offered to take the officers to his stables in his pick-up truck. Defendant opened the truck's glove compartment and the officers saw a syringe. The officers then arrested defendant, searched the truck, and found drugs. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's convictions for possessing a hypodermic syringe and prescription legend drugs. The court held that the search was a valid warrantless administrative search. The court held that the Racing Commission had the power to authorize warrantless administrative searches. The court held that tit.13, § 14.21(a)(2) was constitutional because horse racing was subject to pervasive and long-standing regulation by the state. The court held that even if the search was not a valid warrantless administrative search, the syringe was in plain view, the search of the truck was incidental to the lawful arrest of defendant, and the search of the truck was a valid warrantless search of a vehicle.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for possession of a hypodermic syringe and prescription legend drugs because the syringe and the drugs were found pursuant to a valid warrantless administrative search. The syringe was in plain view, the search of defendant's truck was incidental to a lawful arrest, and the search of the truck was a valid warrantless search of a vehicle.

 

1305 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


In re Kaplan


A-2572-79


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


178 N.J. Super. 487; 429 A.2d 590; 1981 N.J. Super. LEXIS 541


March 3, 1981, Argued  
March 19, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from final determination of Division of Medical Assistance and Health Services, Department of Human Services.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant physician challenged a decision of the Division of Medical Assistance and Health Services, Department of Human Services (New Jersey), which ordered payment of a civil penalty pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 30:4D-17(c) and allowed payment of certain claims submitted by appellant, arguing that § 30:4D-17(c) was inapplicable to him and that he was entitled to payment for all claims submitted, interest on the reimbursement, and counsel fees.


OVERVIEW: Appellant physician sought review of an administrative determination that assessed a civil penalty as provided in N.J. Stat. Ann. § 30:4D-17(c) (1976) and ordered appellee division of medical assistance and health services to pay certain claims submitted by appellant. The court affirmed the part of appellee's order requiring payment to appellant for unpaid claims without interest or counsel fees, and reversed the part of the order requiring appellant to pay the monetary penalty assessed pursuant to § 30:4D-17(c), directing appellant to pay the amount of overpayment made to him. The court rejected appellant's ex post facto argument, holding that the retroactive application of § 30:4D-17(c) did not violate U.S. Const. art. I, § 10 or N.J. Const. art. IV, § 7, par. 3. The court found that the retroactive application of civil penalties violated notions of fundamental fairness, and was an abuse of agency discretion. The court determined that appellant was not entitled to payment of claims submitted after the date of enactment of regulations prohibiting a suspended provider from submitting claims for payment, and that appellant was not entitled to interest or attorney's fees.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part a decision ordering appellant physician to pay a civil penalty and appellee division of medical assistance and health services to pay certain claims submitted by physician, finding that it was an abuse of discretion to retroactively apply civil penalties and that appellant was not entitled to payment of claims submitted after the date the regulation prohibiting payment to suspended providers.

 

1306 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Brodie v. State Bd. of Medical Examiners


A-5080-79


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


177 N.J. Super. 523; 427 A.2d 104; 1981 N.J. Super. LEXIS 471


November 10, 1980, Argued  
February 27, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from a rule promulgated by the State Board of Medical Examiners.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant radiologists challenged the validity of a rule promulgated by respondent State Board of Medical Examiners of the State of New Jersey requiring appellant to provide diagnostic radiological services to licensed chiropractors, upon request, without discrimination on the basis of classification of license, providing that the services requested pertained to skeletal areas of the body.


OVERVIEW: Appellant radiologist provided diagnostic radiological services to licensed physicians but declined to provide these same services to licensed physicians in the chiropractic area. In response to appellant's denial of services in this area, respondent state board of medical examiners promulgated a rule which required appellant to provide the services without discrimination on the basis of classification of license, and the denial of such services constituted intentional discrimination subjecting appellant to disciplinary action by respondent. Appellant sought to stay the effectiveness of the rule pending appeal, which the court denied. The court held that respondent's rule was subject to a rebuttable presumption of validity and that appellant did not carry its burden of proving that the rule was unreasonable. The court held that respondent had broad statutory authority to regulate the practices of medicine, surgery, and chiropractic and the standards of conduct within each and that a trial-type hearing was not statutorily mandated for the adoption of respondent's "rule" as that term was defined in N.J. Admin. Code tit. 13, § 35-6.18.


OUTCOME: A rule promulgated by respondent state board of medical examiners subjecting appellant radiologists to disciplinary action for discriminating against licensed chiropractors in refusing to render their services was deemed valid on the grounds that respondent had broad statutory authority to regulate the area of medicine and that appellant did not carry its burden under a rebuttable presumption of the rule's validity.

 

1307 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


In re Department of Environmental Protection, Div. of Water Resources


A 3681-78


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


177 N.J. Super. 304; 426 A.2d 534; 1981 N.J. Super. LEXIS 458; 15 ERC (BNA) 1751


October 7, 1980, Argued  
February 9, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Department of Environmental Protection.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant chemical company sought review of a decision of the New Jersey Department of Environmental Protection, which imposed certain conditions on appellant's approved permit to construct and operate an industrial wastewater treatment facility.


OVERVIEW: Appellant chemical company filed a permit application with the New Jersey Department of Environmental Protection (DEP) for the construction of a proposed facility that would treat industrial wastewater. The DEP approved appellant's application, but required appellant to have a licensed operator run the plant and the DEP had the right of entry for the purposes of inspection. Appellant challenged the conditions imposed. Upon review, the court affirmed. The court held that the pervasive government regulation exception to the warrant requirement applied because the activity proposed by appellant was integrally related to the issue of water pollution and conservation resources, which was an activity that was extensively regulated. The court reasoned that appellant's participation in the activity resulted in submission to the inspections and that the inspections were reasonably necessary to the enforcement of water pollution regulations. The court found that the permit provision requiring the facility to have a licensed operator was authorized under the Water Pollution Control Act, N. J. Stat. Ann. § 58:10A-1 et seq, where DEP determined an operator was necessary to prevent pollution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a decision that imposed certain condition's on appellant chemical company's approved permit to construct and operate an industrial wastewater treatment facility. The court held that a permit condition allowing administrative agency the right of entry for inspection was constitutional where appellant's activity was integrally related to the issue of water pollution, which was an activity that was pervasively regulated.

 

1308 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rogers


A-4647-78


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


177 N.J. Super. 365; 426 A.2d 1035; 1981 N.J. Super. LEXIS 459


January 6, 1981, Argued  
February 4, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Bergen County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Bergen County, which convicted appellant for armed robbery and illegal possession of revolvers, appellant claimed denial of his U.S. Const. amend. VI and N.J. Const. art. I, § 10 rights of effective assistance of counsel in a criminal proceeding.


OVERVIEW: Appellant and his co-indictees were indicted for armed robbery and illegal possession of revolvers. A hearing was held at appellant's request and appellant contended for the first time that representation of the three defendants by three public defenders from the same office created an irreconcilable conflict of interest. Before trial began, appellant's counsel sought an adjournment and sought to withdraw because appellant refused to confide in him in preparation of a defense. The case was tried and appellant was found guilty. Appellant sought review and the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court saw no shred of support in the record to support any possible contention that counsel was ineffective. The court determined that the only witness appellant could have called to corroborate his testimony was his alleged employer whom he refused to identify to anyone. The court held that no one but appellant could be blamed for the flaw in the defense. The court found no actual conflict existed, nor was actual prejudice demonstrated. The court determined that each defense counsel was inclined to challenge the state's case with equal vigor.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that convicted appellant for armed robbery and illegal possession of revolvers. The court concluded that joint or dual representation of co-defendants by public defenders from the same local office did not constitute a denial or impairment of their constitutional right to counsel.
