In re Application of Mahler


A-4932-79-T3, A-5020-79-T3, A-4983-79-T3, A-5019-79, A-345-80, A-200-80, A-143-80


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


177 N.J. Super. 337; 426 A.2d 1021; 1981 N.J. Super. LEXIS 483


November 17, 1980, Argued  
January 29, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court, Law Division, Bergen County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, corporation and employees, challenged the orders of the Superior Court, Bergen County (New Jersey), which denied their motions to suppress evidence, and declined to issue habeas corpus writs and directed extradition. Pennsylvania had prosecuted appellants, who operated an oil refinery in New Jersey, for illegal dumping into a river in New Jersey that resulted in contamination of the river within the Pennsylvania borders.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, corporation and employees, operated an oil refinery in New Jersey. Appellants were illegally dumping hazardous wastes near a river in New Jersey, which resulted in contamination of the river downstream in Pennsylvania. Pennsylvania prosecuted and seized documents from appellants pursuant to a warrant issued in New Jersey. The trial court denied appellants' motion to suppress, and directed appellants be extradited upon denial of their habeas corpus writs. The court affirmed on appeal. The court concluded that Pennsylvania had jurisdiction to determine the applicability of the exclusionary rule, U.S. Const. amend. IV, and the New Jersey trial court lacked justiciability because there was no actual proceeding in New Jersey. Also, the habeas writs were properly denied because there was no pre-requisite requiring a pre-arrest hearing before the governor used his discretionary power to extradite, and the governor could not be compelled to appear at a habeas corpus hearing to explain his discretionary decision. Appellants were properly charged with violations of Pennsylvania laws, as required by N.J. Stat. Ann. 2A:160-10.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the orders denying appellants', corporation and employees, motion to suppress evidence and writ of habeas corpus. The court concluded that the prosecution for the illegal dumping was in Pennsylvania, and there was no justiciable matter actually before the New Jersey trial court. The court held that a pre-arrest hearing was not a prerequisite to the gubernatorial discretion to extradite appellants.

 

1310 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Student Members of Playcrafters v. Board of Education


A-3954-78


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


177 N.J. Super. 66; 424 A.2d 1192; 1981 N.J. Super. LEXIS 437


December 9, 1980, Submitted  
January 19, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Bergen County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, board of education and education officials, and plaintiff students appealed and cross-appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Bergen County, which held that defendant board of education's school policy which banned extracurricular activities during times of traditional worship was facially constitutional, but as applied, violated U.S. Const. amend. I and N.J. Const. art. I, para. 4.


OVERVIEW: Defendant board of education adopted a policy on school activities that effectively banned most extracurricular scholastic activities during times of traditional religious worship. Plaintiff students commenced an action to enjoin the policy and the lower court ultimately found that the policy was facially constitutional, but as applied, violated the Establishment Clauses of the federal and state constitutions. On appeal and cross-appeal, the court first noted that the challenge was properly in the courts because the exhaustion doctrine did not apply where the challenge was constitutional in nature and the appeal was not moot because the issue was of public importance and bound to recur in the future. The court applied the Lemon test for Establishment Clause challenges and held that defendant's policy met the three-pronged test, and consequently passed constitutional muster. Specifically, the policy had a secular purpose in that it sought to achieve compliance with statutory mandates, did not have a primary effect of advancing religion, and did not create excessive entanglement. Thus, the court affirmed in part, and reversed in part.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part because defendant board's policy did not violate the Establishment Clauses of the federal and state Constitutions, either facially, or as applied. The court applied the traditional three-pronged Establishment Clause test and determined that the policy had a secular purpose, did not advance religion as its primary purpose, and did not create excessive entanglement.

 

1311 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State in Interest of S.Z.


A-3109-79A


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


177 N.J. Super. 32; 424 A.2d 855; 1981 N.J. Super. LEXIS 439


December 16, 1980, Submitted  
January 5, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Juvenile and Domestic Relations Court, Bergen County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of the decision of the Juvenile and Domestic Relations Court, Bergen County (New Jersey), which granted defendants' motions for dismissal of complaints against them for throwing a stone and breaking the front window of complainant's place of business.


OVERVIEW: The state challenged the decision of the juvenile court, which granted defendants' motions for dismissal of complaints against them for throwing a stone and breaking the front window of complainant's place of business. The basis for defendants' motions was that the facts as alleged in the complaints and proved by the state did not constitute a violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C: 17-3 a (1) because the statute required as an element the employment of fire, explosives or other dangerous means. The state contended that these motions were untimely because they were governed by N.J. Ct. R. 3:10-3, which stated that the defense that the indictment failed to charge an offense and the defense that the charge was invalid could not be considered during trial. The court reversed and remanded the cause because Rule 3:10-3 controlled, and the motions should not have been considered at trial. Further, the court held that the trial court erred in limiting the meaning of the statute that a person was guilty if he only employed fire or explosives, and that a retrial of defendants would not violate double jeopardy.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the trial court's dismissal of the complaints against defendants for throwing a rock which broke a window because the motions by defendants should not have been considered at trial. Further, the court held that the trial court erred in limiting the meaning of the statute under which defendants were charged, and that a retrial of defendants would not violate double jeopardy.

 

1312 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State by Division of Weights & Measures in Dep't of Revenue & Finance


A-2621-79


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


177 N.J. Super. 153; 425 A.2d 1074; 1981 N.J. Super. LEXIS 446


December 9, 1980, Argued  
January 2, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Essex County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant manufacturer, sought review of the decision of the Superior Court, Essex County (New Jersey), which convicted him on a charge that defendant offered toy soldiers for sale in package form with the represented net quantity statement on the label not correctly marked contrary to N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 51:1-61 to 1-89, N. J. Admin. Code tit. 13:47D § 4.6.


OVERVIEW: Defendant manufacturre, a New York corporation, appealed from its conviction on a complaint charging that it offered toy soldiers for sale in package form with the represented net quantity statement on the label not correctly marked contrary to N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 51:1-61 to 1-89, N.J. Admin. Code tit. 13:47D § 4.6. Defendant contended that the toy soldiers offered for sale did not comprise a consumer package to which the statutes and the regulation applied. It further contended that the Federal Fair Packaging and Labeling Act preempted the area of legislation and that being a manufacturer located in New York, it committed no offense in New Jersey. The court reversed the conviction and held that a package of toy soldiers did not fall within the regulation defining a consumer package. The consumable or readily depletable items specifically referred to the statutes, such as various foods, coal, ice and liquid fuels, and the phrase "consumption by individuals", in the regulation were limited to items of that nature.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for offering toy soldiers for sale in package form with the represented net quantity statement on the label not correctly marked, because the container of toys was not a consumer package and its contents were not consumable or readily depletable items specifically referred to in the statute or its regulations, such as food, coal, ice and fuel.

 

1313 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


In re Board of Education


A-1430-79


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


176 N.J. Super. 553; 424 A.2d 435; 1980 N.J. Super. LEXIS 755


November 12, 1980, Argued  
December 23, 1980, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certification granted In re Board of Education, 87 N.J. 332, 434 A.2d 81, 1981 N.J. LEXIS 2126 (1981)
Affirmed by In re Board of Education, 86 N.J. 327, 431 A.2d 808, 1981 N.J. LEXIS 1639 (1981)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the New Jersey State Board of Education.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant board of education sought review of an administrative order entered by respondent State Board of Education, which directed appellant to implement a plan for corrective action to address deficiencies in its district's school system.


OVERVIEW: Respondent State Board of Education issued an administrative order that required appellant board of education to implement a plan for corrective action to remedy educational deficiencies in the school system. On appeal, the court affirmed the order and found that the corrective plan complied with the constitutional mandate that the students of the district receive a thorough and efficient education. The court noted that the plan was imposed under the authority of N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 18A:7A-14, 15, which provided respondent with broad authority to issue administrative orders where it determined that a school district was not providing a proper education. The court found that sufficient judicial, executive, and legislative controls existed to ensure that respondent did not abuse the power delegated to it. The court concluded that respondent had authority to assign a monitor general to supervise appellant, and to require appellant to assume the cost of the services of the monitor general. The court rejected appellant's claim that it was denied due process because its case was investigated, prosecuted, and adjudicated by respondent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the administrative order issued by respondent State Board of Education because the corrective plan set forth in the order was not unconstitutional and properly required appellant board of education to address deficiencies in its school system. The court found that respondent was granted broad authority to issue such orders in cases where it determined that a school district was not providing a thorough and efficient education.

 

1314 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Makowitz v. State, Dep't of Civil Service


A-282-79


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


177 N.J. Super. 61; 424 A.2d 1190; 1980 N.J. Super. LEXIS 745


December 2, 1980, Argued  
December 22, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Department of Civil Service.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant police officers sought review of a decision from respondent New Jersey Department of Civil Service which declared them ineligible to sit for a promotional examination because they had not completed five years of continuous service with respondent township's police force prior to the cut-off date for the exam.


OVERVIEW: Appellant police officers challenged a decision from respondent New Jersey Department of Civil Service (commission), which ruled that their years of prior service with another police department could not be tacked on to their service with respondent township in order for them to meet the 5 year continuous service requirement necessary to sit for the promotional exam. On appeal, the court affirmed respondent commission's decision. The court noted that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 11:21-9 stated that seniority rights of officers were based on respective and continuous services. The court found that the commission had long interpreted the "continuous services" referred to in § 11:21-9 as services in the jurisdiction in which the examination was open. The court noted that where the commission's interpretations continued over a period of years without legislative interference, they were given great weight as evidence of the legislature's intent. The court found the argument forwarded by one of appellants that he should be declared eligible to sit for the exam, because he met the continuous service requirement after the cut-off date, but before the exam date, to be without merit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of respondent New Jersey Department of Civil Service (commission), which declared appellant police officers ineligible to sit for respondent township's promotional exam. The court held that the commission's interpretation of continuous service in the particular township assured promotion of employees familiar with local conditions and encouraged the loyalty of employees to their public employers.

 

1315 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Hall v. Mayor & Director of Public Safety


A-815-79


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


176 N.J. Super. 229; 422 A.2d 797; 1980 N.J. Super. LEXIS 705


October 14, 1980, Argued  
November 3, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Camden County, whose opinion is reported at 170 N.J. Super. 307 (1979).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant police officer sought review of an order from the Superior Court, Camden County (New Jersey), which dismissed his complaint in lieu of prerogative writs. Appellant's complaint contested his five-day suspension from duties as a police officer with respondent township's police force for having committed conduct unbecoming an officer and for publicly criticizing the official action of a superior officer.


OVERVIEW: Appellant police officer, in response to a question from a newspaper reporter, stated that certain police officers having large families had applied for food stamps because they could not get along on their salaries. Respondent township suspended appellant for five days as a result of his violation of art. 1, § 10, of the township police department regulations. The court reversed the trial court's dismissal of appellant's complaint challenging the suspension, vacated his suspension, and remanded back to the trial court. The court found that appellant did make statements, which publicly criticized respondent police chief and served to create disharmony in the department and thereby impeded its function. The court noted that if art. I, § 10, was otherwise constitutionally valid, then appellant's speech fell within its reach and was beyond the reach of U.S. Const. amends. I and XIV. However, the court held that art. I, § 10, was not valid because it prohibited all speech that criticized a superior officer, even speech which might have related to matters of public concern and which did not adversely affect the functioning of the department.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, which dismissed appellant police officer's complaint, and vacated the suspension imposed upon him at the departmental hearing and remanded. The court held that respondent township's police department regulation that prohibited all speech that publicly criticized the actions of superior officers was too broad.

In re Loveladies Harbor, Inc.


A-3020-78


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


176 N.J. Super. 69; 422 A.2d 107; 1980 N.J. Super. LEXIS 686


June 9, 1980, Argued  
October 27, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Commissioner of the Department of Environmental Protection, State of New Jersey.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant developers challenged a decision of respondent Department of Environmental Protection, State of New Jersey, which denied two permits for the purpose of filling and dredging 51 acres of land for the development of 108 shore and lagoon front homes.


OVERVIEW: Appellant developers requested a waterfront development permit for 14.8 acres of submerged riparian lands that the state deeded to appellants' predecessors, and a permit to dredge and fill 51 acres. Respondent Department of Environmental Protection denied the permits after a hearing, finding that the application for the development did not meet the statutory or regulatory standards of N.J. Admin. Code. tit. 7, § 7A-1.7. On appeal, the court affirmed the decision, holding that respondent properly denied the wetlands permits because the evidence supported the conclusion that the application for the development did not meet the statutory or regulatory standards. The court rejected appellants' argument that denial of the permits was an unconstitutional taking of property without compensation simply because the most profitable use of the property would have been waterfront development. Respondent suggested a possible alternative plan for development of a portion of the property and that potential use precluded appellants' claim of an unconstitutional taking.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of respondent Department of Environmental Protection, which denied permits for appellant developers' waterfront development, because ample credible evidence supported the decision and the denial was not an unconstitutional taking where there was an alternative use for the property.

Domenick v. Director, Division of Taxation


A-4029-78


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


176 N.J. Super. 121; 422 A.2d 443; 1980 N.J. Super. LEXIS 687


September 16, 1980, Argued  
October 22, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Division of Tax Appeals.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of the final decision of the Division of Tax Appeals (New Jersey), which sustained the denial by respondent director of a claim for partial refund of taxes paid under the New Jersey Gross Income Tax Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. 54A:1-1 et seq. Appellant as a commission-based outside wine and liquor salesman sought to exclude a portion of his business expenses under N.J. Stat. Ann. 54A:5-1(a).


OVERVIEW: Appellant taxpayer sought a refund on the income taxes he paid under the New Jersey Gross Income Tax Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. 54A:1-1 et seq. for the 1976 tax year. He was a commission-based outside wine and liquor salesman who wanted to exclude his business expenses from his gross income. He claimed that because self-employed wine and liquor salesmen could deduct their business expenses under N.J. Stat. Ann. 54A:5-1(b), he should be allowed a similar exclusion under N.J. Stat. Ann. 54A:5-1(a). Respondent director denied his claim for a refund, and the Division of Tax Appeals affirmed the denial. Appellant claimed the denial violated the Equal Protection Clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The court affirmed, holding that the statutory taxation scheme was not unconstitutional, and that there was no requirement under the constitution that all persons be treated in an identical manner. The court found that states were given broad powers to establish their taxation programs, and that differences in treatment would not be subject to attack as long as the differences were justified by an appropriate state interest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed respondent director's denial of appellant taxpayer's claim for a partial refund of his income taxes. The court held that the provisions of the New Jersey Gross Income Tax Act, as applied to appellant, were not unconstitutionally discriminatory.

 

1318 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Radiological Soc. of New Jersey v. Sheeran


A-1148-77


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


175 N.J. Super. 367; 418 A.2d 1300; 1980 N.J. Super. LEXIS 654


April 15, 1980, Argued  
July 17, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Commissioner, Department of Insurance of the State of New Jersey.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs filed a declaratory judgment action recognizing in-hospital radiological services to be within the scope of one insurance coverage, rather than another insurance coverage, and the concomitant right to submit bills directly to subscribers for amounts otherwise not reimbursed by defendant insurer.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs became dissatisfied with the rate of reimbursement for in-patient radiological services they were receiving from defendant insurer via defendant hospitals. Plaintiffs began to bill defendant insurer's subscribers directly for the difference between the reasonable value of their professional services and the amounts paid by defendant insurer. Defendant insurer informed defendant commissioner that plaintiffs were engaging in balance-due billing. Defendant commissioner threatened termination of the defendant hospitals' agreements with defendant insurer if the balance-due billing practice was not stopped. Plaintiff filed a declaratory judgment action that spawned counterclaims and third-party claims. The court held that plaintiffs' in-patient radiological treatments were included in defendant insurer's scope of coverage. Plaintiffs chose to accept reimbursement from defendant insurer via defendant hospitals and that reimbursement constituted payment in full. Acceptance of those payments imposed an obligation on plaintiffs to refrain from balance-due billing. Also, the exclusion of plaintiffs' in-hospital services from certain insurance coverage was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the action taken by Commissioner of the Department of Insurance requesting defendant hospitals to demand that plaintiffs stop billing defendant insurer's subscribers for professional services not otherwise reimbursed, because plaintiffs' acceptance of reimbursement via defendant hospitals constituted full payment for their services.

 

1319 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


In re Toth


A-3245-78


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


175 N.J. Super. 254; 418 A.2d 272; 1980 N.J. Super. LEXIS 644


March 24, 1980, Argued  
July 9, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Superintendent, Division of State Police, Department of Law and Public Safety, State of New Jersey.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant police lieutenant challenged the final decision of the Superintendent, Division of State Police, Department of Law and Public Safety, State of New Jersey, which found him guilty of making an unauthorized copy of a confidential background investigation report on the chairman of the casino control commission and of disseminating the copy to another unauthorized member of the state police.


OVERVIEW: The Superintendent, Division of State Police, found appellant police lieutenant guilty in a disciplinary hearing of making an unauthorized copy of a confidential background investigation report on the chairman of the casino control commission and of disseminating the copy to another police officer. Appellant contended that state police rules relating to handling of the report violated the Right to Know Law. The court held that the report was not a public record within the purview of the Right to Know Law, as N.J. Stat. Ann. § 5:12-52(d), governing appointments to the casino control commission, did not require a written background inquiry of appointees to be made or maintained. The state had implied power to suspend its employees pending disposition of charges. The court held, however, that the hearing officer erred in admitting into evidence the transcribed testimony of another officer that he received a copy of the unauthorized report from appellant, as appellant had no opportunity to cross examine the officer, and the record showed that the finding of guilt was based primarily on the transcript. Accordingly, the matter was reversed and remanded for a new hearing.


OUTCOME: The decision was reversed and remanded for a new trial because the hearing officer impermissibly entered into evidence and considered a police officer's transcribed testimony that he received a copy of the report from appellant; however, appellant was not availed of an opportunity to cross-examine the officer.

 

1320 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Reiman v. Breslin


A-1512-78


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


175 N.J. Super. 353; 418 A.2d 1293; 1980 N.J. Super. LEXIS 653


April 1, 1980, Argued  
July 8, 1980, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certification denied by Reiman v. Breslin, 85 N.J. 147, 425 A.2d 298, 1980 N.J. LEXIS 1795 (1980)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Superior Court, Law Division, Bergen County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, police representatives, sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court, Bergen County (New Jersey), which granted summary judgment to respondent prosecutor in a class action suit challenging respondent's authority to issue on-call subpoenas.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, police representatives, filed a class action suit on behalf of all county officers challenging respondent prosecutor's authority to issue three week on call subpoenas, a procedure which had been developed in response to officers' failure to appear for trial. The trial court granted summary judgment to respondent, and the court affirmed holding that a subpoena issued in New Jersey created a continuing obligation which could not be satisfied until the person was released from it. The court held that respondent was legally obligated to subpoena witnesses in the performance of his duties as a county prosecutor. The court held that notwithstanding the limited scope of the right to travel, the three-week, on-call subpoena was not an unreasonable burden or restriction on the police officers' movement. The court held that the issuance of three-week, on-call subpoenas was a reasonable solution to a problem which obstructed the efficient operation of the criminal justice system. The court held that under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40A:14-135, municipalities were required to compensate their police officers for off-duty hours spent testifying in criminal trials pursuant to a subpoena.


OUTCOME: Grant of summary judgment to respondent prosecutor in class action suit instituted by appellants, police representatives, was affirmed because a New Jersey subpoena created a continuous obligation for the witness to appear until released, respondent had the duty to subpoena witnesses in his prosecution of criminals, and the three week period of the on call subpoena did not unreasonably restrict the officers' right to travel.

 

1321 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Graney


A-1967-79A


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


174 N.J. Super. 455; 416 A.2d 972; 1980 N.J. Super. LEXIS 597


June 3, 1980, Submitted  
June 19, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Ocean County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his sentence in the Superior Court of New Jersey, Ocean County of a mandatory 45-day jail term under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:3-40, as a driver on the revoked list who was involved in an accident resulting in personal injury, and contended that the statute did not apply when the unlicensed driver himself suffered injuries.


OVERVIEW: Defendant suffered personal injuries when the vehicle he was driving left the road and struck a building. He entered a guilty plea to leaving the scene of the accident and driving while on the revoked list and was sentenced to a mandatory 45-day jail term under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:3-40. This statute mandated such a jail term for a driver on the revoked list who was involved in an accident resulting in personal injury. Defendant challenged the sentence and contended that the statute did not apply when the personal injuries were suffered by the violator himself. The court disagreed and affirmed. The primary function of the mandatory jail term was to deter individuals whose licenses were suspended from driving and to ensure the safety of the public on the highways. There was no support for defendant's theory that the legislative concern extended to all members of the public except the violator himself as it required an illogical distortion of the plain language of the statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's 45-day mandatory jail term after he entered a guilty plea to driving while his license was suspended because he was a driver on the revoked list who was involved in an accident resulting in personal injury because the statute applied when the personal injuries were suffered by the violator himself.

 

1322 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Hunterdon Cent. High School Bd. of Education v. Hunterdon Cent. High School Teacher's Asso.


A-4607-78


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


174 N.J. Super. 468; 416 A.2d 980; 1980 N.J. Super. LEXIS 601; 107 L.R.R.M. 2830


May 19, 1980, Argued  
June 19, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Public Employment Relations Commission.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant teachers' association sought arbitration with respondent board of education on the issue of paid religious holidays. Respondent filed a Petition for Scope of Negotiations Determination with the New Jersey Public Employment Relations Commission, which determined that paid religious holidays were unconstitutional, and therefore outside the scope of collective negotiations. Appellant sought review.


OVERVIEW: A teacher's request for a paid leave of absence for religious purposes was denied. Appellant teacher's association filed a claim for arbitration with respondent board of education over the issue. Respondent filed a Petition for Scope of Negotiations Determination with the New Jersey Public Employment Relations Commission. The commission determined that paid religious holidays were unconstitutional under the Establishment Clause, U.S. Const. amend. I, and therefore their consideration was outside the scope of collective negotiations. The commission therefore permanently restrained arbitration of the issue. Appellant sought review, arguing that the commission did not have jurisdiction to consider constitutional issues. The court affirmed the decision, holding that the commission had jurisdiction to consider other laws in determining the scope of collective negotiations under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 34:13A-5.4(d). The court held that paid religious holidays would fail the tripartite test of having a secular purpose, not advancing nor inhibiting religion, and not being an excessive entanglement of government with religion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the Public Employment Relations Commission's decision, holding that the commission had jurisdiction to dispose of the scope issue on a constitutional basis. The court held that paid religious holidays failed the tripartite test of having a secular legislative purpose, a primary effect that neither advances nor inhibits religion, and not fostering an excessive government entanglement with religion.

 

1323 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Davis


A-717-79


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


175 N.J. Super. 130; 417 A.2d 1075; 1980 N.J. Super. LEXIS 628


May 20, 1980, Argued  
June 3, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Superior Court, Law Division, Ocean County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Superior Court of New Jersey, that, upon accepting his plea of non vult for murder, sentenced him to 30 years with 15 years served before parole eligibility pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:11-3b.


OVERVIEW: After defendant's plea of non vult for murder was accepted, he was sentenced to a maximum 30 years imprisonment and the trial court outlined its reason pursuant to N.J. Ct. R. 3:21-4(e). Defendant objected to trial court's assessment that crime was heinous. On appeal, defendant asserted the sentence was manifestly excessive and the trial court's reasons were insufficient because it failed to state findings of mitigating or aggravating factors enumerated in N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:44-1, as required by Rule 3:21-4(e) and § 2C:43-2(d). The court found that the trial court considered such factors although it did not specifically refer to them. Additionally, the court found statements made at sentencing appeared to meet requirements under Rule 3:21-4(e) and § 2C:44-1. The court concluded the trial court acted reasonably in finding aggravating factors outweighed the mitigating factors and the fact certain factors were not especially mitigating did not constitute an abuse of discretion. The issue of credits toward reduction of sentence was improperly presented because that was an issue for parole and sentence was not ex post facto law where he voluntary accepted plea.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment of conviction against defendant, finding that the trial court considered both mitigating and aggravating factors, that the weight of such factors was at the discretion of the trial court, the calculation of credit toward time served was issue for parole board, and the criminal code defendant was sentenced under was not an ex post facto law because he voluntarily accepted plea.

Grieco v. Employees' Retirement System


A-3822-78


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


173 N.J. Super. 474; 414 A.2d 597; 1980 N.J. Super. LEXIS 519


April 29, 1980, Argued  
May 6, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Essex County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Essex County, that entered judgment in favor of respondent employee who was seeking to purchase prior service credit under the pension plan for his previous county employment.


OVERVIEW: The trial court granted respondent employee's writ and ordered appellant city to allow respondent to purchase prior service credit under the pension plan for previous employment respondent had completed with the county. The court reversed the order because it found N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40A:9-5 unconstitutional as applied to pension credit. The court found that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 43:13-22.3 formed the pension system, and all provisions that authorized purchase of credit for prior service required the service to be within the city, not the county. The court found that absent an express provision for the purchase of prior county service, it was unreasonable to infer that such a right existed.


OUTCOME: Judgment that allowed appellant employee to purchase prior service credit under the pension plan based on his previous county employment was reversed. The court found that the applicable statute could not be construed to allow the purchase since there was no express provision authorizing the purchase for prior county service, only prior city service.

Paterson v. Fargo Realty, Inc.


79-3382


DISTRICT COURT OF NEW JERSEY, PASSAIC COUNTY


174 N.J. Super. 178; 415 A.2d 1210; 1980 N.J. Super. LEXIS 828



April 25, 1980 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city demolished a building that had been heavily damaged in a fire and had become a public nuisance. The city brought an action against defendants, current and former owners, to recoup expenses of the demolition. Both sides sought summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: A building was heavily damaged in a fire. Notice was sent to the former owner to repair or tear down the structure. When there was no response the city tore down the structure and filed an action to collect its costs against the owner at the time of the fire and the owner that had purchased the property on the day the notice was sent. Both sides sought summary judgment. The court determined that the defendants were liable to the city for all costs incurred although those costs exceeded the value of the property. The statute under which the city filed its action, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40:48 1.1, was reasonably adopted to assist municipalities in dealing with the financial burden of abating public nuisances and was therefore constitutional. The court also determined that both the former and current owners were liable because they were close corporations and when the former owner received notice the current owner also constructively received notice.


OUTCOME: The court entered judgment in favor of the city and found both the current and former owners of the property liable for the city's full demolition costs.

Board of Education v. Caffiero


A-4739-77, A-829-78


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division

December 4, 1979, Argued

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by Board of Education v. Caffiero, 85 N.J. 133, 425 A.2d 289, 1980 N.J. LEXIS 1742 (1980)
Affirmed by Board of Education v. Caffiero, 86 N.J. 308, 431 A.2d 799, 1981 N.J. LEXIS 1629 (1981)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Middlesex County, whose opinion is reported at 159 N.J. Super. 347 (1978), and from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Union County.
Board of Education v. Caffiero, 159 N.J. Super. 347, 387 A.2d 1263, 1978 N.J. Super. LEXIS 877 (N.J. Super. Ct. Law Div., 1978)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant boards of education sought review of adverse determinations of the Superior Court New Jersey, Middlesex County and Union County, that denied a summary judgment and dismissed a claim, respectively, against respondent parents whose children had vandalized schools. Appellants sought damages under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 18A:37-3, but respondents successfully challenged the constitutionality of the statute.


OVERVIEW: Appellant boards of education had sought recovery of damages in separate actions against parents of pupils who had vandalized schools under the vicarious liability provisions of N.J. Stat. Respondent parents had successfully challenged the constitutionality of that statute as violating due process in separate actions, and leave was granted to consolidate the cases on appeal. The court found the statute constitutional and reversed both orders under review and remanded the cases to the trial courts for further proceedings. The court acknowledged that some jurisdictions found similar statutes unconstitutional, but held that, at least in a civil action, the statute was not unreasonable and did not deprive respondents of property without due process and without equal protection, particularly in light of its presumption in favor of the validity of a legislative act.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the orders under review and remanded to the trial courts for further proceedings. Appellant school boards' statutory claims for damages against respondent parents could proceed because the statute was held to be constitutional in that it didn't deprive respondents of property without due process and equal protection.

Round Valley, Inc. v. Clinton


A-2963-77, A-2964-77


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


173 N.J. Super. 45; 413 A.2d 356; 1980 N.J. Super. LEXIS 487


January 22, 1980, Argued  
March 5, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Hunterdon County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff corporation sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Hunterdon County, invalidating defendant township's land use ordinance as it applied to plaintiff's property. Plaintiff contended that the invalidation, which was only applied to plaintiff's property, was in error.


OVERVIEW: The lower court found defendant township's land use ordinance to be impermissibly exclusionary to the extent that it did not make adequate provision for the municipality's fair share of the least-cost housing needs in its housing region and, after a trial, declared defendant township's land use ordinance unconstitutional as to plaintiff's property and made various other orders implementing the decision. On appeal, the court reversed the decision of the lower court, finding that the lower court had misapplied earlier case law and had erred in granting what amounted to a use variance which would normally have been the function of defendant's zoning board of adjustment. The court held that the lower court's decision that the zoning ordinance was unconstitutional only as applied to plaintiff's property was erroneous.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's decision which declared defendant township's land use ordinances unconstitutional only insofar as they applied to plaintiff corporation's land. It held that the lower court erroneously invalidated the maintenance and performance guarantee provisions of defendant's land use ordinance, and erred in invalidating defendant's 50-acre minimum requirements for planned unit developments.

 

1328 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Kinnelon v. South Gate Associates


A-4057-77 and A-4079-77


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


172 N.J. Super. 216; 411 A.2d 724; 1980 N.J. Super. LEXIS 441


January 28, 1980, Argued  
February 20, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Morris County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant land owner sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court, Morris County (New Jersey), upholding a municipal zoning ordinance that prohibited the use of its land for commercial lumbering or timbering. Appellant contended that the ordinance was preempted by the Farmland Assessment Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 54:4-23.1 et seq., and was invalid.


OVERVIEW: Appellant land owner sought review of a judgment from the trial court prohibiting the use of its land for commercial lumbering or timbering operations. The court affirmed, holding that the zoning ordinance prohibited the use of appellant's lands for commercial lumbering or timbering operations. In addition, the court held that the municipality was authorized to adopt the zoning ordinance pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40:55D-1 et seq. The Farmland Assessment Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 54:4-23.1 et seq, did not preclude municipalities from prohibiting, restricting, or conditioning the use of property for commercial farming or timbering operations where appropriate in light of the considerations legislatively mandated by N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 40:55D-2 and 40:55D-62. The evidence was insufficient to overcome the presumption of the validity and reasonableness of the ordinances.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed and held that the municipal zoning ordinance was not preempted by state legislation. Municipalities were not precluded from prohibiting, restricting, or conditioning the use of property for commercial farming or timbering operations where appropriate in light of considerations legislatively mandated. There was no evidence to overcome the presumption of the validity of the ordinance.

 

1329 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Kenney v. East Brunswick


A-677-78


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


172 N.J. Super. 45; 410 A.2d 713; 1980 N.J. Super. LEXIS 425


October 16, 1979, Argued  
January 21, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Middlesex County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff police officers sought review of an order by the Superior Court of New Jersey which entered a judgment following a nonjury trial in their favor relative to plaintiffs seeking credit for prior service pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. §40A:9-5. Defendant township cross-appealed from these judgments.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff police officers received appointments with defendant township, but had all served as police officers previously. Plaintiffs contended that they were entitled to seniority credit from defendant under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40A:9-5 and its predecessor, N.J. Stat. Ann. §40:11-5, for the years spent in employment of other counties. The court reversed and remanded the cause of action because § 40A:9-5 was unconstitutional. The court found that the essential purpose of the statute was to conserve the seniority rights of the class of public employees covered. The court found no rational basis for the arbitrary exclusion of certain classes of public employees within the statute. Accordingly, the court held that the statute was clearly special and contravened N.J. Const. art. IV, § VII, par.9 (13), which prohibited the passage of special or local laws regulating the internal affairs of municipalities formed for local government and counties.


OUTCOME: Trial court's judgment for plaintiff police officers was reversed and remanded because the court found the statute under which plaintiffs were awarded credit for prior service to be unconstitutional.

In re Adoption of a Child by C.


A-2766-78


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


171 N.J. Super. 553; 410 A.2d 265; 1979 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1005


December 10, 1979, Submitted  
December 20, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Superior Court, Chancery Division, Morris, County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, husband and wife, sought review of an order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, which denied plaintiffs motion requesting the superior court to order the state registrar to change the recorded place of birth of plaintiffs' adopted child to that of plaintiffs.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, husband and wife, became the adoptive parents of a child born in Portugal. The adoption judgment ordered the state registrar, pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 26:8-40.1, to issue a new birth certificate stating the child's birth place as the adoptive parents' residence. The state registrar refused to issue the certificate, alleging that the statute did not permit such change for persons born outside the United States. Upon plaintiffs' motion to enforce the judgment, the trial court held that the provision in the judgment ordering the issuance of the birth certificate was in error, and a second judgment was entered without the provision. Upon plaintiffs' second motion, alleging that the statute violated the equal protection clause of the United States Constitution, the trial court held that good cause was not shown as to why the recorded place of birth should be changed. The court affirmed, holding that § 26:8-40.1 was clear in requiring a proof of good cause before a court could order the recorded change in the adopted person's place of birth. The court further held that the trial court's conclusion that good cause had not been shown was supported by the record.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order denying the motion filed by plaintiffs, husband and wife, requesting the court to order the state registrar to change the recorded place of birth of plaintiffs' adopted child because the relevant statute required a showing of good cause before such a change could be made, and there was sufficient support for the trial court's conclusion that plaintiffs failed to show good cause.

Helmsley-Spear, Inc. v. Rent Leveling Board


A-717-78


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


171 N.J. Super. 254; 408 A.2d 815; 1979 N.J. Super. LEXIS 968


October 29, 1979, Argued  
November 13, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Superior Court, Law Division, Bergen County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landlord appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey that awarded defendant tenant $ 4,498 for rents paid to plaintiff that were deemed excessive under defendant municipality's rent leveling ordinance.


OVERVIEW: Defendant tenant renewed his lease with plaintiff landlord for a three-year term, with the rent increasing each year, beginning October 1971. Defendant municipality enacted a rent leveling ordinance effective November 1974. In 1974 and 1975, defendant tenant signed one-year renewal leases. The ordinance was pre-empted in June 1976 by the U.S. Department of Housing and Urban Development, which set the maximum allowable rent on defendant tenant's apartment at $ 785 per month. Defendant tenant then entered into a two-year lease at a monthly rent of $ 870. Defendant tenant filed a complaint with defendant municipality's Rent Leveling Board. The board determined that plaintiff owed defendant tenant a refund of $ 2,178 for excessive rents paid under the 1971-1974 step-up lease. On appeal, the trial judge affirmed and awarded $ 4,498. On further appeal, the court determined that the ordinance was intended to operate only at the expiration of leases in existence when it was enacted. The award of $ 2,178 was erroneous. The judgment was vacated and the matter remanded to the board to determine what amount defendant tenant was entitled to recover under leases from November 1974.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment awarding defendant tenant $ 4,498 for rents paid to plaintiff landlord that were deemed excessive under defendant municipality's rent leveling ordinance. The ordinance operated at the expiration of leases in existence when it was enacted, and defendant tenant's three-year lease predated the ordinance. The matter was remanded to determine what amount defendant tenant was owed after he renewed in November 1974.

Puttrich v. Smith


A-927-78


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


170 N.J. Super. 572; 407 A.2d 842; 1979 N.J. Super. LEXIS 945


October 3, 1979, Argued  
October 17, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Bergen County District Court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff owner appealed an order of the Bergen County District Court (New Jersey), which granted judgment in favor of defendant tenants in plaintiff's summary dispossess action under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:18-61.1(h).


OVERVIEW: Defendant tenants resided in an apartment on the ground floor of plaintiff owner's building. Plaintiff brought a summary dispossess action against defendants, because he wanted to eliminate the ground-floor apartment and expand the tavern in the building. The trial court entered judgment for defendants. Plaintiff appealed. The court affirmed, because plaintiff failed to establish good cause for evicting defendants under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:18-61.1(h). The court held that plaintiff was required to retire the entire building, not just one of four dwelling units, from the rental market in order to dispossess defendants. The court held that the enactment of subsection (h) was a reasonable exercise of the state's police power in protecting residential tenants from a critical shortage of rental housing. The court was satisfied that the statutory control of units larger than two rental units did not deprive an owner of most of his interest in them.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of defendant tenants, because plaintiff owner failed to establish the statutory good cause for evicting defendants.

State v. Hill


A-2560-78


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


170 N.J. Super. 485; 406 A.2d 1334; 1979 N.J. Super. LEXIS 921


September 17, 1979, Argued  
October 15, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Superior Court, Law Division, Somerset County, whose opinion is reported in State v. Hill, 166 N.J. Super. 224 (1978).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought interlocutory review of a decision of the Superior Court, Somerset County (New Jersey) which determined that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:138-2 was unconstitutional and dismissed two counts of the state's indictments against defendant.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a resident at a state neuropsychiatric institute. The state charged him under the fourth and fifth counts of a five-count indictment with carnal knowledge of two female residents of that institution, in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A: 138-2. Defendant contended that the statute was unconstitutional. The lower court held that the statute was unconstitutional and dismissed the fourth and fifth counts of the state's indictment. The state sought interlocutory review of the decision. On appeal, the lower court's order was reversed and the fourth and fifth counts of the indictment were reinstated. The appellate court held that the statutory classification's distinction between males and females was subject to scrutiny but was constitutional because it served an important governmental in protecting institutionalized feebleminded or mentally ill females, and because the prohibition of sexual intercourse with such persons, who may not fully comprehend the significance or consequences of such conduct, was substantially related to the achievement of that protection.


OUTCOME: The lower court's determination that the applicable statute was unconstitutional and its dismissal of two counts of the state's indictment against defendant was reversed and the counts were reinstated. The appellate court held that the lower court erred in finding the statute unconstitutional because it constituted a proper exercise of legislative police power and was constitutional.

In re Guardianship of Jones


A-3467-77


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


170 N.J. Super. 478; 406 A.2d 1331; 1979 N.J. Super. LEXIS 914


September 18, 1979, Submitted  
October 1, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Camden County Court, Probate Division.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant welfare board challenged a decision of the Camden County Court (New Jersey), which limited the date of appellant's right to reimbursement and deducted a pro rata share of the attorney fees incurred by respondent welfare recipient to secure the judgment from which the recovery was paid.


OVERVIEW: Respondent welfare recipient was injured in an auto accident and entered an agreement to reimburse appellant welfare board for assistance he had received. The court held that appellant was entitled to recover under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 44:10, but reversed the part of the trial court's order that limited appellant's recovery to the time period after the judgment. The court reasoned that the agreement allowed recovery from the date it was entered. The court also reversed the part of the trial court's order that charged appellant's recovery with a pro rata share of the attorney fees. The court reasoned that appellant was not a subrogee in the action and therefore the imposition of attorneys fees was not proper. The court found that appellant had no derivative right to action against the tort feasor and there was no interrelationship between the parties.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the part of the order awarding respondent welfare board recovery from the period of time after the recovery, holding that respondent's right to reimbursement, under an agreement between the parties, began from and after the date of the agreement.

ADA Financial Service Corp. v. State


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


174 N.J. Super. 337; 416 A.2d 908; 1979 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1033


March 27, 1979, Argued  
August 8, 1979, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, Commissioner of Department of Insurance, appealed from a judgment of the Law Division (New Jersey) declaring the provisions of N.J Stat. Ann. § 17:22-6.6a and § 17B:22-8(c) unconstitutional as violative of the Equal Protection and Due Process Clauses of the federal and state constitutions.


OVERVIEW: N.J. Stat. Ann. § 17:22-6.6a prohibited defendant, the Commissioner of Department of Insurance, from renewing the insurance license of any agent or broker that was affiliated with a financial institution. Exclusions in the statute enabled lending institutions engaged in the business of providing certain types of insurance to apply for and renew requisite licenses. Lending institutions engaged in the business of providing any other type of insurance were expressly denied the privilege of being issued or renewing any licenses. A second exception provided that finance companies affiliated with insurance companies were not subjected to the statutory prohibition, but all finance companies not affiliated with insurance companies were prohibited from engaging in the insurance business. Similar language was adopted at N.J. Stat. Ann. § 17B:22-8(c). Plaintiffs, who were agents or brokers, were notified that their licenses would not be renewed because they were in some way affiliated with a financial institution. The court held that the legislation was constitutionally invalid because of the absence of a logical basis for exclusions made by the legislature in the body of the statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court, finding the statutes to be unconstitutional as violative of the equal protection clauses of the federal and state constitutions. The legislature, without rational justification, chose to exempt some persons from a classification to which they logically and fairly belonged. Such statutory underinclusiveness was appropriately found to be so arbitrary as to deny equal protection.

Morris Plains v. Department of Public Advocate


A-853-78, A-2667-78, A-911-78, A-930-78, A-908-78, A-2524-78, A-1153-78, A-2525-78, A-909-78, A-1022-78, A-1047-78, A-906-78, A-919-78, A-939-78, A-2666-78, A-938-78, A-2668-78, A-2635-78, A-2719-78, A-1076-78, A-1051-78, A-1198-78.

State v. Carmel


A-4737-77


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


169 N.J. Super. 370; 404 A.2d 1227; 1979 N.J. Super. LEXIS 872


March 13, 1979, Argued  
July 3, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court, Law Division, Bergen County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant storeowner challenged an interlocutory order from the Superior Court of Bergen County (New Jersey), which denied his motion to suppress material taken from his store. The materials were related to charges against him for violating N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:115-2, by uttering, or possessing with intent to utter or expose obscene and indecent books, magazines, and films as defined by statute.


OVERVIEW: Defendant storeowner appealed an interlocutory order that denied his motion to suppress books, magazines, and films that were seized from his store. Defendant was charged with violating N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:115-2, by uttering, or possessing with intent to utter or expose such materials. The court reversed the order. The court agreed with defendant's claim that the search warrant under which the material was seized was constitutionally defective. The court first ruled that the affidavit in support of the warrant did not provide a sufficient basis for its issuance. The court observed that the affidavit lacked a factual basis in that it contained only general descriptions of the contents of magazines and several titles without relating such descriptions to particular books or magazines. The court also ruled that that the warrant itself was invalid as it suffered from vagueness and overbreadth. Specifically, the warrant authorized seizure of "obscene" and "lewd and indecent" material. Such terms, the court ruled, were not sufficiently definite so that the officer executing the warrant could identify the property sought with reasonable certainty.


OUTCOME: The court reversed an interlocutory order that denied defendant storeowner's motion to suppress obscene material seized from his store. The materials were seized pursuant to a constitutionally defective warrant, in that the supporting affidavit did not provide sufficient basis for the warrant and the warrant itself did not describe with sufficient particularity the items to be seized. The materials were not per se contraband.

Orange Tax Payers Council v. Orange


A-499-77, A-908-77


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


169 N.J. Super. 288; 404 A.2d 1186; 1979 N.J. Super. LEXIS 869


April 30, 1979, Argued  
June 20, 1979, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certification granted Orange Taxpayers Council v. Orange, 81 N.J. 399, 408 A.2d 793, 1979 N.J. LEXIS 1962 (1979)
Affirmed by Orange Taxpayers Council v. Orange, 83 N.J. 246, 416 A.2d 353, 1980 N.J. LEXIS 1354 (1980)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Superior Court, Law Division, Essex County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, city, city rent leveling board, tenants association and tenants challenged the decision from the Superior Court of New Jersey, which granted summary judgment to plaintiff taxpayer corporations and individuals declaring invalid and unenforceable an amendment to a rent leveling ordinance. Defendants asserted the trial judge erred in striking the ordinance and repealing the tax surcharge pass-through provision in the ordinance.


OVERVIEW: Defendants, city, city rent leveling board, tenants association and tenants appealed, with leave granted, from summary judgment declaring invalid and unenforceable an amendment to the rent leveling ordinance. The amendment repealed the tax surcharge provision and required "substantial compliance" with the property maintenance code as a condition precedent to an increase in rents in the action brought by plaintiff taxpayer corporations and individuals. The court found that the basic inquiry in reviewing any rent control scheme was to determine whether it permitted an efficient landlord to realize a just and reasonable return on his property The court held that the rent control insofar as it repealed the pre-existing tax surcharge passthrough provision, was facially constitutional and valid, the Tenants' Property Tax Rebate Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 54:4-6.2, neither preempted the field of municipal rent control nor prevented repeal of tax surcharges allowed incident thereto, and the substantial compliance provisions of the rent control ordinance were not facially invalid. Thus, the court reversed and remanded the proceeding.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the trial court's decision, which granted summary judgment to plaintiff taxpayer corporations and individuals and against defendants, city, city rent leveling board, tenants association and tenants. The court held that the rent control was facially constitutional, did not preempt the municipal rent control nor prevented repeal of tax surcharges and the substantial compliance was facially not invalid.

Velmohos v. Maren Engineering Corp.


A-5075-77


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


168 N.J. Super. 520; 403 A.2d 927; 1979 N.J. Super. LEXIS 784


May 8, 1979, Argued  
May 29, 1979, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certification granted Velmohos v. Maren Engineering Corp., 82 N.J. 288, 412 A.2d 794, 1980 N.J. LEXIS 1841 (1980)
Affirmed by Velmohos v. Maren Engineering Corp., 83 N.J. 282, 416 A.2d 372, 1980 N.J. LEXIS 1351 (1980)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Superior Court, Law Division, Middlesex County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured individual sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, which granted defendant corporations' motions for dismissal on the ground that the statute of limitations, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:14-2, barred the action. Defendants were unrepresented foreign corporations, constitutionally amenable to long-arm service of process under N.J. Ct. R. 4:4-4(c)(1).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff injured individual claimed damages as the result of defective equipment supplied by defendant corporations. Defendants were incorporated in Illinois, neither was registered to do business in New Jersey, and each was constitutionally amenable to long-arm service of process under N.J. Ct. R. 4:4-4(c)(1) by reason of their contacts in the state. Claims for personal injuries were usually barred if an action was not brought within two years from when the cause of action accrued. N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:14-2 contained a tolling provision for such actions against unrepresented foreign corporations. The trial court granted defendants' motions to dismiss, holding that § 2A:14-2, was unconstitutional as applied to defendants. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment of the trial court, finding that § 2A:14-22, did not offend U.S. Const. amend. XIV. There was a reasonable basis for a distinction between the application of the tolling statute as to foreign corporations represented in the state and as to those not so represented, as service on a represented foreign corporation could be easy compared to service on an unrepresented foreign corporation.


OUTCOME: The judgment entered in the trial court, which granted defendant corporations' motion for dismissal, was reversed because the court found that the application of the tolling statute did not offend the Equal Protection Clause.

Trantino v. Department of Corrections


A-625-77, A-2192-77, A-3783-77


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


168 N.J. Super. 220; 402 A.2d 947; 1979 N.J. Super. LEXIS 767


February 27, 1979, Argued  
May 15, 1979, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certification denied by Trantino v. Department of Corrections, 81 N.J. 338, 407 A.2d 1212, 1979 N.J. LEXIS 1842 (1979)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the New Jersey Department of Corrections.
State v. Trantino, 44 N.J. 358, 209 A.2d 117, 1965 N.J. LEXIS 237 (1965)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoners sought review from final decisions of respondent New Jersey Department of Corrections for refusing to grant them work credits toward parole eligibility for their time spent on death row.


OVERVIEW: Appellant prisoners sought review of respondent department of correction's decision to refuse appellants' work credits for time spent on death row. The court rejected appellants' claim that case law mandated the grant despite not working while on death row because appellants were not entitled to work credits for work they did not perform. The legislature intended the grant of work credit predicated on a prisoner's actual performance of work, which applied despite there being good reasons for not working. Appellants' contention that respondent's policy of denying death row inmates work credit was violative of the equal protection clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV was rejected. Such a policy was subject to rational basis scrutiny that existed by distinguishing between death row prisoners and others. The punishment's finality foreclosed any notion of rehabilitation and justified the need to accord different treatment through segregation to prisoners sentenced to death. Those prisoners did not work, and were not entitled to work credits. Appellants did not meet the threshold for equal protection analysis: to demonstrate disparate treatment among members of the same class.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decisions of respondent department of corrections to refuse to grant work credits to appellants prisoners for the time spent on death row because case law did not intend to alter legislative policy that work credit was based upon actual work performed. Moreover, such a policy was not violative of equal protection rights because the policy was subject to rational basis scrutiny.

In re Oertel


A-1366-77


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


167 N.J. Super. 557; 401 A.2d 545; 1979 N.J. Super. LEXIS 739


March 26, 1979, Argued  
April 24, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Division of Medical Assistance and Health Services, Department of Human Services.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant medical device provider sought review of a decision of respondent Division of Medical Assistance and Health Services (New Jersey), which denied him status as an eligible Medicaid provider of orthotic services based on N.J. Admin. Code tit. 10, §§ 55-1.1, 1.2. He challenged the denial claiming the regulation exceeded respondent's rule-making power and because it unconstitutionally delegated government authority to a private agency.


OVERVIEW: Appellant medical device provider was denied certification as an eligible Medicaid provider of orthotic services based on his lack of certification by the American Board of Certification in Orthotics and Prosthetics, Inc. (ABC) in orthotics, as provided by N.J. Admin. Code tit. 10, §§ 55-1.1, 1.2. He contended that the certification requirement exceeded respondent Division of Medical Assistance and Health Service's rule making authority, and that it was an unconstitutional delegation of power to a private agency. The court disposed of the first argument finding that it was a syllogistic turn on state licensing requirements, but the regulation complained of was not a licensing requirement, but rather was an attempt to set up objective criteria for guaranteeing that public money was well spent. On the second argument, the court held that the delegation to a private company for certification purposes was not per se unreasonable, but the record was inadequate for the purpose of review. Accordingly, the court remanded to respondent for limited proceedings on the nature and character of ABC, with further briefs to be submitted. The court retained jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court held that respondent division had not exceeded its rule making authority in establishing criteria for Medicaid providers of orthotics devices, but that the legitimacy of the process required further briefing because respondent had delegated some of the reasonable certification requirement to a private company. The absence in the record of information about the company required a remand and further briefing.

Department of Labor & Industry, Div. of Workplace Standards v. Union Paving & Constr. Co.


A-577-78


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


168 N.J. Super. 19; 401 A.2d 698; 1979 N.J. Super. LEXIS 745


March 27, 1979, Argued  
April 12, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from final decision of Commissioner of Labor and Industry.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant contractor sought review of a decision of the Commissioner of Labor and Industry (New Jersey), which placed appellant's name on a list of firms ineligible for public works contracts for failing to pay prevailing wages, in an action by respondent labor department, pursuant to the debarment provisions of the Prevailing Wage Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. 34:11-56.25, et seq.


OVERVIEW: Appellant contractor underpaid wages on six government contract jobs. Respondent labor department brought an action before the Commissioner of Labor and Industry to have appellant declared ineligible for public works contracts. The court affirmed the decision of the Commissioner in favor of respondent and found that although the Prevailing Wage Act (Act), N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 34:11-56.25, et seq., did not seem to require intentional violations in order to be barred from receiving government contracts, appellants repeated violations raised an inference of intent or flagrant disregard rising to the level of intent that would justify being debarred. The court found that appellant's debarment did not violate due process because the Act did not confer any property rights upon appellant sufficient to meet the threshold due process requirements. The court found that although the debarment clause of the Act appeared to be mandatory on its face, and, thus, susceptible to producing arbitrary results, application of the provision was left to the discretion of the Commissioner and under these facts its application was not arbitrary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the Commissioner of Labor and Industry against appellant contractor in respondent labor department's action to have appellant declared ineligible to receive public works contracts because appellant's repeated violations of the Prevailing Wage Act represented a breach of his statutory duties sufficient to justify debarment.

Ricci v. Senior Citizens & Taxpayers Fed Up with Byrne Democrats


A-1501-76


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


166 N.J. Super. 519; 400 A.2d 117; 1979 N.J. Super. LEXIS 641


February 13, 1979, Argued  
March 19, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Election Law Enforcement Commission.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, political committee and its members, sought review of an order by the Election Law Enforcement Commission (New Jersey), which granted appellee candidate's claims that appellant violated the New Jersey Campaign Contributions and Expenditures Reporting Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 19:44A-1 et seq. The court held that because the advertisement that was run by appellants cost less than the reporting threshold, reporting was unnecessary.


OVERVIEW: Appellee candidate filed a complaint with the Election Law Enforcement Commission which alleged that appellants, political committee and its members, violated the Campaign Contributions and Expenditures Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 19:44A-1 et seq., by running a newspaper advertisement critical of appellee. Appellee argued that appellants did not report the expenditures for the advertisements as required by N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 19:44A-10 and 19:44A-12. The Election Law Commission ruled in favor of appellee, and appellants sought review, arguing that they were not constitutionally subject to the requirements of N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 19:44A-10 and 19:44A-12. The court reversed, holding that reporting requirements were only required when $ 750 or greater was expended. The court stated that groups spending less than that amount were so small in size or consequence that requiring reporting of lesser amounts would impermissibly chill their freedom of expression. The court further stated that concerted campaign activity for or against a candidate for public office was a valid exercise of the freedom of expression and association.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the election law enforcement commission's grant of judgment to appellee candidate on his claims that appellants, political committee and its members, violated the campaign contributions reporting act. The court held that reporting requirements were only required when $ 750 or greater was expended. Thus, appellants were not constitutionally required to report campaign expenditures.

 

1344 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Giacchetto


A-4549-77


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


166 N.J. Super. 351; 399 A.2d 1031; 1979 N.J. Super. LEXIS 675


January 29, 1979, Argued  
March 13, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Somerset County Court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of the order of the Somerset County Court (New Jersey), which, after a trial de novo, affirmed the order of the municipal court finding them guilty of failing to comply with the ordinance requiring owners and tenants to remove snow and ice from sidewalks within 12 hours of daylight after the snow fell or the ice formed. Defendants alleged the ordinance was unconstitutional and the fine excessive.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were found guilty in municipal court of violating the ordinance requiring snow and ice removal within a specified period of time after the snow fell or the ice formed. Defendants sought review by trial de novo in the county court, and the latter affirmed the conviction. Defendants appealed, arguing that the ordinance was unconstitutionally vague and the penalty permitted excessive. The court affirmed, after finding that there were no New Jersey cases on point, by relying on the fact that such ordinances had been upheld elsewhere as a valid exercise of the police power. The court held that contrary to defendants' argument, an ordinance was not invalid merely because it imposed a burden on some citizens necessary for the public good. The court held that as applied to defendants under the evidence adduced, the ordinance was not vague. The court also rejected defendants' argument that the penalty provided by the ordinance, a fine up to $ 500 and imprisonment of up to 90 days for each successive day of noncompliance, was excessive, because the penalty was statutorily authorized and in any event defendants were fined only $ 5.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction of defendants for failure to comply with the city sidewalk snow and ice removal ordinance, finding that as applied to defendants, the ordinance was not unconstitutionally vague, that enactment of the ordinance was a valid exercise of the police power, and that defendants could not challenge the maximum penalty authorized by the ordinance because they received only a nominal fine.
