Gilbert v. State, Dep't of Human Services, Div. of Public Welfare


A-2318-77


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


167 N.J. Super. 217; 400 A.2d 803; 1979 N.J. Super. LEXIS 679


January 16, 1979, Argued  
March 1, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Division of Public Welfare.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant recipient sought review of an order from respondent Division of Public Welfare (New Jersey), which terminated appellant's general assistance benefits.


OVERVIEW: Respondent Division of Public Welfare terminated appellant recipient's welfare benefits because a VISTA stipend increased her monthly income. Appellant contended that the termination was a violation of 42 U.S.C.S.§ 5044(g), which exempted such payments from welfare income calculations. Respondent contended that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 44:8-107 et seq. delegated responsibility to the municipalities and that N.J. Admin. Code tit. 10:85, § 3.3(e)(1)(ii), was not preempted because the general assistance program received no federal funds. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded. The court held that the federal statute superseded the contrary provision of the New Jersey general assistance regulation. The extent of federal financial participation in the totality of the welfare scheme was so pervasive, substantial, and so ultimately ameliorative of the state's traditional obligations in that area of governmental service that the limited component of that scheme maintained by the state alone was not fairly regarded as the performance of a sovereign function under U.S. Const. amend. X. Section 5044(g) was not constitutionally vulnerable and, therefore, preempted tit. 10:85, § 3.3(e)(1)(ii).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of respondent Division of Public Welfare, which terminated appellant recipient's general assistance benefits. The court held that the administration of a welfare program was not regarded as a sovereign state function, and a federal statute exempting VISTA payments from income calculations for welfare purposes preempted the state statute.

 

1346 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Olds v. Klein


A-2876-77


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


166 N.J. Super. 28; 398 A.2d 1311; 1979 N.J. Super. LEXIS 582


January 17, 1979, Argued  
February 7, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the final determination of the Department of Human Services, Division of Public Welfare.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, father and mother on behalf of themselves and their minor children, sought review of a judgment of respondent, Department of Human Services, Division of Public Welfare (New Jersey), which upheld a denial to appellant father of benefits under the Aid to Families with Dependent Children program.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, father and mother on behalf of themselves and their minor children, challenged a decision of respondent, Department of Human Services, Division of Public Welfare, which upheld the denial to appellant father of benefits under the Aid to Families with Dependent Children (AFDC) program. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that appellant father was not entitled to benefits under the AFDC-N program granted to individuals with insufficient income because he was a full-time college student who had refused to accept full-time employment. The court found that appellant father did not establish "good cause" to refuse where he had marketable skills and was capable of supporting his family. The court found that appellant father's college training had in the past enabled him to obtain employment as a laboratory technician in three different chemical research facilities.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of respondent, Department of Human Services, Division of Public Welfare, which denied Aid to Families with Dependent Children benefits to appellant father because he did not establish "good cause" for his refusal to accept full-time employment and he had marketable skills that had enabled him to obtain employment in the past.

 

1347 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Rubin v. Glaser


A-2043-77


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


166 N.J. Super. 258; 399 A.2d 984; 1979 N.J. Super. LEXIS 631


December 11, 1978, Argued  
February 1, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Division of Tax Appeals.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant nonresident property owners sought review of a decision of the Division of Tax Appeals (New Jersey), which denied a rebate on property taxes paid on appellants' summer home in an action against respondent State of New Jersey and state and local officials, and held that matters of constitutional adjudication of the Homestead Rebate Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 54:4-3.80 et seq., fell outside the scope of its allotted jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: Appellant nonresident property owners were denied a homestead rebate on their vacation home which was admittedly not their principal place of residence. They sought review through the Division of Tax Appeals against respondent State of New Jersey and state and local officials, challenging the constitutionality of the Homestead Rebate Act (Act), N.J. Stat. Ann. § 54:4-3.80 et seq, as violating the Privileges and Immunities Clause, U.S. Const., art. IV, § 2, cl. 1, and equal protection under U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The Division denied the rebate but held that matters of constitutional adjudication fell outside the scope of its allotted jurisdiction. The court upheld the denial of the rebate and found the Act to be constitutional. The court found that the Act did not disqualify appellants from eligibility for the rebate on the ground of their nonresidency but because their New Jersey property was not their principal dwelling. The court held that the allocation of tax burden based upon principal residence did not violate the Privileges and Immunities Clause or equal protection.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of a property tax rebate for appellant nonresident property owners in their challenge against respondent State of New Jersey and state and local officials as to the constitutionality of the Homestead Rebate Act (Act). The court found that the Act did not violate the Privileges and Immunities Clause nor equal protection in its allocation of tax burden according to a taxpayer's principal place of residence.

Civil Service Com. v. Senate of New Jersey


A-3252-76


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


165 N.J. Super. 144; 397 A.2d 1098; 1979 N.J. Super. LEXIS 529


December 5, 1978, Submitted  
January 5, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Superior Court, Law Division, Mercer County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant general assembly challenged the decision of the Superior Court, Mercer County (New Jersey), which granted the motion of appellees, civil service and police training commissions, for judgment on the pleadings declaring unconstitutional all legislation waiving civil service merit and fitness qualifications for certain individuals and authorizing their permanent appointment to civil service positions.


OVERVIEW: Appellees, civil service and police training commissions, brought a declaratory action against appellant general assembly, challenging special legislation waiving civil service merit and fitness qualifications for certain individuals to civil service positions. The trial court granted appellees' motion for judgment on the pleadings, finding that the legislation violated N.J. Const. art. IV, § VII, para. 9(5). On appeal, the court vacated the judgment and determined that the trial court's decision was void, because it should have dismissed appellees' complaint on the grounds that the action did not present a justiciable controversy where there was present a viable statute affecting the rights or status of appellees. Rather, the court held that appellees improperly sought to have the trial court provide an advisory opinion that future legislation of the same type would not be constitutional. The court further held that appellees had not sought timely review of any of the numerous statutes of the type they found objectionable.


OUTCOME: The court vacated and voided the grant of the motion of appellees, civil service and police training commissions, for judgment on the pleadings in a declaratory judgment action against appellee general assembly, because there was no viable statute affecting appellees' rights and thus the complaint did not present a justiciable controversy.

State v. Cross


A-3699-77


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


164 N.J. Super. 368; 396 A.2d 604; 1978 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1223


November 28, 1978, Argued  
December 14, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Somerset County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed an order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Somerset County, which granted defendants' motions to suppress evidence seized without a warrant from the glove compartment of an automobile in which defendants were riding.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were stopped and ticketed for speeding. When the officer radioed for an investigative check on the car's registration, he was told that the car had been stolen. While arresting defendants for possession of a stolen motor vehicle, defendants insisted that the car was not stolen. The officer began to search the car for personal identification of defendants, and discovered capsules and tablets in the glove compartment of the automobile. After returning to the station, the officer requested that the status of the vehicle be checked more carefully. He was advised that one defendant owned the car, that he had reported the car as stolen, but that it had been returned to him, and the report had not been cancelled. The trial court granted defendants' motions to suppress the evidence found in the glove compartment, and the state appealed the order. The court reversed and remanded, holding that the search was justified as incidental to a valid arrest. The court held that the information on which the officer relied was ascertained to be erroneous only after the arrest and search had taken place. The officer had acted reasonably and had relied on the information in good faith.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's grant of defendants' motion to suppress evidence and remanded, holding that the search of the glove compartment was justified as incidental to a valid arrest because the information on which the officer relied was ascertained to be erroneous only after the arrest and search had taken place, and the officer had acted reasonably and had relied on the information in good faith.

 

1350 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ciuffini


A-1775-76


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


164 N.J. Super. 145; 395 A.2d 904; 1978 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1172


October 30, 1978, Submitted  
December 6, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Ocean County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal defendant appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Ocean County, following jury verdicts finding defendant guilty of assault with intent to commit sodomy, pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:90-2.


OVERVIEW: Criminal defendant appealed from the trial court's judgment, following a conviction for assault with intent to commit sodomy, pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:90-2. He contended that the trial judge erred in precluding affirmative evidence or cross-examination on the alleged victim's consensual participation. The court reversed the conviction, finding that consensual participation was a valid defense. The court reasoned that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:110-1, which criminalized sodomy between consenting adults, was an unconstitutional exercise of the state's police power, so that defendant had a right to investigate that area. The court rejected the state's argument that the ruling was harmless, because the conviction was based on assault, which precluded consent. The court found that the trial court's instruction made the holding of assault contingent on the jury's finding non-consensual sodomy. The court also found that defendant was permitted to probe the victim's alleged drug use at the new trial, as use of drugs had a potential effect on the victim's ability to perceive and recall.


OUTCOME: The court reversed criminal defendant's conviction for assault with intent to commit sodomy, finding that consensual participation would be a valid defense, and denial of defendant's right to investigate consent constituted error.

 

1351 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


New Jersey Asso. on Correction v. Lan


A-459-78


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


164 N.J. Super. 115; 395 A.2d 889; 1978 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1206


October 30, 1978, Argued  
December 1, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Superior Court, Law Division, Mercer County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff citizen group sought review of the decision of the Superior Court, Mercer County (New Jersey), which upheld the constitutionality of the Institutional Construction Bond Act of 1978, c.79, 1978 N.J. Laws 79.


OVERVIEW: The state submitted a referendum, the Institutional Construction Bond Act of 1978, c.79, 1978 N.J. Laws 79, to voters for approval. Plaintiff citizens challenged the constitutionality of the referendum on the ground that it embraced a multiplicity of purposes in violation of N.J. Const. art. IV, § 7, para. 4 and art. VIII, § 2, para. 3. The referendum passed and was upheld as constitutional by the trial court. Plaintiffs sought review of the trial court's decision. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's decision because the commonality of the proposed expenditures was not in compliance with the single subject rule of N.J. Const. art. VIII, § 2, para. 3. The single subject rule prohibited the packaging of disparate objects or works into a single proposition submitted to the voters for a single vote. The court held that the construction of a building, or buildings, without advice concerning the use of the building was not an appropriate legislative object because the law was too general and obtained voter approval without limit as to its multiple purposes in violation of the constitution.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision upholding the constitutionality of a referendum to construct public buildings. The court held that the purpose of the buildings was not explained in the referendum and did not allow voters the opportunity to approve a single measure, in violation of the constitution's single object or work rule.

Wright v. Plaza Ford


A-2052-75


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


164 N.J. Super. 203; 395 A.2d 1259; 1978 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1181

Also, although not named as a separate party, appellant attorney sought review of three orders orally entered holding him in contempt for misconduct in the presence of the judge of compensation.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner employee suffered myocardial infarction at respondent employer's place of business after petitioner ran up a flight of steps when his boss told him to turn off an alarm. Petitioner had not worked since. Total disability was attributed to the disability incurred in his last employment with respondent. The court found that the administrative tribunal was incompetent to adjudge the contempt. Regarding the fee awarded to a resident medical witness, the court held that it could not exceed $ 50 inclusive of his services in making an examination and report incidental to testifying.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment as to counsel and witness fees. The adjudication and imposition of sentence for the contempts of appellant attorney were reversed and vacated for lack of jurisdiction. The court also held that the fee awarded to a resident medical witness could not exceed $ 50.

New Jersey Div. of Youth & Family Services v. W.


D-704-75


Juvenile and Domestic Relations Court of New Jersey, Cumberland County


165 N.J. Super. 492; 398 A.2d 611; 1978 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1363



November 2, 1978 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the Division of Youth and Family Services, sought an order from the Juvenile and Domestic Relations Court of New Jersey, Cumberland County, to permit an investigation into the circumstances of defendants' infant child, and directing his parents to assist and cooperate in its investigation of the welfare of the infant.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, Division of Youth and Family Services sought an investigative order. N.J. Stat. Ann. § 30:4C-12 permitted plaintiff to apply for an investigative order where it had previously requested the parents to allow an investigation into the conditions and care of a child, but has been refused. The statute implied a complaint from an outside agency or concerned citizen which plaintiff has a duty to investigate. There had been no such complaint in this case. Plaintiff was on its own motion, seeking to investigate the circumstances of this child. The sole fact upon which plaintiff relied was the judicial finding 22 months prior to the date of this hearing that defendants were incapable of parenting their children. Thus, the mere coming before the court, citing a conclusionary fact without evidentiary facts to sustain that conclusion, was insufficient. Plaintiff's application for the issuance of an order requiring investigation was denied without prejudice.


OUTCOME: The application was denied was because there had been no new facts presented by plaintiff upon which to find probable cause for the investigative order.

Princeton v. New Jersey Dep't of Education


A-1528-76A-1687-76 A-1665-76 A-1653-76 A-1858-76


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


163 N.J. Super. 389; 394 A.2d 1240; 1978 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1138


October 5, 1978, Argued  
October 31, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Superior Court, Law Division, Mercer County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, municipalities and constituent members of regional school districts, appealed from the decision of the Superior Court, Mercer County (New Jersey), which entered summary judgment in favor of defendants, municipalities, the governor, and other state officials, after holding that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 18A:13-23.1 was unconstitutional but refusing to enjoin the implementation and enforcement of § 18A:13-23.1.


OVERVIEW: N.J. Stat. Ann. § 18A:13-23.1 was adopted as a supplement to the Public School Education Act of 1975, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 18A:7A-1 et seq. in order to ease the impact of a new budget allocation scheme on communities which had previously made contributions by the number of pupils sent to their school district. The new method, enacted by § 29 of the Public School Education Act of 1975, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 18A:13-23, required that budget allocation be apportioned according to equalized valuations or ratables in each community. Section 18A:23.1 called for a gradual, five-year phase-in of the § 29 basis of cost-sharing. Plaintiffs, municipalities and constituent members of regional school districts, challenged the interim phase-in of § 18A:13-23.1 as unconstitutional arguing that the retention of the per pupil basis for allocation of budget appropriations violated the constitutional mandate requiring the state to provide a thorough and efficient system of education. The court affirmed the trial court's refusal to enjoin enforcement of § 29 and held that § 29 was constitutional and a manifestly reasonable exercise of legislative power beyond the ambit of judicial interference.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's refusal to enjoin the implementation and enforcement of supplemental legislation to the Public School Education Act which called for the gradual phase-in of a new method of budget allocation for school districts within certain communities. The court disagreed with the trial court and held that the supplemental legislation was constitutional and a reasonable exercise of legislative power.

In re Estate of Sharp


A-4619-76


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


163 N.J. Super. 148; 394 A.2d 381; 1978 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1115


October 5, 1978, Submitted  
October 17, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Superior Court, Chancery Division, Mercer County, whose opinion is reported at 151 N.J. Super. 579.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant testator's estate sought review of a judgment entered in the Superior Court of New Jersey, Mercer County, which held that the will of the testator was void pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 3A:3-10 because no provision or mention was made for respondent afterborn child who survived appellant.


OVERVIEW: Appellant testator's estate sought review of a judgment entered by the court below, which held that testator's will was void pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 3A:3-10, on the grounds that no provision or mention was made for respondent afterborn child who survived appellant. The court held that prior state precedents that sustained the validity of the common law rule that barred an illegitimate child from inheriting from an intestate father were overruled. The court also declared that the common law rule applicable to illegitimate children of a male parent was unconstitutional and that all illegitimate children had the same right to intestate inheritance from their parents as legitimate children. The court held that the appellant's will was void pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 3A:3-10 because it lacked a provision for plaintiff's afterborn child. Finally, the court held that the order that declared respondent to be the sole heir entitled to the estate by intestate succession was warranted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment except for that portion of the judgment that declared N.J. Stat. Ann. § 3A:4-7 to be unconstitutional. The will of appellant testator was held to be void because no provision or mention was made for respondent afterborn child who survived appellant. The order that declared respondent to be the sole heir entitled to the estate by way of intestacy was held to have been warranted.

Scharwenka v. Cryogenics Management, Inc.


A-820-77


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


163 N.J. Super. 16; 394 A.2d 137; 1978 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1129


September 18, 1978, Submitted  
October 12, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Division of Workers' Compensation.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner widow appealed a judgment of the New Jersey Division of Workers' Compensation which granted respondent employer's motion to dismiss petitioner's dependency claim petition in a workers' compensation action.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner widow filed a dependency claim petition against respondent employer and sought to recover workers' compensation benefits arising from her husband's disappearance and presumed death which had occurred more than two years' prior to her claim. Respondent filed a motion to dismiss on the ground that petitioner's claim was barred by the statute of limitations. The Division of Workers' Compensation dismissed petitioner's claim, and she appealed. The court affirmed, holding that the petition was barred by the statute of limitations pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 34:15-51which provided that workers' compensation claims were to be filed within two years after the date of the employee's accident. The court held that every rational inference from the facts and circumstances of the decedent's accident was that he died on or about the date of his disappearance and that petitioner's contention that she would have been precluded from bringing any action prior to the expiration of the seven year period for unexplainable absence was without merit. Also without merit was petitioner's contention that § 34:15-51 was unconstitutional because it was not tolled until her minor son's adulthood.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of petitioner widow's claim for dependency benefits from respondent employer, holding that her claim was barred by the two year statute of limitations because decedent had died more than two years prior to the filing of her claim.

 

1357 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wein


A-2444-76


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


162 N.J. Super. 159; 392 A.2d 607; 1978 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1068


September 11, 1978, Argued  
September 19, 1978, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certification denied by State v. Wein, 79 N.J. 464, 401 A.2d 220, 1978 N.J. LEXIS 1120 (1978)
Certification granted by State v. Wein, 79 N.J. 464, 401 A.2d 220, 1978 N.J. LEXIS 1121 (1978)
Reversed by State v. Wein, 80 N.J. 491, 404 A.2d 302, 1979 N.J. LEXIS 1267 (1979)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Superior Court, Law Division, Essex County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed their convictions for conspiracy to sell and deliver obscene motion picture films and for selling and distributing a specific eight millimeter motion picture, entered in the Superior Court, Law Division, Essex County (New Jersey), asserting that the indictment was defective because it failed to charge scienter and that the prosecution failed to prove the three elements of the Miller test for obscenity.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were charged with and convicted of selling obscene materials and with conspiracy to sell obscene materials. The court modified the judgment, vacating the substantive convictions because the indictment failed to charge scienter where it specified only that defendants unlawfully sold obscene materials. The court affirmed the conspiracy convictions, holding that the indictment sufficiently charged scienter where it charged that defendants conspired willfully to sell obscene materials. This language sufficiently communicated to defendants a charge of intentional conspiracy to effect the sale of obscene materials, and by plainest implication it connoted that defendants knew of the nature and character of the material conspired to be sold. The court rejected defendants' contention that the prosecution failed to prove the three Miller elements of obscenity: defendants did not contend that the films had serious value; expert testimony was not needed to show that the films appealed to the prurient interest where the films were admitted into evidence; and the prosecution showed that the films violated local state community standards.


OUTCOME: The court modified the judgment to vacate the conviction on the count of sale of an obscene film, finding the indictment defective for failing to charge scienter. The court affirmed the convictions for conspiracy to sell obscene materials, holding that the indictment alleged scienter and that the prosecution proved the three elements of the Miller test.

New Jersey Bell Tel. Co. v. State, Dep't of Public Utilities, Board of Public Utility Comm'rs


A-1121-76


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


162 N.J. Super. 60; 392 A.2d 216; 1978 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1061


February 28, 1978, Argued  
August 21, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the New Jersey Board of Public Utility Commissioners.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant telephone company sought a de novo review of a decision from the New Jersey Board of Public Utility Commissioners and determination of its application for a rate increase.


OVERVIEW: Appellant telephone company sought a rate increase within months of being given rate relief. When it was dissatisfied with the decision from the Board of Public Utility Commissioners, appellant sought a de novo judicial review. Appellant claimed the rates were confiscatory. The court held that it lacked the power to conduct a de novo review, it could only determine whether the rates set by the board were reasonable. The claim of confiscation could only be upheld if the court found the rate of return was illegally arrived at. In determining the reasonableness of the rates, the court examined the company's rate base, its income and expenses, and the rate of return. The court found no merit to appellant's contention that the board denied rate relief for predetermined reasons unrelated to the merits of its application. In deferring to the board's expertise, the court found a sufficient record to support the board's decision. It also found no violation of the Open Public Meetings Act or the Administrative Procedure Act and it affirmed the decision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the rates set by respondent board because appellant telephone company was not entitled to a de novo review, and in deferring to respondent's expertise, it found that the rates were reasonably set in accordance with proper procedures.

Swiss Village Associates v. Municipal Council of Wayne


A-767-76


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


162 N.J. Super. 138; 392 A.2d 596; 1978 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1065


May 1, 1978, Argued

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Passaic County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant municipal counsel appealed a decision from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Passaic County, which granted summary judgment to defendant and held that zoning ordinance that failed to provide for high rise residential buildings was invalid.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff applied to defendant township for zoning for high rise residential apartment buildings. After the zoning board denied the request, plaintiff sought judicial review. The trial court granted defendant's motion for summary judgment and held that defendant's zoning ordinance, which failed to provide for high rise luxury apartments, was invalid. Defendant township appealed. The court held that zoning was a municipal function which carried a strong presumption of validity. Defendant township was not required to provide for every use within its borders. The court was unwilling to hold as a matter of law, that the ordinance was invalid because it prohibited such reasonable use of an acceptable mode of housing.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision which granted summary judgment to plaintiff developer because it was unwilling to rule that the ordinance, which precluded high rise apartment houses, was invalid.

1361 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Klebanow v. Glaser


A-3632-76


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


159 N.J. Super. 596; 388 A.2d 1015; 1978 N.J. Super. LEXIS 937


March 7, 1978, Argued  
May 22, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from a final decision of the Director of the Division of Taxation in the Department of the Treasury.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer challenged a decision from respondent Director of the Division of Taxation in the Department of the Treasury (New Jersey), which denied his claim for a refund of capital gains taxes paid under protest, on grounds that the statute authorizing the tax, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 54:8B-1 et seq., was unconstitutional as applied to him.


OVERVIEW: Appellant taxpayer moved in state and thereafter sold stock. After the stock sale, the legislature passed a statute authorizing a capital gains tax, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 54:8B-1 et seq., which applied retroactively to all sales occurring from the beginning of the calendar year. Appellant paid the tax under protest, then filed a claim for a refund, which was denied. He claimed that he sold the stock while a state resident in reliance on the non-existence of a capital gains tax, and would not have sold the stock had the tax been in effect. Appellant filed suit against respondents, tax division and officials, claiming that the statute was unconstitutional as applied retroactively to his case. On appeal, the court affirmed the decision of respondents, finding that at the time appellant sold his shares of corporate stock he should have been aware that the legislature was seriously considering some form of income tax which, if enacted, would have probably conformed to the generally accepted practice of making a tax law applicable, beginning usually on January 1, to that part of the year which preceded its enactment.


OUTCOME: Decision of respondents, tax division and officials, denying appellant taxpayer's claim for a refund of capital gains tax was affirmed because the statute under which the tax was retroactively assessed was not unconstitutional.

Van Horn v. Trenton


A-2391-76


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


159 N.J. Super. 115; 387 A.2d 373; 1978 N.J. Super. LEXIS 866


March 6, 1978, Argued  
May 8, 1978, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certification granted by Van Horn v. Trenton, 77 N.J. 509, 391 A.2d 522, 1978 N.J. LEXIS 1085 (1978)
Reversed by Van Horn v. Trenton, 80 N.J. 528, 404 A.2d 615, 1979 N.J. LEXIS 1266 (1979)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Mercer County District Court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city challenged the decision of the Mercer County District Court (New Jersey), which granted summary judgment in favor of plaintiff officer awarding him counsel fees incurred for legal services rendered in connection with grand jury consideration of charges against him.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff officer fired his police revolver in self defense and, at the conclusion of its investigation, the grand jury found no basis for any criminal charges against him. However, plaintiff was required to retain counsel for the purpose of representing him during the investigation and incurred counsel fees and disbursements. Defendant city refused to pay or reimburse plaintiff for the costs of retaining counsel, and the trial court granted summary judgment in plaintiff's favor with an award of fees. On review, the court reversed and remanded. The court found that the threatened charges, on account of which the attorney was retained, were incidental to the performance of plaintiff's duties as a police officer. The requirement of reimbursement under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40A:14-155, however, did not apply because the court concluded that plaintiff was never a defendant in any action or legal proceeding.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment in favor of plaintiff officer was reversed and remanded for further proceedings. The court found that the statutory provision at issue was inapplicable because plaintiff had not been charged with a criminal act against which he had to defend. Plaintiff was not entitled to reimbursement of costs of retaining counsel for a grand jury investigation.

 

1363 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Shanley v. Nuzzo


D-1095-77


Juvenile and Domestic Relations Court of New Jersey, Bergen County


160 N.J. Super. 436; 390 A.2d 158; 1978 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1347



April 25, 1978 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff father sought child support from defendant mother under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:4-18 for their two children who were in his custody. The mother filed a motion to dismiss the father's complaint on the grounds that the court lacked jurisdiction to determine the non-support matter.


OVERVIEW: The parties were divorced in New York several years earlier. The mother was awarded custody of the children, but on an informal basis, had surrendered custody to the father. Both parties were living in New Jersey when the father petitioned the court for child support. The mother argued that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:4-18(e), (f) compelled support by a husband but made no similar provision for a mother to support her children. The father contended that § 2A:4-18(b) authorized the court with the same power as the superior court to order support from a former wife. The court declined to address the father's argument that the statute was discriminatory and unconstitutional because it could base its decision on other grounds. The court found that § 2A:4-18(e), (f) did not apply because the parties were divorced and there was no desertion. Because the superior court had recognized that parents shared an equal duty to support their children, the court found that its concurrent jurisdiction under § 2A:4-18(b) permitted it to order a wife to pay child support. Denying the mother's motion to dismiss the father's complaint, the court ordered a hearing on whether support should be awarded.


OUTCOME: The court ruled that it had jurisdiction to order a former wife to pay support for her children, denied the mother's motion to dismiss the father's petition for child support, and ordered a hearing to determine whether support should be awarded to the father.

Urban Farms, Inc. v. Wayne Passaic County


A-1506-76


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


159 N.J. Super. 61; 386 A.2d 1357; 1978 N.J. Super. LEXIS 823


March 20, 1978, Argued  
April 21, 1978, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certification denied by Urban Farms, Inc. v. Wayne, 78 N.J. 330, 395 A.2d 199, 1978 N.J. LEXIS 472 (1978)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Division of Tax Appeals.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent township and petitioner taxpayer each appealed the decision of the Division of Tax Appeals (New Jersey), which found certain parcels of petitioner's land entitled to farmland assessment under the Farmland Assessment Act of 1964, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 54:4-23.1 et seq., and valued the land at the highest value for agricultural land.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner taxpayer operated certain parcels of land as a tree farm. The tax court found that the parcels were entitled to farmland assessment under the Farmland Assessment Act of 1964 (Act), N.J. Stat. Ann. § 54:4-23.1 et seq. The tax court also valued the land at $ 720 an acre, based on a finding that the land was "cropland harvested." Respondent township challenged the finding of farmland assessment and petitioner challenged the valuation. On appeal, the court affirmed the decision that the parcels were entitled to farmland assessment and reversed the valuation and remanded to the tax court for a hearing on the appropriate valuation. The court held that the evidence was sufficient to support the finding that the parcels were devoted to agricultural use as defined under the Act and that respondent had failed to meet its burden of overcoming the presumptive constitutionality of the Act. The court also held that the parcels should be valued as "woodland" and not "cropland harvested."


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the finding that petition taxpayer's land was entitled to farmland assessment and reversed the valuation of the land, remanding the matter for a hearing to determine the appropriate valuation. The court found that the tree farm was entitled to valuation as woodland, and not as cropland harvested, as contended by respondent township.

 

1365 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


In re B.


A-416-77


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


158 N.J. Super. 542; 386 A.2d 893; 1978 N.J. Super. LEXIS 821


March 13, 1978, Argued  
April 18, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Essex County Domestic Relations Court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient sought review of a final order of commitment of respondent county, entered by the Essex County Juvenile and Domestic Relations Court (New Jersey) pursuant to N.J. Ct. R. 4:74-7(f), involuntarily committing appellant to the county hospital on a finding that appellant was dangerous to herself and others as a result of mental illness. Appellant claimed that the evidence was insufficient to support an involuntary commitment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant patient was involuntarily committed to the county hospital after a hearing at which the only witness was a psychiatrist who testified that appellant was potentially dangerous to others because she suffered from mood swings that compromised her judgment and caused her to act impulsively. While appellant's appeal was pending, she was discharged from the hospital. Respondent county argued that the discharge mooted the appeal, and that the evidence was sufficient to support the involuntary commitment. The court reversed. Discharge of appellant did not moot her appeal because serious collateral legal consequences stemmed from the commitment order, in that respondent filed a lien against appellant's property to secure payment for the care and maintenance of appellant during her confinement for which appellant would not be liable if her confinement were improper. The psychiatrist's opinion that appellant was "potentially dangerous to others" was insufficient to establish the legally-required likelihood that, by reason of her mental illness, appellant would constitute a danger to others or herself if not confined.


OUTCOME: The order involuntarily committing appellant patient to respondent county's hospital was reversed. The appeal was not mooted by appellant's discharge from the hospital while the appeal was pending. Evidence that appellant was mentally ill, without additional evidence that the illness caused appellant to be a danger to herself or others, was insufficient to support an involuntary commitment order.

State v. Porro


A-498-77


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


158 N.J. Super. 269; 385 A.2d 1258; 1978 N.J. Super. LEXIS 790


February 16, 1978, Argued  
April 13, 1978, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal dismissed by State v. Porro, 77 N.J. 504, 391 A.2d 517, 1978 N.J. LEXIS 1053 (1978)
Writ of certiorari denied Porro v. New Jersey, 439 U.S. 1047, 99 S. Ct. 724, 58 L. Ed. 2d 706, 1978 U.S. LEXIS 4233 (1978)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Bergen County, whose opinion reported at 152 N.J. Super. 259 (1977).
State v. Porro, 152 N.J. Super. 259, 377 A.2d 950, 1977 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1054 (Law Div., 1977)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed the order of the Superior Court, Law Division, Bergen County (New Jersey), which denied defendants' motion challenging the grand jury which indicted defendants for conspiracy and misconduct in office.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were indicted for conspiracy and misconduct in office. The trial court denied defendants' motion that the systematic exclusion of full-time students and the under-representation of certain groups from the grand jury violated their rights to due process and equal protection and under N.J. Const. art. I, § 8 (1947). The court affirmed, holding that full-time students were not a "cognizable group" the exclusion of which would rob a grand jury of its cross-sectional quality. The court found that the exclusion of students did not target a large portion of the population, was rationally warranted to protect students from the hardships of jury duty, and was not an invidious discrimination based on race, color, creed, national origin, ancestry, matrimonial status or sex. The court further found that the failure to update voter registration lists as required by N.J. Stat. Ann. § 19:31-15 that were used to select grand jurors had no relationship to the under-representation of women, blacks, laborers and blue-collar workers and that any such disparity did not result from intentional discrimination, but rather from the use of voter registration lists and individualized excuses.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of defendants' motions challenging the grand jury which indicted them for conspiracy and misconduct in office, holding that because full-time students were not a constitutionally cognizable group, their systematic exclusion was not improper, and that any under-representation of blacks, women, and blue collar workers resulted from the use of voter registration lists, not intentional discrimination.

State v. De Marco


A-4811-76


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


157 N.J. Super. 341; 384 A.2d 1113; 1978 N.J. Super. LEXIS 765


March 7, 1978, Submitted  
March 29, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Superior Court, Law Division, Hudson County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants challenged a decision of the Superior Court (New Jersey), which ordered suppression of evidence of two vehicles and held that the Motor Vehicle Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:10-6, did not give license to the police to enter upon defendants' business property to commence a search. The state contended that the trial court erred in deciding that the two Chevrolet Blazers were motor vehicles and § 39:10-6 did not apply to private property.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were indicted for bringing stolen property into New Jersey, receiving a stolen vehicle, and possession of motor vehicles with altered serial numbers, after they failed to produce ownership papers for the vehicles and the inspectors seized and impounded the vehicles. Defendants moved to suppress the evidence seized in a warrantless search. The trial judge ordered suppression of the evidence and held that the Motor Vehicle Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:10-6, did not give license to the police to enter upon defendants' business property to commence a search. The state contended that the trial court erred in deciding that the two Chevrolet Blazers were motor vehicles and argued that § 39:10-6 did not apply to private property. On appeal, the court affirmed the order suppressing the evidence relating to the inoperable Blazer, but reversed the order relating to the operable Blazer. The court stated that defendants were unable to produce proof of ownership and seizure of the operable vehicle was proper. The court stated that the inoperable Blazer was an inoperable shell of a car, did not constitute a motor vehicle under the statute, and was thus improperly seized.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order suppressing the evidence relating to the inoperable Blazer but reversed the order relating to the operable Blazer. The court stated that it was correctly held that the inoperable Blazer which was an inoperable shell of a car, did not constitute a motor vehicle under the statute and therefore ,the police improperly seized it. The court stated that other Blazer, in the process of being operable, was properly seized.

Niglio v. New Jersey Racing Com.


A-4844-75


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


158 N.J. Super. 182; 385 A.2d 925; 1978 N.J. Super. LEXIS 799


November 7, 1977, Argued  
March 29, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from New Jersey Department of Law and Public Safety, Division of New Jersey Racing Commission.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant licensee challenged a decision from the Department of Law and Public Safety, Division of New Jersey Racing Commission finding that appellant, the spouse of a disqualified person, was not permitted to obtain a license to race horses. Appellant contended that such denial was a violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 37:2-1, which guaranteed certain rights to married persons.


OVERVIEW: Appellant licensee's license to race a horse she owned was suspended, following a hearing before a state steward, on the ground that a spouse of a disqualified person was likewise barred from participating in racing. It was not controverted that appellant's husband, with whom she was living and by whom she was employed, had been convicted of criminal offenses, and that her husband was disqualified from racing. Appellant claimed that the decision violated the rights provided her by N.J. Stat. Ann. § 37:2-1, guaranteeing certain rights to married persons. Substantially all of the testimony before the hearing officer conducting the hearing related to appellant's dependence on her husband. It was also apparent to the hearing officer that appellant had an inability to operate independently. The judgment was affirmed because a plain reading of the statute prohibited appellant from acquiring a license.


OUTCOME: The judgment that suspended the horse racing license of appellant licensee was affirmed because a plain reading of the statute at issue mandated that appellant, as a spouse of a disqualified racing participant, was prohibited from holding a horse racing license. The court found that there was no violation of her rights as a married individual.

Teaneck v. Firemen's Mut. Benevolent Asso.

PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Bergen County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff township sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Bergen County that issued a conditional injunction against defendants, firefighters and union, preventing the defendants from striking, but granted defendants the ability to apply to vacate if plaintiff did not comply with certain conditions.


OVERVIEW: After a labor dispute occurred between plaintiff township and defendants, firefighters and union, 15 firefighters of 18 scheduled to report for duty failed to report. Plaintiff sought an injunction. The trial court granted an injunction prohibiting any strikes by defendants, together with certain conditions. The injunction conditions stipulated that the parties had to meet with a fact finder and had to enter negotiations as provided by the conditions. The injunction also stipulated that if plaintiff failed to comply with the conditions, defendants could apply to vacate the injunction. Plaintiff sought review. The court affirmed the injunction itself, but reversed the conditions holding that it was incumbent upon the trial court to prohibit, unqualifiedly, the illegal strike, thus it could not be conditioned. However, the trial court had equitable jurisdiction to fashion a complete remedy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the injunction itself, but reversed the conditions attendant to the injunction. The court held that the trial court had equitable jurisdiction to fashion a complete remedy. However, it was incumbent upon the trial court to prohibit, unqualifiedly, the illegal strike, thus the injunction could not be conditioned.

State v. Celmer


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


157 N.J. Super. 242; 384 A.2d 894; 1978 N.J. Super. LEXIS 889


November 22, 1977, Argued  
March 10, 1978, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certification granted by State v. Celmer, 79 N.J. 464, 401 A.2d 221, 1978 N.J. LEXIS 1122 (1978)
Reversed by State v. Celmer, 80 N.J. 405, 404 A.2d 1, 1979 N.J. LEXIS 1240 (1979)


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Celmer, 143 N.J. Super. 371, 362 A.2d 1330, 1976 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1144 (N.J. Super. Ct., 1976)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state appealed from a decision of the Monmouth County, (New Jersey) Court that sustained the defendant's conviction for driving under the influence, but reversed his convictions for speeding and disregard of a traffic signal. Defendant was convicted in the lower municipal court of driving under the influence of alcohol, speeding, and disregarding a traffic signal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted in the municipal court of driving under the influence of alcohol (DUI), speeding, and disregarding a traffic signal. Defendant appealed. A trial de novo was held in the trial court. The trial court sustained the defendant's DUI conviction, but reversed his convictions for speeding and disregard of a traffic signal. Defendant had argued, for the first time on appeal, that the municipal court lacked jurisdiction because N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40:97-1, which established the municipal court, was unconstitutional. Plaintiff state appealed. The issue on appeal was whether the municipal court had jurisdiction to decide defendants' case de novo on the theory of de facto jurisdiction where no objection to the municipal court's authority was raised in the municipal court. The court noted that the municipal court was an inferior court that developed from laws pertaining to police courts and camp meeting associations. The court concluded that the municipal court was validly established, thus had jurisdiction to enforce state statutes prescribing motor vehicle operation. The trial court judgment of acquittal in the DUI was reversed. The case was remanded for resentencing.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court judgment of acquittal of the defendant for speeding and disregard of a traffic signal. The case was remanded for resentencing. The court found that the municipal court had been created in accordance with the custom and laws when it came into being, thus as a municipal court it had authority to hear cases that dealt with enforcement of motor vehicle operation statutes.

State v. Roberson


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


156 N.J. Super. 551; 384 A.2d 195; 1978 N.J. Super. LEXIS 838


February 16, 1978, Argued  
March 8, 1978, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of New Jersey that denied defendant's motion to suppress evidence and convicted defendant for possession of stolen items.


OVERVIEW: Police, who previously arrested defendant for driving without insurance one month prior, stopped defendant who was operating a motor vehicle. A six-month license suspension was statutorily mandated for a first violation. Defendant produced a driver's license and registration, but did not produce an insurance identification card. Defendant was arrested and an inventory search of the vehicle uncovered stolen tires and an attache case. Defendant's motion to suppress was denied, and he was convicted of possession of stolen items. Defendant sought review contending the arrest was improper and the search was excessive in scope. The court affirmed the conviction holding that the police properly arrested defendant. The police were not circumscribed by express statutory authority to impound and search motor vehicles.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's possession of stolen items conviction. The court held that the police were not circumscribed by express statutory authority to impound and search motor vehicles. The police properly arrested defendant for driving with a suspended license.

 

1372 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Bonnet v. State


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


155 N.J. Super. 520; 382 A.2d 1175; 1978 N.J. Super. LEXIS 682


October 24, 1977, Argued  
January 24, 1978, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Bonnet v. State, 78 N.J. 325, 395 A.2d 194, 1978 N.J. LEXIS 446 (1978)


PRIOR HISTORY: Bonnet v. State, 141 N.J. Super. 177, 357 A.2d 772, 1976 N.J. Super. LEXIS 856 (N.J. Super. Ct., 1976)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a class action, plaintiffs, taxpayers, black residents, low-income families of Essex County, and the City of Newark, challenged the judgment of a trial court (New Jersey) which dismissed their complaint. In this action plaintiffs alleged that the New Jersey system of financing welfare and judiciary-administration functions through state-mandated costs imposed upon the counties, to be met through local realty taxes was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, taxpayers, black residents, low-income families of Essex County, and the City of Newark, brought a class action suit alleging that the state system of financing welfare and judiciary-administration functions through state-mandated costs imposed upon the counties, to be met through local realty taxes resulted in a denial of equal protection, violated the principle of uniformity of taxation, and negated an "implicit premise of local government." The trial court dismissed plaintiffs' complaint and stated that the system of state-mandated costs at issue was not unconstitutional. Plaintiffs challenged the trial court' s judgment. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment and held that there were no equal protection violations because there was a rational basis for counties to bear a share of the costs in question. Likewise, the court held that uniformity of taxation was faithfully followed, as the fiscal responsibilities of these costs had been uniformly levied upon all taxable property. Also, the counties' rights to self-government and to be free of any unwarranted distribution of the state's fiscal responsibility were not violated by these statutory cost schemes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment and held that the system of state-mandated costs for financing welfare and judiciary administration functions was not unconstitutional. The court stated that issues raised by plaintiffs, taxpayers, black residents, low-income families of Essex County, and the City of Newark, were public policy issues that were to be resolved by the legislature and not by the courts.

Cain v. New Jersey State Parole Board


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


155 N.J. Super. 245; 382 A.2d 683; 1978 N.J. Super. LEXIS 657


December 6, 1977, Argued  
January 9, 1978, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant inmates sought review of administrative determinations of respondent, the State Parole Board (New Jersey), which found that defendants were not entitled to parole.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were inmates of county facilities who had been sentenced to two or more consecutive terms, each less than one year, but in the aggregate greater than one year. Each applied to respondent New Jersey State Parole Board for parole, after having served at least one year of their aggregate terms. Respondent denied parole, finding that each was ineligible under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 30:4-123.35. Defendants appealed, and the court affirmed. The statute provided that no county prisoner was to be eligible for parole until incarcerated for at least one year; that eligibility was further limited to inmates whose sentences might have been served in state prison; and that parole was not intended to be available to county inmates serving disorderly person sentences of six months. It held that county inmates sentenced to consecutive sentences, where each sentence had a term of at least one year, were eligible for parole upon completion of the aggregated minimum sentence, or one-third of the aggregated maximum term; that parole eligibility would not arise until after at least one full year; and that different treatment of county and state prison inmates was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed administrative rulings of respondent, the State Parole Board, finding that defendants were not eligible for parole, because as county inmates, they were eligible only if they had been sentenced to consecutive sentences, with each having a term of at least one year, and had completed the aggregated minimum sentence, or one-third of the aggregated maximum.

 

1374 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Blecker


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


155 N.J. Super. 93; 382 A.2d 400; 1978 N.J. Super. LEXIS 653; 93 A.L.R.3d 288


September 20, 1977, Argued  
January 4, 1978, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed orders of the trial court (New Jersey), which convicted them of knowingly selling obscene material to a person under the age of 18 years, in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:115-1.8.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were convicted of knowingly selling obscene material to a person under the age of 18, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:115-1.8. Defendants appealed, arguing the trial court erroneously failed to instruct the jury that the prosecution had to prove that defendants knew or should have known the age of the minor. The court found that the prosecution was not required to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that defendants knew or should have known from his appearance that the buyer of the obscene material was under 18 years of age. The trial court did not err in refusing to submit defendants' instruction to the jury because the instruction would have permitted the jury to acquit based on a finding that the prosecution failed to affirmatively prove that defendants knew the minor's age. Because the requested charge in part misstated the law, the trial judge properly rejected it in its entirety. Regardless, any error in refusing the charge was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt because the fact that the minor appeared to be over 18 years old was not alone a defense to the crime. Further, there was no claim that defendants did not know the minor's age. Defendants' convictions were thus affirmed.


OUTCOME: The orders convicting defendants of knowingly selling obscene material to a person under the age of 18 were affirmed because the trial court did not err in refusing to give a jury instruction that improperly allowed the jury to acquit defendants based on a finding that the prosecution failed to prove that defendants knew the buyer's age. Regardless, any error in not giving the charge was harmless.

Bastas v. Board of Review


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


155 N.J. Super. 312; 382 A.2d 923; 1978 N.J. Super. LEXIS 664


September 19, 1977, Submitted  
January 4, 1978, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant alien challenged the denial of unemployment compensation by respondent Board of Review for the Department of Labor and Industry (New Jersey), which was based upon appellant's status as an alien not authorized to be employed gainfully in the United States.


OVERVIEW: Appellant alien worked for respondent company almost three years until she was laid off for lack of work. Because she did not provide an alien registration card or any proof that she could lawfully work in the United States, it was determined that she was unavailable for work within the meaning of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 43:21-4(c) and, therefore, ineligible for benefits. At a hearing before the Appeal Tribunal of respondent Board of Review for the state's Department of Labor and Industry, upon advice of counsel appellant refused to answer questions about her country origin, her citizenship, and her right to work in the United States, on the assertion that the questions were irrelevant to her availability for work and unconstitutional. On appeal, the court affirmed the denial of unemployment benefits, because appellant failed to demonstrate that she was available for work. The court held that in a civil proceeding appellant's failure to testify about her status permitted the inference that she could not successfully support her right to work. The burden was on appellant to establish a right to unemployment compensation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of unemployment benefits to appellant by respondent Board of Review, because appellant's failure to testify about her alien status permitted the inference that she could not successfully support her right to work.

New Jersey State Chamber of Commerce v. New Jersey Election Law Enforcement Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


155 N.J. Super. 218; 382 A.2d 670; 1977 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1229


October 3, 1977, Argued  
December 20, 1977, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, state election commission and others, sought relief from a judgment of the trial court (New Jersey), invalidating the statutory regulation of political information organizations under the New Jersey Campaign Contributions and Expenditures Reporting Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 91:44A-1 et seq., on the ground that it had a chilling effect in respect to U.S. Const. amend. I freedoms.


OVERVIEW: The trial court ruled in favor of respondent lobbyist organizations' challenge to the constitutionality of the New Jersey Campaign Contributions and Expenditures Reporting Act (act), N.J. Stat. Ann. § 19:44A-1 et seq., on the ground that the imposition of reporting obligations on political information organizations would discourage single issue groups from exercising their freedom of expression under U.S. Const. amend. I. On appeal, the court held that where legislation generally served a proper public purpose, facial invalidation of the entire legislation should be avoided where feasible and the legislation judicially construed to narrow or expand its effect to erase the unconstitutional aspect. Accepting the trial court's finding as to the chilling effect upon groups who collected or spent small sums of money to influence legislation, the court adopted a threshold annual limitation of $ 750 for reporting requirements. The court justified its action as an effort to modify the statute in order to save it from unconstitutionality by implementing a threshold proposed in a pending amendment to the act.


OUTCOME: The judgment invalidating the statutory regulation of political organizations under the New Jersey Campaign Contributions and Expenditures Reporting Act on the ground of overbreadth of the statute in respect to First Amendment freedoms was reversed. The court held that it was improper for the trial court to hold the statute facially invalid without first attempting to save the constitutionality of the statute by appropriate construction.

State v. Budco Quality Theaters, Inc.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Camden County Court of New Jersey, Law Division (Criminal)


155 N.J. Super. 50; 382 A.2d 102; 1977 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1361; 3 Media L. Rep. 2028



December 9, 1977 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, outdoor movie theater, sought review of a decision of the Municipal Court (New Jersey) that convicted defendant of exhibiting a film depicting acts of sado-masochistic abuse on an outdoor screen visible from beyond the theater audience area, in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:170-25.18.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, an outdoor movie theater, displayed a film that displayed acts of sadomasochistic abuse. The movie screen was 40' by 80' in size. Defendant was charged with exhibiting a film depicting acts of sadomasochistic abuse on an outdoor screen visible from beyond the theater audience area in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:170-25.18. A police officer testified that the screen could be readily seen from various other locations including the parking lot of a nearby motor inn, a state highway, and a field outside of the theater. The municipal court convicted defendant. Defendant sought review contending that its First Amendment rights were violated. The court affirmed the conviction holding that the statute was narrowly constructed. A state could adopt more stringent controls on communicative materials available to youths than on those available to adults.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction holding that more stringent controls on communicative materials available to youths could be adopted by a state, than on those available to adults. The statute, prohibiting the presentation of sado-masochistic scenes by an outdoor theater, was narrowly constructed.

Trenton v. Mercer County Board of Taxation


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


155 N.J. Super. 181; 382 A.2d 651; 1977 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1225


October 17, 1977, Submitted  
December 2, 1977, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city challenged a judgment from the Division of Tax Appeals (New Jersey), which affirmed respondent Mercer County Board of Taxation's promulgation of a tax table under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 54:3-17 that excluded the receipts of the Public Utility Gross Receipts Tax from county tax apportionment.


OVERVIEW: Respondent Mercer County Board of Taxation prepared a tax equalization table pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 54:3-17 under which it excluded the receipts of the Public Utility Gross Receipts Tax (PUGRT) from county tax apportionment. Appellant city challenged the table, arguing that the exclusion of municipal revenue realized through the PUGRT under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 54:30A-61 violated equal protection and the ban on special legislation respecting taxation or the regulation of municipal affairs. The Division of Tax Appeals affirmed respondent's promulgation of the table, and the court affirmed, finding that there was no constitutional requirement that all municipal revenue sources be treated in precisely the same manner in county tax apportionment. Nor did the court find it necessary that a particular tax revenue be included in the equalization process. The court found that appellant did not meet its heavy burden to establish the absence of a relevant distinction and legitimate legislative aims. The court found that here there was no classification among municipalities, only among revenue sources. Such classification, the court found, had a rational basis and was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order from the Division of Tax Appeals, which found that respondent Mercer County Board of Taxation's tax table, excluding the receipts of the Public Utility Gross Receipts Tax from county apportionment, was proper. The court found that such exclusion did not violate equal protection or the ban on special legislation respecting taxation or the regulation of appellant city's affairs.

 

1379 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Yellow Duck Nursery, Inc. v. Department of Institutions & Agencies


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


155 N.J. Super. 56; 382 A.2d 381; 1977 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1220


September 20, 1977, Argued  
November 23, 1977, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, private day care centers, sought administrative review of a determination by respondent, the Department of Institutions and Agencies of the State of New Jersey, which ordered appellants to comply with N.J. Admin. Code tit. 10, § 122-2.7(d)(1), which required a second adult to be provided in addition to the driver when more than six children were transported in one vehicle.


OVERVIEW: Respondent, Department of Institutions and Agencies, adopted an administrative rule that required day care centers to provide for a second adult in any vehicle transporting more than six children. N.J. Admin. Code. tit. 10, § 122-2.7(d)(1). Appellants were private day care centers, as defined in N.J. Stat. Ann. 18A:70-1. Appellants were ordered to comply with the rule after respondent found that it was a reasonable regulation adopted pursuant to a rational statute. Appellants claimed on appeal that enforcement of the rule violated their rights to equal protection because the rule did not apply to public, quasi-public, and charitable child care centers. The court rejected appellants' claims and affirmed respondent's order. The court ruled that the second adult regulation was an integral portion of safety and health of all children, and that every day care center that was under respondent's supervision, by reason of other laws or regulations, was required to abide with the same standard. Accordingly, the court found that enforcement of the rule did not violate appellants' rights to equal protection and affirmed respondent's order.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed an order by respondent, the Division of Youth and Family Services, that required appellants, private day care centers, to comply with its rule that required a second adult in vehicles that transported more than six children. The rule did not violate appellants' equal protection rights because all facilities under respondent's jurisdiction had to provide the same protection.

 

1380 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


North Jersey Suburbanite Co. v. State


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


154 N.J. Super. 126; 381 A.2d 34; 1977 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1153


September 26, 1977, Argued  
October 31, 1977, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certification denied by North Jersey Suburbanite Co. v. State, 75 N.J. 601, 384 A.2d 831, 1978 N.J. LEXIS 747 (1978)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff periodical publisher challenged the decision of the trial court (New Jersey), which found in favor of defendant state in plaintiff's declaratory action, and which found that N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 35:1-2.1 and 2.2 was not unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff periodical publisher distributed a weekly tabloid free of charge. Defendant state refused to publish statutorily mandated public notices in plaintiff's newspaper. Plaintiff then filed a declaratory action, seeking declaration of N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 35:1-2.1 and 2.2. The trial court found in favor of defendant. On appeal, the court found that the statute required that a newspaper have a general paid circulation, and measurable news content. Further, the court found that it was the legislature's intention that published official notices come to the attention of as wide and diverse a readership as possible. Application of the reasonable relation test established the nexus between the challenged criteria and the advancement of a valid legislative purpose. Thus, the classification that plaintiff challenged was not shown to be arbitrary, capricious or unrelated to the specific objective of the legislation. Therefore, the trial court's judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Trial court's decision that found in favor of defendant state in plaintiff periodical publisher's declaratory action was affirmed. The statute that plaintiff challenged was constitution because there was a reasonable relation between the challenged criteria and the advancement of a valid legislative purpose.

Palagonia v. Newark

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the decision of the trial court (New Jersey) that found that the gender-based classification system utilized in its retirement plan was unconstitutional because it discriminated against female participants.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review when the gender-based classification system it utilized in its retirement plan was found to be unconstitutionally discriminatory because it treated female participants differently than male participants. The court affirmed the judgment. It concluded that even if the lower court was incorrect in applying the strict scrutiny test to invalidate this particular gender-based classification, the classification would similarly be unconstitutional if a less rigorous standard was used.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, concluding that appellant's classification system was unconstitutionally discriminatory regardless of whether a strict scrutiny test or a less rigorous standard was utilized.

Adoption of B. v. B.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Union County Court of New Jersey, Probate Division


152 N.J. Super. 546; 378 A.2d 90; 1977 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1355



July 26, 1977 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff grandparents petitioned to adopt their deceased daughter's son, who was born out of wedlock and who had lived in the grandmother's home since birth. Defendant natural father cross-petitioned for custody of his child.


OVERVIEW: The grandparents' petition for adoption and the father's cross-petition for custody of the child were consolidated. The mother of the child had lived with the child in the grandmother's home for about two years after the child's birth. The mother then moved to New York and lived there until her death, but the mother left the child with the grandmother out of concern for the child's welfare. The father of the child admitted to paternity of the child six months after the child's birth and was ordered to pay child support. The father visited the child at the grandmother's home, but his visits became less frequent after the mother left the home. The court held that the father could not be denied custody by virtue of his status as an unwed father under N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 9: 2 -13 or 9: 3-18. Further, the court denied the grandparents' petition for adoption in the absence of consent by the father, because he had not forsaken his parental obligations under N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 9: 3-18(d) or 9: 3-24. However, the court granted custody to the grandparents with liberal visitation rights to the father, because it would be psychologically detrimental to remove him from his home since birth.


OUTCOME: The court denied the father's cross-petition for custody and ordered that custody remain with the grandparents of the child. The court gave the father liberal visitation rights.

 

1383 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Fiore v. Hudson County Employees Pension Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


151 N.J. Super. 524; 377 A.2d 702; 1977 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1029


June 14, 1977, Argued  
July 13, 1977, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff challenged an order of a trial court (New Jersey), which denied his motion for an order to declare that a suit that he filed on the behalf of pensioners whose checks were subject to defendant pension commission's allegedly illegal deductions could be litigated as a class action.


OVERVIEW: The trial court denied plaintiff pensioner's motion for an order to declare that a suit that he filed on the behalf of pensioners, whose checks were subject to allegedly illegal deductions by defendant pension commission, was maintainable as a class action. The trial court also granted defendant's summary judgment motion and dismissed the complaint. The court reversed the denial of plaintiff's motion for certification of the action as a class on appeal, and directed the trial court to hold a hearing as to whether the action qualified for that treatment. The court found that the fact that plaintiff was the only pensioner who filed a claim regarding the deductions at issue did not preclude the certification, and that the determining factor was whether his claim was typical of those of the individuals that he sought to represent. The court also determined that any individual who did not wish to be represented in the litigation could always have opted out of the class. The court further held that plaintiff's case relied on interpreting the pension statute, which was a question of law that was common to all members of the class.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's denial of plaintiff pensioner's motion to certify his suit against defendant pension commission as to allegedly illegal pension check deductions as a class action, and ordered a hearing on that issue. The court held that the crucial factor was if plaintiff's claim was typical of those of the asserted class, and that his case relied on interpreting the pension statute, which was a common question of law.
