Common Cause v. New Jersey Election Law Enforcement Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


151 N.J. Super. 265; 376 A.2d 1237; 1977 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1003


June 28, 1977, Argued  
July 1, 1977, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certification granted Common Cause v. New Jersey Election Law Enforcement Com., 75 N.J. 23, 379 A.2d 253, 1977 N.J. LEXIS 896 (1977)
Affirmed by Common Cause v. New Jersey Election Law Enforcement Com., 74 N.J. 231, 377 A.2d 643, 1977 N.J. LEXIS 157 (1977)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant organization sought review of the validity of N.J. Admin. Code § 19:25-15.36, which had been adopted by respondent commission, purportedly under the authority of the New Jersey Campaign Contributions and Expenditures Reporting Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 19:44A-1 et seq., with respect to contributions to the winner of the primary election for the office of governor for the purpose of paying off primary election expenses.


OVERVIEW: Appellant organization challenged the validity of N.J. Admin. Code § 19:25-15.36, which had been adopted by respondent commission, purportedly under the authority of the New Jersey Campaign Contributions and Expenditures Reporting Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 19:44A-1 et seq. The court held that § 19:25-15.36 contravened the policy and express provisions of § 19:44A-1 et seq., and were illegal and void. The court held that the language of the statute was clear. The court held that contributions in excess of $ 600 could not be made on behalf of the winner of the gubernatorial primary for any purpose after the date of the primary election. The court held that the purpose of the statute was to provide that general election campaigns for the office of governor would be financed with public support, so that the candidates would be free from the improper influence that large individual contributions would tend to exert. N.J. Stat. Ann. § 19:44A-27. The court held that the distinction between winners and losers rested upon a real and substantial relation to the basic object of the legislation.


OUTCOME: The court held that a regulation adopted by respondent commission directly contravened the provisions of a statute. The court held that the language of the statute was clear and that the regulation was illegal and void.

K.S.B. Technical Sales Corp. v. North Jersey Dist. Water Supply Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


151 N.J. Super. 218; 376 A.2d 960; 1977 N.J. Super. LEXIS 998


June 1, 1977, Argued  
June 30, 1977, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, which declared that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 52:33-2 was unconstitutional, but held that the bids submitted in accordance with such specifications were binding and ordered that they be received and opened by defendant.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, manufacturer and taxpayer, filed suit against defendant commission and sought a declaration that three New Jersey Buy American statutes, N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 40A:11-18, 52:32-1, 52:33-2 were unconstitutional and against public policy, and an order that would strike the Buy American requirement from an addendum to the specifications for a filtration plant. The trial court held that the statutes did not conflict with U.S. Const. art. 1, § 8, cl. 3 and were not facially unconstitutional, however, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 52:33-2, as incorporated in the addendum, conflicted with the General Agreement on Tariffs and Trade and the Supremacy Clause and was unconstitutional. Plaintiffs contended on appeal that the trial court erred in not holding that the statutes were unconstitutional on their face. The court affirmed because the bids that were submitted in compliance with the addendum were unlawful, void, and of no effect. However, the court reversed the portions of the judgment that declared the bids submitted in compliance with the Buy American addendum to be binding and ordered the commission to receive and open them.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court because the Buy American statutes were not facially unconstitutional, but they were unconstitutional as incorporated in the addendum. The court reversed the portions of the judgment that declared the bids submitted in compliance with the addendum to be binding and ordered defendant commission to receive and open them was reversed.

OVERVIEW: Appellant conservation organization sought tax exempt status for land within respondent borough under the Green Acres Tax Exemption Program, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 54:4-3.63 et seq. The Department of Environmental Protection exempted part of the land, and found that appellant could not prove title to the remainder. Both parties sought review. The court rejected respondent's claims that the exemption program was an unconstitutional delegation of authority without guidelines. 1387 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Dome Realty, Inc. v. Paterson


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


150 N.J. Super. 448; 375 A.2d 1240; 1977 N.J. Super. LEXIS 950


May 23, 1977, Submitted  
June 8, 1977, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landlords filed a complaint that attacked the constitutionality of a city ordinance that established a condition precedent to the right of a landlord to recover from tenants the amount of an increase in real estate taxes through a tax surcharge. Defendant city appealed the decision of the trial court (New Jersey), and contended that plaintiffs lacked standing because there had been no tax increase and plaintiffs had not been injured.


OVERVIEW: Defendant city enacted a rent control ordinance that permitted landlords to pass on to tenants the amount of any annual tax increase unless the landlord was in arrears on his taxes. Plaintiff landlords filed a complaint that attacked the ordinance as unconstitutional. Defendant contended that plaintiffs lacked standing because there had been no tax increase, and plaintiffs had not been injured. The court held that plaintiffs had standing because the contested legislation could significantly affect plaintiffs, as property owners, and others similarly situated. The court held that plaintiffs had no duty to exhaust their administrative remedies because the attack was purely legal, and the local board had no power or jurisdiction to entertain the issue. The court held that the condition imposed was intended to create a tax collection device for defendant's benefit, and that it had no rational nexus with defendant's legislative authority to enact a rent control ordinance. The court held that the imposition of such a condition or penalty was oppressive, arbitrary, and unreasonable. The court held that the ordinance invaded a field of legislation, taxation, preempted by state statutes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court, and held that a city ordinance, which established a condition precedent to the right of a landlord to recover from tenants the amount of an increase in real estate taxes through a tax surcharge, was unconstitutional. The court held that the ordinance had no rational nexus with defendant's legislative authority to enact a rent control ordinance.

Mt. Laurel Township v. Barbieri


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


151 N.J. Super. 27; 376 A.2d 541; 1977 N.J. Super. LEXIS 976


February 14, 1977, Argued  
June 7, 1977, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff township appealed a decision of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, which denied its motion to vacate a consent judgment that physically partitioned defendant property owners' land. Plaintiff also appealed the dismissal of its independent action that sought to set aside the trial court's partition judgment, restrain defendants from selling their property, and require them to apply for subdivision approval.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff township filed an action against defendant property owners that sought to set aside a partition judgment as fraudulently procured. The trial court dismissed the action. Plaintiff then filed a motion to vacate the partition judgment. The trial court denied the motion. Plaintiff appealed both decisions. The court reversed and remanded the motion to vacate and dismissed the other appeal as moot. The court found that it was clear that the partition proceeding was designed and pursued by defendants solely to circumvent the subdivision statute and the allegedly onerous conditions imposed upon the proposed subdivision of defendants' property by plaintiff's resolution. The court found that the partition judgment was entered without plaintiff having the benefit of a hearing, and that the judgment was unsupported by any evidence that would justify the partition. The court found that the final order, which was drafted with the consent of defendants, divided the property in exactly the manner sought in the subdivision application. The court held that the consent partition judgment did not fall within the exemption for court-ordered subdivisions in N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40:55-1.2.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's dismissal of plaintiff township's motion to vacate defendant property owners' consent partition judgment. The court dismissed as moot plaintiff's independent action to vacate the judgment. The court remanded the case for the trial court to resolve defendants' counterclaims. The court held that the partition decree effectuated to avoid government subdivision controls was not an exempt court-ordered subdivision.

 

1389 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Feintuch


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


150 N.J. Super. 414; 375 A.2d 1223; 1977 N.J. Super. LEXIS 945


May 17, 1977, Argued  
June 6, 1977, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, Union County, which affirmed the decision of the municipal court in a trial de novo and found defendant guilty of leaving the scene of an accident with complainant despite defendant's claim that he had no knowledge of the accident.


OVERVIEW: Defendant driver was found guilty in municipal court of leaving the scene of an accident with complainant. A motion for judgment of acquittal was denied. After a trial de novo defendant was found guilty by the county court. On appeal the court held that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:4-129(b) should have been construed to require proof of knowledge of involvement in an accident in a prosecution for leaving the scene. The absence of the word "knowingly" from the law was not construed as intent to create a strict liability offense. The state produced evidence of an accident and defendant's failure to stop. Defendant denied knowledge of any impact. The trial judge assessed the probative force of the inference of defendant's knowledge of the accident that arose once the state proved that an impact occurred. The trial judge held that the probative weight of the inference of knowledge that arose from proof of impact outweighed the probative force of defendant's denial of knowledge and found defendant guilty. The court affirmed as there was sufficient evidence to support the trial judge's finding beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant left the scene of an accident contrary to the statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed and held there was sufficient evidence to support the trial judge's finding that defendant left the scene of the accident in violation of the statute despite defendant's claim of a lack of knowledge of the accident. The trial judge was within his authority when he believed the inference of knowledge due to the impact over the defendant's denial of knowledge.

State v. Trotwood


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


150 N.J. Super. 115; 374 A.2d 1256; 1977 N.J. Super. LEXIS 917


May 10, 1977, Submitted  
May 24, 1977, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his convictions of two separate violations for hitchhiking, in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. 39:4-59, by the West Windsor Township Municipal Court (New Jersey), and asserted that the statute was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of two violations of hitchhiking in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. 39:4-59, which he challenged on the grounds that the statute was unconstitutional. Defendant asserted that his equal protection rights were violated by the application of the statute. The court affirmed the convictions because defendant failed to show that he was a member of a suspect class therefore the standard that the trial court applied to decide on the issue of constitutionality was appropriate. The rational relationship test was properly used to determine the issue of constitutionality of the statute. The compelling state interest test was applicable in situations where there was a showing that there was a suspect classification. Common experience did not support the conclusion that only poor people hitchhike.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions of hitchhiking because the trial court properly applied the rational relationship test to determine that the statute that prohibited hitchhiking on the highway was constitutional.

Ammond v. Keating


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


150 N.J. Super. 5; 374 A.2d 498; 1977 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1265


May 13, 1977, Argued  
May 18, 1977, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of New Jersey entered a judgment invalidating those portions of N.J. Const. art IV, § I, para. 2, and its statutory implementing provision, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 52:10B-6, which imposed a one-year residency requirement in the senatorial district from which a state senator sought election as a condition to membership in the state senate. Plaintiff incumbent challenged that judgment.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff incumbent challenged the right of defendant candidate to run for state senate where he had not met the New Jersey residency requirements of one year. The trial court found N.J. Const. art IV, § I, para. 2, and its statutory implementing provision, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 52:10B-6, that imposed a one-year residency requirement in the senatorial district from which a state senator sought election as a condition to membership in the state senate, to be unconstitutional. The court reversed and remanded, holding that the constitutional and statutory residency requirement for the office of state senator filled a compelling state need and was rationally related to legitimate state objectives. The court reasoned that other statutes that required a longer residency requirement had been found to be constitutional with the United States Supreme Court. The court concluded that art IV, § I, para. 2 was constitutional and defendant's name was to be stricken off the primary election ballot.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's ruling and ordered defendant candidate's name stricken off the primary election ballot, holding that because defendant did not meet the one year residency requirement, he could not be a candidate for state senate.

Rybeck v. Rybeck


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


150 N.J. Super. 151; 375 A.2d 269; 1977 N.J. Super. LEXIS 921


April 25, 1977, Argued  
May 11, 1977, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed an order of the trial court (New Jersey) denying their motion for summary judgment in an action in which they sought a declaration that defendant violated its insurance contract by ceasing to make continuation payments under the New Jersey Automobile Reparation Reform Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:6A-1 et seq., and a declaration that the statute was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff wife filed a negligence action against her husband and defendant individual after an automobile accident. Plaintiff wife and her husband then filed a declaratory action against his insurer, seeking a declaration that defendant insurer violated its insurance contract and that the New Jersey Automobile Reparation Reform Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:6A-1 et seq., was unconstitutional. Plaintiffs' motion for summary judgment in the declaratory action based on the constitutionality of the statute was denied, and they appealed. The negligence action was subsequently settled. The court held that plaintiffs lost their standing to challenge the constitutionality of the statute when they settled the negligence action. Plaintiffs no longer had a stake in the outcome since they received their requested relief in the settlement, and any opinion on the constitutionality of the statute would have merely been advisory.


OUTCOME: Plaintiffs' appeal of the order denying their motion for summary judgment was dismissed because their settlement of a related negligence action negated their standing and any opinion on the constitutionality of the New Jersey Automobile Reparation Reform Act would have been merely advisory.

 

1393 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. De Piano


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


150 N.J. Super. 309; 375 A.2d 1169; 1977 N.J. Super. LEXIS 935


December 14, 1976, Argued  
May 10, 1977, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of the judgments of the trial court (New Jersey), that convicted them of possessing obscene materials with the intent to sell.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were convicted on charges of possessing obscene materials with intent to sell. Defendants appealed on several grounds, urging vacation of their convictions and sentences. The court affirmed the trial judgment. Defendants criticized the "judicial engraftment" of the Miller test on L. 1971, c. 449, that the grand jury was not presented with any evidence of the charge that one defendant violated N.J. Stat. Ann. 2A:115-2, and that the indictment should be dismissed for failing to set forth that they had scienter regarding the character and content of the obscene materials, among others. The court affirmed the convictions. The court held that defendants' criticism regarding the "judicial engraftment" of the Miller test was disregarded. The construction given the statute satisfied the Miller test's requirement that the prohibited hardcore sexual conduct be specifically defined by the applicable state law, as written. Supporting evidence in the form of testimony and actual magazines purchased unquestionably met the Miller test's requirements and were sufficient to support the charge. Lastly, implied knowledge was sufficient to satisfy the scienter element.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions, holding that implied knowledge was enough to satisfy the scienter requirement, the grand jury had more than enough evidence with which to issue the indictment in the form of testimony and three magazines that satisfied the Miller test, and defendants' criticism regarding judicial engraftment satisfied the Miller test's requirement that prohibited sexual conduct be specifically defined in the statute.

Skolski v. Woodcock


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


149 N.J. Super. 340; 373 A.2d 1008; 1977 N.J. Super. LEXIS 869


March 1, 1977, Submit

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prosecutor challenged the judgment of the Superior Court (New Jersey), which enjoined appellant and the county chief of detectives from terminating respondent county employee based on his failure to reside in the county as required by N.J. Stat. Ann. § 11:22-7.


OVERVIEW: Respondent county employee resided in the county when he was hired as an investigator, but during his employment, respondent established residency in another county. The chief of detectives told respondent that he would be dismissed if he did not move back to the county. The trial court enjoined appellant prosecutor and the chief from terminating respondent's employment. On appeal, the court found that respondent was appointed a county detective pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:157-2, which identified respondent as a member of the classified service. As a member of the classified service, respondent was subject to the residency requirement N.J. Stat. Ann. § 11:22-7. The court held that the § 11:22-7 required residency within the county not only as a condition for eligibility for appointment to the office of county detective but also as a condition for continued employment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded directing the trial court to enter an order terminating respondent county employee from his position as a county detective because of respondent's failure to meet the statutory residency requirement.

Associates Consumer Discount Co. v. Bozzarello


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


149 N.J. Super. 358; 373 A.2d 1016; 1977 N.J. Super. LEXIS 872


March 1, 1977, Submitted  
April 7, 1977, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff foreign corporation appealed a grant of summary judgment from the trial court (New Jersey) in favor of defendant companies, dismissing plaintiff's complaint for monies allegedly due on a credit agreement between the parties. Defendants motioned for the summary judgment arguing that plaintiff failed to comply with part of the Corporation Business Activities Reporting Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 14A:13-14 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Summary judgment for defendant companies dismissing plaintiff foreign corporation's complaint for monies allegedly due on a credit agreement between the parties was affirmed on the grounds that the court found no constitutional infirmity in requiring foreign corporations to give notice of their commercial activity in the state and in sanctioning those who failed to comply under the Corporation Business Activities Reporting Act (Act), N.J. Stat. Ann. § 14A:13-14 et seq. After plaintiff brought suit in New Jersey, defendants contended that plaintiff was barred from suit pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 14A:13-20, because it had not filed a notice of business activities report as required by N.J. Stat. Ann. § 14A:13-15 as part of the Act. Defendants argued that the tax was an unconstitutional burden upon interstate commerce. On appeal, the court found no constitutional violation for either the notice requirement or the noncompliance sanction of disallowing suit in New Jersey. The court concluded that the provisions were entirely reasonable means designed to achieve an essential state purpose-- the strengthening of the enforcement of its tax laws. The court affirmed the summary judgment.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment for defendant companies, dismissing plaintiff foreign corporation's complaint for monies allegedly due on a credit agreement between the parties, was affirmed on the grounds that the court found no constitutional infirmity in requiring foreign corporations to give notice of their commercial activity in the state and in sanctioning those who failed to comply under the Corporation Business Activities Reporting Act.

Pet Dealers Asso. v. Division of Consumer Affairs, Dep't of Law & Public Safety


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


149 N.J. Super. 235; 373 A.2d 688; 1977 N.J. Super. LEXIS 855; 22 U.C.C. Rep. Serv. (Callaghan) 16


October 19, 1976, Argued  
March 21, 1977, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff pet dealers appealed the validity of respondent division of consumer affairs' regulations governing the sale of pet cats and dogs adopted pursuant to the Consumer Fraud Act, N. J. Stat. Ann. § 56:8-4.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff pet dealers challenged the validity of regulations governing the sale of pet cats and dogs adopted pursuant to the Consumer Fraud Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 56:8-4. Plaintiff first contended that the regulations conflicted with Article 2 of the Uniform Commercial Code (UCC), N.J. Stat. Ann. § 12A:2-101 et seq., in that they provided consumers with broader remedies than those available under the UCC. The court found that remedies in the UCC were intended to give stability to the law of commercial transactions, but did not purport to limit the police power. The court found the regulations a proper exercise of police power. It also rejected plaintiffs' argument that the regulations created an invalid, unconstitutional classification. Because the majority of the complaints concerned pet dealers, that fact was sufficient support for the classification and provided a reasonable basis for the classification that was not purely arbitrary. Thus, no invidious discrimination existed in the regulations. Finally, the court found the regulations were not invidiously vague, and that they did not prohibit the sale of mixed breed animals.


OUTCOME: The court held that respondent division of consumer affairs' regulations challenged by plaintiff pet dealers were valid because there was no conflict between the Uniform Commercial Code and the Consumer Fraud Act, the classification had a reasonable basis and was not purely arbitrary, the regulations were not invidiously vague, and the regulations did not prohibit the sale of mixed breed animals.

 

1397 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Robinson


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


148 N.J. Super. 278; 372 A.2d 634; 1977 N.J. Super. LEXIS 787


March 1, 1977, Argued  
March 17, 1977, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought a review of an order of the Superior Court of New Jersey, which denied defendant's post conviction motion to modify defendant's sentence by a transfer to a drug treatment program pursuant to N.J. Ct. R. 3:21-10(b).


OVERVIEW: While incarcerated on a criminal offense, defendant filed a motion for transfer to a drug treatment program pursuant to N.J. Ct. R. 3:21-10(a), which the lower court considered as a request for the transfer under R. 3:21-10(b). However, the lower court denied defendant's motion because it was not timely filed under R. 3:21-10(a). On appeal, the court reversed and remanded the order of the lower court holding that defendant's motion was timely under R. 3:21-10(b). The court further held that a literal reading of R. 3:21-10(b) revealed that as long as the motion was supported by proper documentation, it could be filed at any time. Finally, the court held that, in exercising its discretion in the matter, the lower court must determine whether the purposes for defendant's continued custody outweighed the interests sought to be served by defendant's transfer to a drug treatment facility.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded an order of the lower court, which denied defendant's post conviction motion to modify defendant's sentence by a transfer to a drug treatment program. A literal reading of the statute, under which defendant's motion was considered, supported the timeliness of the motion.

 

1398 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Powers


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


148 N.J. Super. 415; 372 A.2d 1122; 1977 N.J. Super. LEXIS 804


February 22, 1977, Submitted  
March 14, 1977, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant trucking company sought review of the judgment of the Burlington County Court (New Jersey), which convicted defendant of carrying a load in excess of the weight permitted for that type of vehicle, pursuant to the provisions of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:3-84.


OVERVIEW: Defendant trucking company was charged on two separate occasions when a truck it owned was found to be carrying a load in excess of the weight permitted for that type of vehicle pursuant to the provisions of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:3-84. After a hearing in municipal court, defendant was found guilty as charged and fined for each offense. Defendant was again found guilty on a trial de novo on the record. The court affirmed the decision of the trial court. The court held that the statute specifying both the amount of allowable weight as well as the method by which compliance was determined was not unconstitutionally vague. Defendant's construction of the statute was unacceptable and productive of confusion of statutory language that the court found clear. If the distances referred to simply measured axle length, the legislature could have said so, without resorting to the device of the distance between two parallel transverse vertical planes to measure permissible axle weight.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court in convicting defendant trucking company of two counts of carrying a load in excess of the weight permitted for that type of vehicle. The court held that the statute specifying both the amount of allowable weight as well as the method by which compliance was determined was not unconstitutionally vague, and that the statutory language was clear.

 

1399 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Ballou v. State, Dep't of Civil Service


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


148 N.J. Super. 112; 372 A.2d 333; 1977 N.J. Super. LEXIS 770; 18 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 408


February 7, 1977, Argued  
March 7, 1977, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee sought review of the decision from respondent New Jersey Department of Civil Service, which dismissed her appeal challenging the appointment of a veteran under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 11:27-4 affording veterans an absolute preference to state positions.


OVERVIEW: Appellant employee filed a complaint with respondent New Jersey Department of Civil Service when a veteran was appointed over her to a position in which she had performed temporarily for three years and received the highest score in a competitive examination for the position. Respondent dismissed appellant's complaint, finding that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 11:27-4 mandated the appointment of veteran whenever he is among those certified. Appellant then sought review of respondent's decision, arguing that § 11:27-4 was unconstitutional in granting veteran's an absolute preference to state positions. The court held that § 11:27-4 was not inconsistent with N.J. Const. art. VII, § 1, para. 2 because that constitutional provision gave the basis for the state's veteran's preference laws. The court also held that the due process and equal protection clauses in U.S. Const. amend. XIV were not violated by § 11:27-4 because the statute was neither arbitrary, capricious, nor unreasonable and bore a rational relationship to the state's legitimate objective of providing a preference to veterans and because the award of benefits on the basis of veteran's status had not involved a suspect class.


OUTCOME: The decision of respondent New Jersey Department of Civil Service dismissing an appeal on the appointment of a veteran pursuant the state's veteran's preference statute was affirmed, because the statute was found to meet federal and state constitutional requirements where it was rationally related to a legitimate state objective of providing a preference to veterans and where the award of benefits to veterans had not involved a suspect class.

 

1400 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Curtis


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Superior Court of New Jersey, Appellate Division


148 N.J. Super. 235; 372 A.2d 612; 1977 N.J. Super. LEXIS 780


February 7, 1977, Argued  
February 25, 1977, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Morris County Court (New Jersey), which affirmed defendant's conviction for violating the disorderly persons offense of tampering with an electric meter, pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:170-64. Defendant claimed that that the presumptive evidence provision of § 2A:170-64 was unconstitutional and that his conviction should have been set aside.


OVERVIEW: After an electric company meter reader found that the outdoor meter on defendant's house was upside down so that the meter ran backwards, defendant was convicted of the disorderly persons offense of tampering with an electric meter, in violation of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:170-64. The conviction was affirmed in a de novo trial. Defendant appealed, claiming that a part of § 2A:170-64, which permitted the existence of certain conditions of the electric meter to constitute presumptive evidence of intent to defraud, was unconstitutional. The court affirmed and held that by applying the inference in § 2A:170-64 to the facts, it was able to conclude that it was more likely than not that defendant tampered with the meter with fraudulent intent. Such an inference was rational when tested by human conduct and experience, for the only person who was usually motivated to tamper with a meter was the one who would profit financially from such tampering. Accordingly, § 2A:170-64 met the constitutional challenge. Because there was sufficient evidence of tampering to support the application of the presumptive evidence rule, defendant was properly convicted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment that defendant was properly convicted of the disorderly persons offense of tampering with an electric meter. The court held that the condition of the electric meter met the statutory presumption of evidence of defendant's intent to defraud. Because the presumption was proper and constitutional, defendant's conviction was proper.
